SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2181
  SECTION: [Terminology](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    This memo does not use the oft used expressions MUST, SHOULD, MAY, or
    TEXT[!MUST]:    their negative forms.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2308
  SECTION: [- Negative Answers from Authoritative Servers](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Name servers authoritative for a zone MUST include the SOA record of
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the zone in the authority section of the response when reporting an
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NXDOMAIN or indicating that no data of the requested type exists.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the containing zone is signed [RFC2065] the SOA and appropriate
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NXT and SIG records MUST be added.

  SECTION: [- Caching Negative Answers](#section-5)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    This TTL decrements in a similar manner to a normal cached answer and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    upon reaching zero (0) indicates the cached negative answer MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be used again.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The NXT record, if it exists in the authority section of a negative
    TEXT[!MUST]:    answer received, MUST be stored such that it can be be located and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    returned with SOA record in the authority section, as should any SIG
    TEXT[!MUST]:    records in the authority section.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The NXT record MUST have the same owner name as the query
    TEXT[!MUST]:    name for NODATA responses.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Negative responses without SOA records SHOULD NOT be cached as there
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    is no way to prevent the negative responses looping forever between a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    pair of servers even with a short TTL.

  SECTION: [- Negative answers from the cache](#section-6)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When a server, in answering a query, encounters a cached negative
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response it MUST add the cached SOA record to the authority section
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of the response with the TTL decremented by the amount of time it was
    TEXT[!MUST]:    stored in the cache.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If a NXT record was cached along with SOA record it MUST be added to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the authority section.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If a SIG record was cached along with a NXT
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    record it SHOULD be added to the authority section.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    As with all answers coming from the cache, negative answers SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    have an implicit referral built into the answer.

  SECTION: [Server Failure (OPTIONAL)](#section-7.1)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    In either case a resolver MAY cache a server failure response.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If it
    TEXT[!MUST]:    does so it MUST NOT cache it for longer than five (5) minutes, and it
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST be cached against the specific query tuple <query name, type,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    class, server IP address>.

  SECTION: [Dead / Unreachable Server (OPTIONAL)](#section-7.2)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    A server MAY cache a dead server indication.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If it does so it MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NOT be deemed dead for longer than five (5) minutes.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The indication
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST be stored against query tuple <query name, type, class, server
    TEXT[!MUST]:    IP address> unless there was a transport layer indication that the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    server does not exist, in which case it applies to all queries to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    that specific IP address.

  SECTION: [- Changes from RFC 1034](#section-8)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Non-authoritative negative answers MAY be cached.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The SOA record from the authority section MUST be cached.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2782
  SECTION: [Abstract](#name-abstract)
    TEXT[!MUST]: Such specification MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    define the symbolic name to be used in the Service field of the SRV
    TEXT[!MUST]:    record as described below.
    TEXT[!MUST]: It also MUST include security
    TEXT[!MUST]:    considerations.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Service SRV records SHOULD NOT be used in the absence
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    of such specification.
    TEXT[!MUST]: A client MUST attempt to
    TEXT[!MUST]:         contact the target host with the lowest-numbered priority it can
    TEXT[!MUST]:         reach; target hosts with the same priority SHOULD be tried in an
    TEXT[!MUST]:         order defined by the weight field.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Larger
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:         weights SHOULD be given a proportionately higher probability of
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:         being selected.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Domain
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:         administrators SHOULD use Weight 0 when there isn't any server
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:         selection to do, to make the RR easier to read for humans (less
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:         noisy).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The following
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:         algorithm SHOULD be used to order the SRV RRs of the same
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:         priority:
    TEXT[!MUST]: There MUST be one or more
    TEXT[!MUST]:         address records for this name, the name MUST NOT be an alias (in
    TEXT[!MUST]:         the sense of RFC 1034 or RFC 2181).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A SRV-cognizant client SHOULD use this procedure to locate a list of
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    servers and connect to the preferred one:
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    - Port numbers SHOULD NOT be used in place of the symbolic service
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:      or protocol names (for the same reason why variant names cannot
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:      be allowed: Applications would have to do two or more lookups).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    - A client MUST parse all of the RR's in the reply.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    - If the Additional Data section doesn't contain address records
    TEXT[!MUST]:      for all the SRV RR's and the client may want to connect to the
    TEXT[!MUST]:      target host(s) involved, the client MUST look up the address
    TEXT[!MUST]:      record(s).

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2845
  SECTION: [- TSIG RR Format](#section-2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: TSIG is a meta-RR and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST not be cached.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Names and definitions of new algorithms
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST be registered with IANA.

  SECTION: [- Protocol Operation](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the TSIG
    TEXT[!MUST]:    record cannot be added without causing the message to be truncated,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the server MUST alter the response so that a TSIG can be included.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The client SHOULD at this
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    point retry the request using TCP (per [RFC1035 4.2.2]).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If an incoming message contains a TSIG record, it MUST be the last
    TEXT[!MUST]:    record in the additional section.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If a TSIG record is present in any other position, the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    packet is dropped and a response with RCODE 1 (FORMERR) MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    returned.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    algorithm name or key name is unknown to the recipient, or if the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    message digests do not match, the whole DNS message MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    discarded.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the message is a query, a response with RCODE 9
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (NOTAUTH) MUST be sent back to the originator with TSIG ERROR 17
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (BADKEY) or TSIG ERROR 16 (BADSIG).
    TEXT[!MUST]: If no key is available to sign
    TEXT[!MUST]:    this message it MUST be sent unsigned (MAC size == 0 and empty MAC).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A message to the system operations log SHOULD be generated, to warn
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the operations staff of a possible security incident in progress.

  SECTION: [- Protocol Details](#section-4)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The client MUST store the message digest from the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    request while awaiting an answer.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Clients SHOULD only attempt signed
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    transactions with servers who are known to support TSIG and share
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    some secret key with the client -- so, this is not a problem in
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    practice.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The server MUST not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    generate a signed response to an unsigned request.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    When a server detects an error relating to the key or MAC, the server
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD send back an unsigned error message (MAC size == 0 and empty
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    MAC).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If an error is detected relating to the TSIG validity period,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the server SHOULD send back a signed error message.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the error is not a TSIG error the response MUST be generated as
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specified in [4.2].
    TEXT[!MUST]: The TSIG MUST be included on the first and last DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    envelopes.
    TEXT[!MUST]: It is expensive to include it on every envelopes, but it
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST be placed on at least every 100'th envelope.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    client TSIG verification fails, the client MUST close the connection.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If the client does not receive TSIG records frequently enough (as
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    specified above) it SHOULD assume the connection has been hijacked
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    and it SHOULD close the connection.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The client SHOULD treat this the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    same way as they would any other interrupted transfer (although the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    exact behavior is not specified).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If one exists, the server is REQUIRED to return a TSIG RR in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The server MUST perform the following checks in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    following order, check KEY, check TIME values, check MAC.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If a non-forwarding server does not recognize the key used by the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    client, the server MUST generate an error response with RCODE 9
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (NOTAUTH) and TSIG ERROR 17 (BADKEY).
    TEXT[!MUST]: This response MUST be unsigned
    TEXT[!MUST]:    as specified in [4.3].
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The server SHOULD log the error.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the server time is outside the time interval specified by the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    request (which is: Time Signed, plus/minus Fudge), the server MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    generate an error response with RCODE 9 (NOTAUTH) and TSIG ERROR 18
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (BADTIME).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The server SHOULD also cache the most recent time signed
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    value in a message generated by a key, and SHOULD return BADTIME if a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    message received later has an earlier time signed value.
    TEXT[!MUST]: A response
    TEXT[!MUST]:    indicating a BADTIME error MUST be signed by the same key as the
    TEXT[!MUST]: It MUST include the client's current time in the time
    TEXT[!MUST]:    signed field, the server's current time (a u_int48_t) in the other
    TEXT[!MUST]:    data field, and 6 in the other data length field.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If a TSIG fails to verify, the server MUST generate an error response
    TEXT[!MUST]:    as specified in [4.3] with RCODE 9 (NOTAUTH) and TSIG ERROR 16
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (BADSIG).
    TEXT[!MUST]: If
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the TSIG does not validate, that response MUST be discarded, unless
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the RCODE is 9 (NOTAUTH), in which case the client SHOULD attempt to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    verify the response as if it were a TSIG Error response, as specified
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in [4.3].
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: A message containing an unsigned TSIG record or a TSIG
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    record which fails verification SHOULD not be considered an
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    acceptable response; the client SHOULD log an error and continue to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    wait for a signed response until the request times out.
    TEXT[!MAY]: The client MAY retry the request
    TEXT[!MAY]:    using the key specified by the server.
    TEXT[!MUST]: This should never occur, as a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    server MUST NOT sign a response with a different key than signed the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    request.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: In this case
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the client SHOULD log the event.
    TEXT[!MUST]: DNS resolvers MUST NOT adjust any
    TEXT[!MUST]:    clocks in the client based on BADTIME errors, but the server's time
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in the other data field SHOULD be logged.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    If the response RCODE is 9 (NOTAUTH) and TSIG ERROR is 16 (BADSIG),
    TEXT[!MAY]:    this is a MAC error, and client MAY retry the request with a new
    TEXT[!MAY]:    request ID but it would be better to try a different shared key if
    TEXT[!MAY]:    one is available.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Client SHOULD keep track of how many MAC errors
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    are associated with each key.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Clients SHOULD log this event.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A server acting as a forwarding server of a DNS message SHOULD check
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    for the existence of a TSIG record.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the name on the TSIG is not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of a secret that the server shares with the originator the server
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST forward the message unchanged including the TSIG.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the name
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of the TSIG is of a key this server shares with the originator, it
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST process the TSIG.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the TSIG passes all checks, the forwarding
    TEXT[!MUST]:    server MUST, if possible, include a TSIG of his own, to the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    destination or the next forwarder.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If no transaction security is
    TEXT[!MUST]:    available to the destination and the response has the AD flag (see
    TEXT[!MUST]:    [RFC2535]), the forwarder MUST unset the AD flag before adding the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    TSIG to the answer.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3007
  SECTION: [- Data and message signatures](#section-1.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    As specified in [RFC3008], the DNSSEC validation process performed by
    TEXT[!MUST]:    a resolver MUST NOT process any non-zone keys unless local policy
    TEXT[!MUST]:    dictates otherwise.
    TEXT[!MUST]: When performing secure dynamic update, all zone
    TEXT[!MUST]:    data modified in a signed zone MUST be signed by a relevant zone key.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Thus, host
    TEXT[!MAY]:    and user keys MAY be used to generate SIG(0) records to authenticate
    TEXT[!MAY]:    updates and MAY be used in the TKEY [RFC2930] process to generate
    TEXT[!MAY]:    TSIG shared secrets.

  SECTION: [- Signatory strength](#section-1.5)
    TEXT[!MUST]: Updating [RFC2535], this field
    TEXT[!MUST]:    SHOULD be set to 0 in KEY records, and MUST be ignored.

  SECTION: [- Authentication](#section-2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    TSIG or SIG(0) records MUST be included in all secure dynamic update
    TEXT[!MUST]:    messages.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the message contains a TSIG generated by a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    dynamically configured shared secret, the principal is the same as
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the one that authenticated the TKEY process; if the TKEY process was
    TEXT[!MUST]:    unauthenticated, no information is known about the principal, and the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    associated TSIG shared secret MUST NOT be used for secure dynamic
    TEXT[!MUST]:    update.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SIG(0) signatures SHOULD NOT be generated by zone keys, since
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    transactions are initiated by a host or user, not a zone.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNSSEC SIG records (other than SIG(0)) MAY be included in an update
    TEXT[!MUST]:    message, but MUST NOT be used to authenticate the update request.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If an update fails because it is signed with an unauthorized key, the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    server MUST indicate failure by returning a message with RCODE
    TEXT[!MUST]:    REFUSED.

  SECTION: [- Policy](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: By
    TEXT[!MUST]:    default, a principal MUST NOT be permitted to make any changes to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    zone data; any permissions MUST be enabled though configuration.

  SECTION: [- Standard policies](#section-3.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Implementations SHOULD allow access control policies to use the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    principal as an authorization token, and MAY also allow policies to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    grant permission to a signed message regardless of principal.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Implementations SHOULD allow per-name access control, and SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    provide a concise representation of the principal's own name, its
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    subdomains, and all names in the zone.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Additionally, a server SHOULD allow restricting updates by RR type,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    so that a principal could add, delete, or modify specific record
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    types at certain names.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Implementations SHOULD allow per-type access
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    control, and SHOULD provide concise representations of all types and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    all "user" types, where a user type is defined as one that does not
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    affect the operation of DNS itself.

  SECTION: [- User types](#section-3.1.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: SOA
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    and NS records SHOULD NOT be modified by normal users, since these
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    types create or modify delegation points.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NXT records MUST NOT be created, modified, or deleted by dynamic
    TEXT[!MUST]:    update, as their update may cause instability in the protocol.

  SECTION: [- Adding SIGs](#section-4.1)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    An authorized update request MAY include SIG records with each RRset.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Since SIG records (except SIG(0) records) MUST NOT be used for
    TEXT[!MUST]:    authentication of the update message, they are not required.
    TEXT[!MAY]: The server MAY examine SIG records and drop SIGs with
    TEXT[!MAY]:    a temporal validity period in the past.

  SECTION: [- Deleting SIGs](#section-4.2)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    If a principal is authorized to update SIG records and the update
    TEXT[!MAY]:    specifies the deletion of SIG records, the server MAY choose to
    TEXT[!MAY]:    override the authority and refuse the update.

  SECTION: [- Non-explicit updates to SIGs](#section-4.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the updated zone is secured, the RRset affected by an update
    TEXT[!MUST]:    operation MUST, at the completion of the update, be signed in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    accordance with the zone's signing policy.
    TEXT[!MUST]: This will usually require
    TEXT[!MUST]:    one or more SIG records to be generated by one or more zone keys
    TEXT[!MUST]:    whose private components MUST be online [RFC3008].
    TEXT[!MAY]:    When the contents of an RRset are updated, the server MAY delete all
    TEXT[!MAY]:    associated SIG records, since they will no longer be valid.

  SECTION: [- Effects on the zone](#section-4.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If any changes are made, the server MUST, if necessary, generate a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    new SOA record and new NXT records, and sign these with the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    appropriate zone keys.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3225
  SECTION: [Protocol Changes](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The DO bit cleared
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (set to zero) indicates the resolver is unprepared to handle DNSSEC
    TEXT[!MUST]:    security RRs and those RRs MUST NOT be returned in the response
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (unless DNSSEC security RRs are explicitly queried for).
    TEXT[!MUST]: The DO bit
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of the query MUST be copied in the response.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    More explicitly, DNSSEC-aware nameservers MUST NOT insert SIG, KEY,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    or NXT RRs to authenticate a response as specified in [RFC2535]
    TEXT[!MUST]:    unless the DO bit was set on the request.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A recursive DNSSEC-aware server MUST set the DO bit on recursive
    TEXT[!MUST]:    requests, regardless of the status of the DO bit on the initiating
    TEXT[!MUST]:    resolver request.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the initiating resolver request does not have
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the DO bit set, the recursive DNSSEC-aware server MUST remove DNSSEC
    TEXT[!MUST]:    security RRs before returning the data to the client, however cached
    TEXT[!MUST]:    data MUST NOT be modified.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In the event a server returns a NOTIMP, FORMERR or SERVFAIL response
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    to a query that has the DO bit set, the resolver SHOULD NOT expect
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DNSSEC security RRs and SHOULD retry the query without EDNS0 in
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    accordance with section 5.3 of [RFC2671].

  SECTION: [Security Considerations](#name-security-considerations)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The absence of DNSSEC data in response to a query with the DO bit set
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST NOT be taken to mean no security information is available for
    TEXT[!MUST]:    that zone as the response may be forged or a non-forged response of
    TEXT[!MUST]:    an altered (DO bit cleared) query.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3445
  SECTION: [Definition of the KEY RR](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In the flags field, all bits except bit 7 are reserved and MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    zero.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The protocol field MUST be set to 3.

  SECTION: [Changes from RFC 2535 KEY RR](#section-4)
    TEXT[!MUST]: They MUST be set to 0
    TEXT[!MUST]:       and MUST be ignored by the receiver.
    TEXT[!MUST]: It MUST be set to 0
    TEXT[!MUST]:       and MUST be ignored by the receiver.
    TEXT[!MUST]: They are reserved, MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:       set to zero and MUST be ignored by the receiver.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The authoritative data for a zone MUST NOT include any KEY records
    TEXT[!MUST]:    with a protocol octet other than 3.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Name servers and resolvers SHOULD accept KEY RR sets that contain KEY
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    RRs with a value other than 3.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Note that KEY RRs with a protocol octet value
    TEXT[!MUST]:    other than 3 MUST NOT be used to authenticate DNS data.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3597
  SECTION: [Transparency](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    To enable new RR types to be deployed without server changes, name
    TEXT[!MUST]:    servers and resolvers MUST handle RRs of unknown type transparently.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    To ensure the correct operation of equality comparison (section 6)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and of the DNSSEC canonical form (section 7) when an RR type is known
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to some but not all of the servers involved, servers MUST also
    TEXT[!MUST]:    exactly preserve the RDATA of RRs of known type, except for changes
    TEXT[!MUST]:    due to compression or decompression where allowed by section 4 of
    TEXT[!MUST]:    this memo.
    TEXT[!MUST]: In particular, the character case of domain names that
    TEXT[!MUST]:    are not subject to compression MUST be preserved.

  SECTION: [Domain Name Compression](#section-4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    To avoid such corruption, servers MUST NOT compress domain names
    TEXT[!MUST]:    embedded in the RDATA of types that are class-specific or not well-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    known.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Receiving servers MUST decompress domain names in RRs of well-known
    TEXT[!MUST]:    type, and SHOULD also decompress RRs of type RP, AFSDB, RT, SIG, PX,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NXT, NAPTR, and SRV (although the current specification of the SRV RR
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in [RFC2782] prohibits compression, [RFC2052] mandated it, and some
    TEXT[!MUST]:    servers following that earlier specification are still in use).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Future specifications for new RR types that contain domain names
    TEXT[!MUST]:    within their RDATA MUST NOT allow the use of name compression for
    TEXT[!MUST]:    those names, and SHOULD explicitly state that the embedded domain
    TEXT[!MUST]:    names MUST NOT be compressed.

  SECTION: [Text Representation](#section-5)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    An implementation MAY also choose to represent some RRs of known type
    TEXT[!MAY]:    using the above generic representations for the type, class and/or
    TEXT[!MAY]:    RDATA, which carries the benefit of making the resulting master file
    TEXT[!MAY]:    portable to servers where these types are unknown.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Even though an RR of known type represented in the \# format is
    TEXT[!MUST]:    effectively treated as an unknown type for the purpose of parsing the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RDATA text representation, all further processing by the server MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    treat it as a known type and take into account any applicable type-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specific rules regarding compression, canonicalization, etc.

  SECTION: [Equality Comparison](#section-6)
    TEXT[!MUST]: To ensure that
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the outcome of the comparison is identical whether the RR is known to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the server or not, specifications for new RR types MUST NOT specify
    TEXT[!MUST]:    type-specific comparison rules.

  SECTION: [Additional Section Processing](#section-8)
    TEXT[!MUST]: Future RR
    TEXT[!MUST]:    type specifications MAY specify type-specific additional section
    TEXT[!MUST]:    processing rules, but any such processing MUST be optional as it can
    TEXT[!MUST]:    only be performed by servers for which the RR type in case is known.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3658
  SECTION: [Reserved Words](#section-1.2)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    The key words "MAY", "MAY NOT", "MUST", "MUST NOT", "REQUIRED",
    TEXT[!MAY]:    "RECOMMENDED", "SHOULD", and "SHOULD NOT" in this document are to be
    TEXT[!MAY]:    interpreted as described in BCP 14, RFC 2119 [RFC2119].

  SECTION: [Protocol Change](#section-2.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    All DNS servers and resolvers that support DS MUST support the OK bit
    TEXT[!MUST]:    [RFC3225] and a larger message size [RFC3226].
    TEXT[!MUST]: In order for a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    delegation to be considered secure the delegation MUST contain a DS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRset.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If a query contains the OK bit, a nameserver returning a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    referral for the delegation MUST include the following RRsets in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    authority section in this order:
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the DS or NXT RRsets with signatures
    TEXT[!MUST]:    do not fit in the DNS message, the TC bit MUST be set.
    TEXT[!MUST]: DS RRsets MUST NOT appear
    TEXT[!MUST]:    at non-delegation points or at a zone's apex.

  SECTION: [RFC 2535 2.3.4 and 3.4: Special Considerations at Delegation](#section-2.2.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Each DS RRset stored in the parent zone MUST be signed by at least
    TEXT[!MUST]:    one of the parent zone's private keys.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The parent zone MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    contain a KEY RRset at any delegation point.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Delegations in the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    parent MAY contain only the following RR types: NS, DS, NXT and SIG.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The NS RRset MUST NOT be signed.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A secure zone MUST contain a self-signed KEY RRset at its apex.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Upon
    TEXT[!MAY]:    verifying the DS RRset from the parent, a resolver MAY trust any KEY
    TEXT[!MAY]:    identified in the DS RRset as a valid signer of the child's apex KEY
    TEXT[!MAY]:    RRset.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Resolvers configured to trust one of the keys signing the KEY
    TEXT[!MAY]:    RRset MAY now treat any data signed by the zone keys in the KEY RRset
    TEXT[!MAY]:    as secure.
    TEXT[!MUST]: In all other cases, resolvers MUST consider the zone
    TEXT[!MUST]:    unsecure.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    An authoritative nameserver queried for type DS MUST return the DS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRset in the answer section.

  SECTION: [Special processing for DS queries](#section-2.2.1.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When a nameserver is authoritative for the parent zone at a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    delegation point and receives a query for the DS record at that name,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    it MUST answer based on data in the parent zone, return DS or
    TEXT[!MUST]:    negative answer.
    TEXT[!MUST]: As these queries are only expected to originate
    TEXT[!MUST]:    from recursive nameservers which are not DS-aware, the authoritative
    TEXT[!MUST]:    nameserver MUST answer with:
    TEXT[!MAY]:    A nameserver authoritative for only the child zone, that is also a
    TEXT[!MAY]:    caching server MAY (if the RD bit is set in the query) perform
    TEXT[!MAY]:    recursion to find the DS record at the delegation point, or MAY
    TEXT[!MAY]:    return the DS record from its cache.
    TEXT[!MUST]: In this case, the AA bit MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NOT be set in the response.

  SECTION: [Special processing when child and an ancestor share](#section-2.2.1.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When a nameserver receives a query for (<QNAME>, DS, <QCLASS>), the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response MUST be determined from reading these rules in order:

  SECTION: [Modification on use of KEY RR in the construction of Responses](#section-2.2.1.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A query for KEY RR MUST NOT trigger any additional section
    TEXT[!MUST]:    processing.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    KEY records SHOULD NOT be added to the additional records section in
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    response to any query.

  SECTION: [Signer's Name (replaces RFC 3008 section 2.7)](#section-2.2.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The signer's name field of a SIG RR MUST contain the name of the zone
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to which the data and signature belong.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The combination of signer's
    TEXT[!MUST]:    name, key tag, and algorithm MUST identify a zone key if the SIG is
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to be considered material.
    TEXT[!MAY]: This document defines a standard policy
    TEXT[!MAY]:    for DNSSEC validation; local policy MAY override the standard policy.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The
    TEXT[!MUST]:    combination of signer's name, key tag, and algorithm MUST identify a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    key if this SIG(0) is to be processed.

  SECTION: [RFC 3090 section 2.1: Globally Secured](#section-2.2.3.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The KEY RRset at a zone's apex MUST be self-signed by a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    private key whose public counterpart MUST appear in a zone signing
    TEXT[!MUST]:    KEY RR (2.a) owned by the zone's apex and specifying a mandatory-to-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    implement algorithm.
    TEXT[!MUST]: This KEY RR MUST be identified by a DS RR in a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    signed DS RRset in the parent zone.

  SECTION: [Comments on Protocol Changes](#section-2.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: Many old nameservers and resolvers MUST be upgraded
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to take advantage of DS.

  SECTION: [Wire Format of the DS record](#section-2.4)
    TEXT[!MAY]: Other keys
    TEXT[!MAY]:    MAY sign the child's apex KEY RRset.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Algorithm MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be allowed to sign DNS data.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: For interoperability
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    reasons, keeping number of digest algorithms low is strongly
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    RECOMMENDED.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DS records MUST point to zone KEY records that are allowed to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    authenticate DNS data.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The indicated KEY records protocol field MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be set to 3; flag field bit 7 MUST be set to 1.

  SECTION: [DS Example](#section-3.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    This example has only one DS record for the child, but parents MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    allow multiple DS records to facilitate key roll-over and multiple
    TEXT[!MUST]:    KEY algorithms.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Note the NXT record
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD only be examined after verifying the corresponding signature.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc3757
  SECTION: [Introduction](#section-1)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    The key words "MAY","MAY NOT", "MUST", "MUST NOT", "REQUIRED",
    TEXT[!MAY]:    "RECOMMENDED", "SHOULD", and "SHOULD NOT" in this document are to be
    TEXT[!MAY]:    interpreted as described in BCP 14, RFC 2119 [1].

  SECTION: [The Secure Entry Point (SEP) Flag](#section-2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: One SHOULD NOT assign special
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    meaning to the key if the bit is set to 0.

  SECTION: [DNSSEC Protocol Changes](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The bit MUST NOT be used during the resolving and verification
    TEXT[!MUST]:    process.

  SECTION: [Operational Guidelines](#section-4)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    The SEP bit is set by the key-pair-generator and MAY be used by the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    zone signer to decide whether the public part of the key pair is to
    TEXT[!MAY]:    be prepared for input to a DS RR generation function.

  SECTION: [Security Considerations](#section-5)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    No trust in a key should be inferred from this flag - trust MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    inferred from an existing chain of trust or an out-of-band exchange.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc4034
  SECTION: [The DNSKEY Resource Record](#section-2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The DNSKEY RR is not intended as a record for storing arbitrary
    TEXT[!MUST]:    public keys and MUST NOT be used to store certificates or public keys
    TEXT[!MUST]:    that do not directly relate to the DNS infrastructure.

  SECTION: [The Flags Field](#section-2.1.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: If bit 7 has value 1,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    then the DNSKEY record holds a DNS zone key, and the DNSKEY RR's
    TEXT[!MUST]:    owner name MUST be the name of a zone.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If bit 7 has value 0, then
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the DNSKEY record holds some other type of DNS public key and MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NOT be used to verify RRSIGs that cover RRsets.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    intended to be a hint to zone signing or debugging software as to the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    intended use of this DNSKEY record; validators MUST NOT alter their
    TEXT[!MUST]:    behavior during the signature validation process in any way based on
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the setting of this bit.
    TEXT[!MUST]: A DNSKEY RR with the SEP set and the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Zone Key flag not set MUST NOT be used to verify RRSIGs that cover
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRsets.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Bits 0-6 and 8-14 are reserved: these bits MUST have value 0 upon
    TEXT[!MUST]:    creation of the DNSKEY RR and MUST be ignored upon receipt.

  SECTION: [The Protocol Field](#section-2.1.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Protocol Field MUST have value 3, and the DNSKEY RR MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    treated as invalid during signature verification if it is found to be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    some value other than 3.

  SECTION: [The DNSKEY RR Presentation Format](#section-2.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Flag field MUST be represented as an unsigned decimal integer.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Protocol Field MUST be represented as an unsigned decimal integer
    TEXT[!MUST]:    with a value of 3.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Algorithm field MUST be represented either as an unsigned decimal
    TEXT[!MUST]:    integer or as an algorithm mnemonic as specified in Appendix A.1.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Public Key field MUST be represented as a Base64 encoding of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Public Key.

  SECTION: [The RRSIG Resource Record](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The RRSIG RR MUST only be used
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to carry verification material (digital signatures) used to secure
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNS operations.
    TEXT[!MUST]: A RRSIG and NSEC (see Section 4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST exist for the same name as a CNAME resource record in a signed
    TEXT[!MUST]:    zone.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    An RRSIG RR MUST have the same class as the RRset it covers.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The TTL value of an RRSIG RR MUST match the TTL value of the RRset it
    TEXT[!MUST]:    covers.

  SECTION: [The Labels Field](#section-3.1.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The value of the Labels field MUST NOT count either the null (root)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    label that terminates the owner name or the wildcard label (if
    TEXT[!MUST]:    present).
    TEXT[!MUST]: The value of the Labels field MUST be less than or equal
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to the number of labels in the RRSIG owner name.

  SECTION: [Signature Expiration and Inception Fields](#section-3.1.5)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The RRSIG record MUST NOT be used for
    TEXT[!MUST]:    authentication prior to the inception date and MUST NOT be used for
    TEXT[!MUST]:    authentication after the expiration date.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Because
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of this, all comparisons involving these fields MUST use "Serial
    TEXT[!MUST]:    number arithmetic", as defined in [RFC1982].

  SECTION: [The Signer's Name Field](#section-3.1.7)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Signer's Name field MUST contain the name of the zone of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    covered RRset.
    TEXT[!MUST]: A sender MUST NOT use DNS name compression on the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Signer's Name field when transmitting a RRSIG RR.

  SECTION: [Signature Calculation](#section-3.1.8.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:                Each RR MUST have the same owner name as the RRSIG RR;
    TEXT[!MUST]:                Each RR MUST have the same class as the RRSIG RR;
    TEXT[!MUST]:                Each RR in the RRset MUST have the RR type listed in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:                RRSIG RR's Type Covered field;
    TEXT[!MUST]:                Each RR in the RRset MUST have the TTL listed in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:                RRSIG Original TTL Field;
    TEXT[!MUST]:                Any DNS names in the RDATA field of each RR MUST be in
    TEXT[!MUST]:                canonical form; and
    TEXT[!MUST]:                The RRset MUST be sorted in canonical order.

  SECTION: [The RRSIG RR Presentation Format](#section-3.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: When
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the mnemonic is not known, the TYPE representation as described in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    [RFC3597], Section 5, MUST be used.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Algorithm field value MUST be represented either as an unsigned
    TEXT[!MUST]:    decimal integer or as an algorithm mnemonic, as specified in Appendix
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A.1.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Labels field value MUST be represented as an unsigned decimal
    TEXT[!MUST]:    integer.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Original TTL field value MUST be represented as an unsigned
    TEXT[!MUST]:    decimal integer.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Signature Expiration Time and Inception Time field values MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    represented either as an unsigned decimal integer indicating seconds
    TEXT[!MUST]:    since 1 January 1970 00:00:00 UTC, or in the form YYYYMMDDHHmmSS in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    UTC, where:
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Key Tag field MUST be represented as an unsigned decimal integer.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Signer's Name field value MUST be represented as a domain name.

  SECTION: [The NSEC Resource Record](#section-4)
    TEXT[!MUST]: An RRSIG (see Section 3) and NSEC MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    exist for the same name as does a CNAME resource record in a signed
    TEXT[!MUST]:    zone.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The NSEC RR SHOULD have the same TTL value as the SOA minimum TTL
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    field.

  SECTION: [The Next Domain Name Field](#section-4.1.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A sender MUST NOT use DNS name compression on the Next Domain Name
    TEXT[!MUST]:    field when transmitting an NSEC RR.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Owner names of RRsets for which the given zone is not authoritative
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (such as glue records) MUST NOT be listed in the Next Domain Name
    TEXT[!MUST]:    unless at least one authoritative RRset exists at the same owner
    TEXT[!MUST]:    name.

  SECTION: [The Type Bit Maps Field](#section-4.1.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Bits representing pseudo-types MUST be clear, as they do not appear
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in zone data.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If encountered, they MUST be ignored upon being read.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Blocks with no types present MUST NOT be included.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Trailing zero
    TEXT[!MUST]:    octets in the bitmap MUST be omitted.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Trailing zero octets not specified MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    interpreted as zero octets.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Bits corresponding to the delegation NS RRset and the RR
    TEXT[!MUST]:    types for which the parent zone has authoritative data MUST be set;
    TEXT[!MUST]:    bits corresponding to any non-NS RRset for which the parent is not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    authoritative MUST be clear.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A zone MUST NOT include an NSEC RR for any domain name that only
    TEXT[!MUST]:    holds glue records.

  SECTION: [The NSEC RR Presentation Format](#section-4.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: When the mnemonic is not known, the TYPE representation
    TEXT[!MUST]:    described in [RFC3597], Section 5, MUST be used.

  SECTION: [Processing of DS RRs When Validating Responses](#section-5.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The DNSKEY RR referred
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to in the DS RR MUST be a DNSSEC zone key.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The DNSKEY RR Flags MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    have Flags bit 7 set.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the DNSKEY flags do not indicate a DNSSEC
    TEXT[!MUST]:    zone key, the DS RR (and the DNSKEY RR it references) MUST NOT be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    used in the validation process.

  SECTION: [The DS RR Presentation Format](#section-5.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Key Tag field MUST be represented as an unsigned decimal integer.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Algorithm field MUST be represented either as an unsigned decimal
    TEXT[!MUST]:    integer or as an algorithm mnemonic specified in Appendix A.1.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Digest Type field MUST be represented as an unsigned decimal
    TEXT[!MUST]:    integer.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Digest MUST be represented as a sequence of case-insensitive
    TEXT[!MUST]:    hexadecimal digits.

  SECTION: [Canonical RR Ordering within an RRset](#section-6.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: Therefore, if an implementation detects duplicate RRs when
    TEXT[!MUST]:    putting the RRset in canonical form, it MUST treat this as a protocol
    TEXT[!MUST]:    error.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the implementation chooses to handle this protocol error
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in the spirit of the robustness principle (being liberal in what it
    TEXT[!MUST]:    accepts), it MUST remove all but one of the duplicate RR(s) for the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    purposes of calculating the canonical form of the RRset.

  SECTION: [Security Considerations](#section-8)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The table of algorithms in Appendix A and the key tag calculation
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    algorithms in Appendix B include the RSA/MD5 algorithm for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    completeness, but the RSA/MD5 algorithm is NOT RECOMMENDED, as
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    explained in [RFC3110].

  SECTION: [DNSSEC Algorithm and Digest Types](#appendix-A)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A DNSSEC aware resolver or name server MUST implement all MANDATORY
    TEXT[!MUST]:    algorithms.

  SECTION: [DNSSEC Algorithm Types](#appendix-A.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:                                 Zone
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Value Algorithm [Mnemonic]  Signing  References   Status
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    ----- -------------------- --------- ----------  ---------
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:      0   reserved
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:      1   RSA/MD5 [RSAMD5]         n      [RFC2537]  NOT RECOMMENDED
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:      2   Diffie-Hellman [DH]      n      [RFC2539]   -
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:      3   DSA/SHA-1 [DSA]          y      [RFC2536]  OPTIONAL
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:      4   Elliptic Curve [ECC]              TBA       -
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:      5   RSA/SHA-1 [RSASHA1]      y      [RFC3110]  MANDATORY
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    252   Indirect [INDIRECT]      n                  -
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    253   Private [PRIVATEDNS]     y      see below  OPTIONAL
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    254   Private [PRIVATEOID]     y      see below  OPTIONAL
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    255   reserved

  SECTION: [Private Algorithm Types](#appendix-A.1.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The public key area in the DNSKEY
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RR and the signature area in the RRSIG RR begin with a wire encoded
    TEXT[!MUST]:    domain name, which MUST NOT be compressed.

  SECTION: [Key Tag Calculation](#appendix-B)
    TEXT[!MUST]: Implementations MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NOT assume that the key tag uniquely identifies a DNSKEY RR.
    TEXT[!MUST]: It is not necessary to use the following reference
    TEXT[!MUST]:    code verbatim, but the numerical value of the Key Tag MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    identical to what the reference implementation would generate for the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    same input.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Key Tags MUST be calculated
    TEXT[!MUST]:    using the algorithm described here rather than the ones complement
    TEXT[!MUST]:    checksum.

  SECTION: [Key Tag for Algorithm 1 (RSA/MD5)](#appendix-B.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Please note that Algorithm 1 is NOT RECOMMENDED.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc4035
  SECTION: [Including DNSKEY RRs in a Zone](#section-2.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: For each private key used to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    create RRSIG RRs in a zone, the zone SHOULD include a zone DNSKEY RR
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    containing the corresponding public key.
    TEXT[!MUST]: A zone key DNSKEY RR MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    have the Zone Key bit of the flags RDATA field set (see Section 2.1.1
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of [RFC4034]).
    TEXT[!MUST]: Public keys associated with other DNS operations MAY
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be stored in DNSKEY RRs that are not marked as zone keys but MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be used to verify RRSIGs.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the zone administrator intends a signed zone to be usable other
    TEXT[!MUST]:    than as an island of security, the zone apex MUST contain at least
    TEXT[!MUST]:    one DNSKEY RR to act as a secure entry point into the zone.

  SECTION: [Including RRSIG RRs in a Zone](#section-2.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    For each authoritative RRset in a signed zone, there MUST be at least
    TEXT[!MUST]:    one RRSIG record that meets the following requirements:
    TEXT[!MAY]: An RRset MAY have multiple RRSIG RRs
    TEXT[!MAY]:    associated with it.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    An RRSIG RR itself MUST NOT be signed, as signing an RRSIG RR would
    TEXT[!MUST]:    add no value and would create an infinite loop in the signing
    TEXT[!MUST]:    process.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The NS RRset that appears at the zone apex name MUST be signed, but
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the NS RRsets that appear at delegation points (that is, the NS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRsets in the parent zone that delegate the name to the child zone's
    TEXT[!MUST]:    name servers) MUST NOT be signed.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Glue address RRsets associated
    TEXT[!MUST]:    with delegations MUST NOT be signed.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    There MUST be an RRSIG for each RRset using at least one DNSKEY of
    TEXT[!MUST]:    each algorithm in the zone apex DNSKEY RRset.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The apex DNSKEY RRset
    TEXT[!MUST]:    itself MUST be signed by each algorithm appearing in the DS RRset
    TEXT[!MUST]:    located at the delegating parent (if any).

  SECTION: [Including NSEC RRs in a Zone](#section-2.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Each owner name in the zone that has authoritative data or a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    delegation point NS RRset MUST have an NSEC resource record.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The TTL value for any NSEC RR SHOULD be the same as the minimum TTL
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    value field in the zone SOA RR.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    An NSEC record (and its associated RRSIG RRset) MUST NOT be the only
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRset at any particular owner name.
    TEXT[!MUST]: That is, the signing process
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST NOT create NSEC or RRSIG RRs for owner name nodes that were not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the owner name of any RRset before the zone was signed.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The type bitmap of every NSEC resource record in a signed zone MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    indicate the presence of both the NSEC record itself and its
    TEXT[!MUST]:    corresponding RRSIG record.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Bits corresponding to the delegation NS RRset and any
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRsets for which the parent zone has authoritative data MUST be set;
    TEXT[!MUST]:    bits corresponding to any non-NS RRset for which the parent is not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    authoritative MUST be clear.

  SECTION: [Including DS RRs in a Zone](#section-2.4)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: A DS RRset SHOULD be present at a delegation point when the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    child zone is signed.
    TEXT[!MAY]: The DS RRset MAY contain multiple records,
    TEXT[!MAY]:    each referencing a public key in the child zone used to verify the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    RRSIGs in that zone.
    TEXT[!MUST]: All DS RRsets in a zone MUST be signed, and DS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRsets MUST NOT appear at a zone's apex.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A DS RR SHOULD point to a DNSKEY RR that is present in the child's
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    apex DNSKEY RRset, and the child's apex DNSKEY RRset SHOULD be signed
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    by the corresponding private key.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The TTL of a DS RRset SHOULD match the TTL of the delegating NS RRset
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    (that is, the NS RRset from the same zone containing the DS RRset).

  SECTION: [Changes to the CNAME Resource Record](#section-2.5)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If a CNAME RRset is present at a name in a signed zone, appropriate
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRSIG and NSEC RRsets are REQUIRED at that name.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Other types MUST NOT be present at that name.

  SECTION: [DNSSEC RR Types Appearing at Zone Cuts](#section-2.6)
    TEXT[!MUST]: At the parental side of a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    zone cut (that is, at a delegation point), NSEC RRs are REQUIRED at
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the owner name.

  SECTION: [Serving](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A security-aware name server MUST support the EDNS0 ([RFC2671])
    TEXT[!MUST]:    message size extension, MUST support a message size of at least 1220
    TEXT[!MUST]:    octets, and SHOULD support a message size of 4000 octets.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: As IPv6
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    packets can only be fragmented by the source host, a security aware
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    name server SHOULD take steps to ensure that UDP datagrams it
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    transmits over IPv6 are fragmented, if necessary, at the minimum IPv6
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    MTU, unless the path MTU is known.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A security-aware name server that receives a DNS query that does not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    include the EDNS OPT pseudo-RR or that has the DO bit clear MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    treat the RRSIG, DNSKEY, and NSEC RRs as it would any other RRset and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST NOT perform any of the additional processing described below.
    TEXT[!MAY]: As long as the response is always
    TEXT[!MAY]:    consistent for each query to the name server, the name server MAY
    TEXT[!MAY]:    return one of the following:
    TEXT[!MUST]: The CD bit
    TEXT[!MUST]:    is controlled by resolvers; a security-aware name server MUST copy
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the CD bit from a query into the corresponding response.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The AD bit
    TEXT[!MUST]:    is controlled by name servers; a security-aware name server MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    ignore the setting of the AD bit in queries.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A security aware name server that synthesizes CNAME RRs from DNAME
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    RRs as described in [RFC2672] SHOULD NOT generate signatures for the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    synthesized CNAME RRs.

  SECTION: [Authoritative Name Servers](#section-3.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Upon receiving a relevant query that has the EDNS ([RFC2671]) OPT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    pseudo-RR DO bit ([RFC3225]) set, a security-aware authoritative name
    TEXT[!MUST]:    server for a signed zone MUST include additional RRSIG, NSEC, and DS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRs, according to the following rules:
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  RRSIG RRs that can be used to authenticate a response MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:       included in the response according to the rules in Section 3.1.1.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  NSEC RRs that can be used to provide authenticated denial of
    TEXT[!MUST]:       existence MUST be included in the response automatically according
    TEXT[!MUST]:       to the rules in Section 3.1.3.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  Either a DS RRset or an NSEC RR proving that no DS RRs exist MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:       be included in referrals automatically according to the rules in
    TEXT[!MUST]:       Section 3.1.4.

  SECTION: [Including RRSIG RRs in a Response](#section-3.1.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    When responding to a query that has the DO bit set, a security-aware
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    authoritative name server SHOULD attempt to send RRSIG RRs that a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    security-aware resolver can use to authenticate the RRsets in the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    response.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: A name server SHOULD make every attempt to keep the RRset
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    and its associated RRSIG(s) together in a response.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  When placing a signed RRset in the Answer section, the name server
    TEXT[!MUST]:       MUST also place its RRSIG RRs in the Answer section.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If space does not permit inclusion
    TEXT[!MUST]:       of these RRSIG RRs, the name server MUST set the TC bit.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  When placing a signed RRset in the Authority section, the name
    TEXT[!MUST]:       server MUST also place its RRSIG RRs in the Authority section.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  When placing a signed RRset in the Additional section, the name
    TEXT[!MUST]:       server MUST also place its RRSIG RRs in the Additional section.
    TEXT[!MAY]:       If space does not permit inclusion of both the RRset and its
    TEXT[!MAY]:       associated RRSIG RRs, the name server MAY retain the RRset while
    TEXT[!MAY]:       dropping the RRSIG RRs.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If this happens, the name server MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:       set the TC bit solely because these RRSIG RRs didn't fit.

  SECTION: [Including DNSKEY RRs in a Response](#section-3.1.2)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    When responding to a query that has the DO bit set and that requests
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the SOA or NS RRs at the apex of a signed zone, a security-aware
    TEXT[!MAY]:    authoritative name server for that zone MAY return the zone apex
    TEXT[!MAY]:    DNSKEY RRset in the Additional section.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The name server SHOULD NOT include the DNSKEY RRset unless there is
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    enough space in the response message for both the DNSKEY RRset and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    its associated RRSIG RR(s).
    TEXT[!MUST]: If there is not enough space to include
    TEXT[!MUST]:    these DNSKEY and RRSIG RRs, the name server MUST omit them and MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NOT set the TC bit solely because these RRs didn't fit (see Section
    TEXT[!MUST]:    3.1.1).

  SECTION: [Including NSEC RRs in a Response](#section-3.1.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When responding to a query that has the DO bit set, a security-aware
    TEXT[!MUST]:    authoritative name server for a signed zone MUST include NSEC RRs in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    each of the following cases:

  SECTION: [Including NSEC RRs: No Data Response](#section-3.1.3.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the zone contains RRsets matching <SNAME, SCLASS> but contains no
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRset matching <SNAME, SCLASS, STYPE>, then the name server MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    include the NSEC RR for <SNAME, SCLASS> along with its associated
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRSIG RR(s) in the Authority section of the response (see Section
    TEXT[!MUST]:    3.1.1).
    TEXT[!MUST]: If space does not permit inclusion of the NSEC RR or its
    TEXT[!MUST]:    associated RRSIG RR(s), the name server MUST set the TC bit (see
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Section 3.1.1).

  SECTION: [Including NSEC RRs: Name Error Response](#section-3.1.3.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the zone does not contain any RRsets matching <SNAME, SCLASS>
    TEXT[!MUST]:    either exactly or via wildcard name expansion, then the name server
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST include the following NSEC RRs in the Authority section, along
    TEXT[!MUST]:    with their associated RRSIG RRs:
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    it does, the name server SHOULD only include the NSEC RR and its
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    RRSIG RR(s) once in the Authority section.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If space does not permit inclusion of these NSEC and RRSIG RRs, the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    name server MUST set the TC bit (see Section 3.1.1).

  SECTION: [Including NSEC RRs: Wildcard Answer Response](#section-3.1.3.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the zone does not contain any RRsets that exactly match <SNAME,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    SCLASS> but does contain an RRset that matches <SNAME, SCLASS, STYPE>
    TEXT[!MUST]:    via wildcard name expansion, the name server MUST include the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    wildcard-expanded answer and the corresponding wildcard-expanded
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRSIG RRs in the Answer section and MUST include in the Authority
    TEXT[!MUST]:    section an NSEC RR and associated RRSIG RR(s) proving that the zone
    TEXT[!MUST]:    does not contain a closer match for <SNAME, SCLASS>.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If space does
    TEXT[!MUST]:    not permit inclusion of the answer, NSEC and RRSIG RRs, the name
    TEXT[!MUST]:    server MUST set the TC bit (see Section 3.1.1).

  SECTION: [Including NSEC RRs: Wildcard No Data Response](#section-3.1.3.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The name server MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    include the following NSEC RRs in the Authority section, along with
    TEXT[!MUST]:    their associated RRSIG RRs:
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    it does, the name server SHOULD only include the NSEC RR and its
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    RRSIG RR(s) once in the Authority section.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If space does not permit inclusion of these NSEC and RRSIG RRs, the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    name server MUST set the TC bit (see Section 3.1.1).

  SECTION: [Including DS RRs in a Response](#section-3.1.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If a DS RRset is present at the delegation point, the name server
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST return both the DS RRset and its associated RRSIG RR(s) in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Authority section along with the NS RRset.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If no DS RRset is present at the delegation point, the name server
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST return both the NSEC RR that proves that the DS RRset is not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    present and the NSEC RR's associated RRSIG RR(s) along with the NS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRset.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The name server MUST place the NS RRset before the NSEC RRset
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and its associated RRSIG RR(s).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If space does not permit inclusion of the DS or NSEC RRset and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    associated RRSIG RRs, the name server MUST set the TC bit (see
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Section 3.1.1).

  SECTION: [Responding to Queries for DS RRs](#section-3.1.4.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: In
    TEXT[!MUST]:    this case, the name server MUST return an authoritative "no data"
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response showing that the DS RRset does not exist in the child zone's
    TEXT[!MUST]:    apex.

  SECTION: [Responding to Queries for Type AXFR or IXFR](#section-3.1.5)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    However, an authoritative name server MAY choose to reject the entire
    TEXT[!MAY]:    zone transfer if the zone fails to meet any of the signing
    TEXT[!MAY]:    requirements described in Section 2.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    chooses to perform its own zone validation MUST NOT selectively
    TEXT[!MUST]:    reject some RRs and accept others.
    TEXT[!MUST]: As with any other
    TEXT[!MUST]:    authoritative RRset, the DS RRset MUST be included in zone transfers
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of the zone in which the RRset is authoritative data.
    TEXT[!MUST]: As
    TEXT[!MUST]:    with any other authoritative RRs, NSEC RRs MUST be included in zone
    TEXT[!MUST]:    transfers of the zone in which they are authoritative data.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The
    TEXT[!MUST]:    parental NSEC RR at a zone cut MUST be included in zone transfers of
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the parent zone, and the NSEC at the zone apex of the child zone MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be included in zone transfers of the child zone.
    TEXT[!MUST]: As with any other authoritative
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRs, RRSIG RRs MUST be included in zone transfers of the zone in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    which they are authoritative data.

  SECTION: [The AD and CD Bits in an Authoritative Response](#section-3.1.6)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: A security-aware name server SHOULD clear the CD bit when
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    composing an authoritative response.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A security-aware name server MUST NOT set the AD bit in a response
    TEXT[!MUST]:    unless the name server considers all RRsets in the Answer and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Authority sections of the response to be authentic.
    TEXT[!MAY]: A security-aware
    TEXT[!MAY]:    name server's local policy MAY consider data from an authoritative
    TEXT[!MAY]:    zone to be authentic without further validation.
    TEXT[!MUST]: However, the name
    TEXT[!MUST]:    server MUST NOT do so unless the name server obtained the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    authoritative zone via secure means (such as a secure zone transfer
    TEXT[!MUST]:    mechanism) and MUST NOT do so unless this behavior has been
    TEXT[!MUST]:    configured explicitly.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A security-aware name server that supports recursion MUST follow the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    rules for the CD and AD bits given in Section 3.2 when generating a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response that involves data obtained via recursion.

  SECTION: [The DO Bit](#section-3.2.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The resolver side of a security-aware recursive name server MUST set
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the DO bit when sending requests, regardless of the state of the DO
    TEXT[!MUST]:    bit in the initiating request received by the name server side.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the DO bit in an initiating query is not set, the name server side
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST strip any authenticating DNSSEC RRs from the response but MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NOT strip any DNSSEC RR types that the initiating query explicitly
    TEXT[!MUST]:    requested.

  SECTION: [The CD Bit](#section-3.2.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The name server side MUST copy the setting of the CD bit from a query
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to the corresponding response.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The name server side of a security-aware recursive name server MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    pass the state of the CD bit to the resolver side along with the rest
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    When the CD bit is set, the recursive name server SHOULD, if
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    possible, return the requested data to the originating resolver, even
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    if the recursive name server's local authentication policy would
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    reject the records in question.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the CD bit is set,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the name server side SHOULD return the data from the BAD cache; if
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the CD bit is not set, the name server side MUST return RCODE 2
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (server failure).

  SECTION: [The AD Bit](#section-3.2.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The name server side of a security-aware recursive name server MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NOT set the AD bit in a response unless the name server considers all
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRsets in the Answer and Authority sections of the response to be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    authentic.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The name server side SHOULD set the AD bit if and only if
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the resolver side considers all RRsets in the Answer section and any
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    relevant negative response RRs in the Authority section to be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    authentic.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The resolver side MUST follow the procedure described in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Section 5 to determine whether the RRs in question are authentic.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    However, for backward compatibility, a recursive name server MAY set
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the AD bit when a response includes unsigned CNAME RRs if those CNAME

  SECTION: [EDNS Support](#section-4.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A security-aware resolver MUST include an EDNS ([RFC2671]) OPT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    pseudo-RR with the DO ([RFC3225]) bit set when sending queries.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A security-aware resolver MUST support a message size of at least
    TEXT[!MUST]:    1220 octets, SHOULD support a message size of 4000 octets, and MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    use the "sender's UDP payload size" field in the EDNS OPT pseudo-RR
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to advertise the message size that it is willing to accept.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    security-aware resolver's IP layer MUST handle fragmented UDP packets
    TEXT[!MUST]:    correctly regardless of whether any such fragmented packets were
    TEXT[!MUST]:    received via IPv4 or IPv6.

  SECTION: [Signature Verification Support](#section-4.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A security-aware resolver MUST support the signature verification
    TEXT[!MUST]:    mechanisms described in Section 5 and SHOULD apply them to every
    TEXT[!MUST]:    received response, except when:
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A security-aware resolver's support for signature verification MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    include support for verification of wildcard owner names.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Security-aware resolvers MAY query for missing security RRs in an
    TEXT[!MAY]:    attempt to perform validation; implementations that choose to do so
    TEXT[!MAY]:    must be aware that the answers received may not be sufficient to
    TEXT[!MAY]:    validate the original response.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When attempting to retrieve missing NSEC RRs that reside on the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    parental side at a zone cut, a security-aware iterative-mode resolver
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST query the name servers for the parent zone, not the child zone.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When attempting to retrieve a missing DS, a security-aware
    TEXT[!MUST]:    iterative-mode resolver MUST query the name servers for the parent
    TEXT[!MUST]:    zone, not the child zone.

  SECTION: [Determining Security Status of Data](#section-4.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A security-aware resolver MUST be able to determine whether it should
    TEXT[!MUST]:    expect a particular RRset to be signed.

  SECTION: [Configured Trust Anchors](#section-4.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A security-aware resolver MUST be capable of being configured with at
    TEXT[!MUST]:    least one trusted public key or DS RR and SHOULD be capable of being
    TEXT[!MUST]:    configured with multiple trusted public keys or DS RRs.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Since a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    security-aware resolver will not be able to validate signatures
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    without such a configured trust anchor, the resolver SHOULD have some
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    reasonably robust mechanism for obtaining such keys when it boots;
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    examples of such a mechanism would be some form of non-volatile
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    storage (such as a disk drive) or some form of trusted local network
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    configuration mechanism.

  SECTION: [Response Caching](#section-4.5)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A security-aware resolver SHOULD cache each response as a single
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    atomic entry containing the entire answer, including the named RRset
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    and any associated DNSSEC RRs.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The resolver SHOULD discard the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    entire atomic entry when any of the RRs contained in it expire.

  SECTION: [Handling of the CD and AD Bits](#section-4.6)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    A security-aware resolver MAY set a query's CD bit in order to
    TEXT[!MAY]:    indicate that the resolver takes responsibility for performing
    TEXT[!MAY]:    whatever authentication its local policy requires on the RRsets in
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the response.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A security-aware resolver MUST clear the AD bit when composing query
    TEXT[!MUST]:    messages to protect against buggy name servers that blindly copy
    TEXT[!MUST]:    header bits that they do not understand from the query message to the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response message.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A resolver MUST disregard the meaning of the CD and AD bits in a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response unless the response was obtained by using a secure channel
    TEXT[!MUST]:    or the resolver was specifically configured to regard the message
    TEXT[!MUST]:    header bits without using a secure channel.

  SECTION: [Caching BAD Data](#section-4.7)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    To prevent such unnecessary DNS traffic, security-aware resolvers MAY
    TEXT[!MAY]:    cache data with invalid signatures, with some restrictions.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Resolvers that implement a BAD cache MUST take steps to prevent the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    cache from being useful as a denial-of-service attack amplifier,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    particularly the following:
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  Since RRsets that fail to validate do not have trustworthy TTLs,
    TEXT[!MUST]:       the implementation MUST assign a TTL.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: This TTL SHOULD be small,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       in order to mitigate the effect of caching the results of an
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       attack.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    o  In order to prevent caching of a transient validation failure
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       (which might be the result of an attack), resolvers SHOULD track
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       queries that result in validation failures and SHOULD only answer
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       from the BAD cache after the number of times that responses to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       queries for that particular <QNAME, QTYPE, QCLASS> have failed to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       validate exceeds a threshold value.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Resolvers MUST NOT return RRsets from the BAD cache unless the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    resolver is not required to validate the signatures of the RRsets in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    question under the rules given in Section 4.2 of this document.

  SECTION: [Synthesized CNAMEs](#section-4.8)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A validating security-aware resolver MUST treat the signature of a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    valid signed DNAME RR as also covering unsigned CNAME RRs that could
    TEXT[!MUST]:    have been synthesized from the DNAME RR, as described in [RFC2672],
    TEXT[!MUST]:    at least to the extent of not rejecting a response message solely
    TEXT[!MUST]:    because it contains such CNAME RRs.
    TEXT[!MAY]: The resolver MAY retain such
    TEXT[!MAY]:    CNAME RRs in its cache or in the answers it hands back, but is not
    TEXT[!MAY]:    required to do so.

  SECTION: [Stub Resolvers](#section-4.9)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A security-aware stub resolver MUST support the DNSSEC RR types, at
    TEXT[!MUST]:    least to the extent of not mishandling responses just because they
    TEXT[!MUST]:    contain DNSSEC RRs.

  SECTION: [Handling of the DO Bit](#section-4.9.1)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    A non-validating security-aware stub resolver MAY include the DNSSEC
    TEXT[!MAY]:    RRs returned by a security-aware recursive name server as part of the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    data that the stub resolver hands back to the application that
    TEXT[!MAY]:    invoked it, but is not required to do so.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A validating security-aware stub resolver MUST set the DO bit,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    because otherwise it will not receive the DNSSEC RRs it needs to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    perform signature validation.

  SECTION: [Handling of the CD Bit](#section-4.9.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A non-validating security-aware stub resolver SHOULD NOT set the CD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    bit when sending queries unless it is requested by the application
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    layer, as by definition, a non-validating stub resolver depends on
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the security-aware recursive name server to perform validation on its
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    behalf.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A validating security-aware stub resolver SHOULD set the CD bit,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    because otherwise the security-aware recursive name server will
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    answer the query using the name server's local policy, which may
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    prevent the stub resolver from receiving data that would be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    acceptable to the stub resolver's local policy.

  SECTION: [Handling of the AD Bit](#section-4.9.3)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    A non-validating security-aware stub resolver MAY chose to examine
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the setting of the AD bit in response messages that it receives in
    TEXT[!MAY]:    order to determine whether the security-aware recursive name server
    TEXT[!MAY]:    that sent the response claims to have cryptographically verified the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    data in the Answer and Authority sections of the response message.
    TEXT[!MUST]: In any case, a security-aware stub resolver MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NOT place any reliance on signature validation allegedly performed on
    TEXT[!MUST]:    its behalf, except when the security-aware stub resolver obtained the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    data in question from a trusted security-aware recursive name server
    TEXT[!MUST]:    via a secure channel.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A validating security-aware stub resolver SHOULD NOT examine the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    setting of the AD bit in response messages, as, by definition, the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    stub resolver performs its own signature validation regardless of the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    setting of the AD bit.

  SECTION: [Authenticating DNS Responses](#section-5)
    TEXT[!MUST]: To authenticate an apex DNSKEY RRset by using an initial key,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the resolver MUST:
    TEXT[!MUST]: The absence of DNSSEC data in a response MUST NOT by
    TEXT[!MUST]:    itself be taken as an indication that no authentication information
    TEXT[!MUST]:    exists.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A resolver SHOULD expect authentication information from signed
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    zones.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: A resolver SHOULD believe that a zone is signed if the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    resolver has been configured with public key information for the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    zone, or if the zone's parent is signed and the delegation from the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    parent contains a DS RRset.

  SECTION: [Special Considerations for Islands of Security](#section-5.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If a validator cannot
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    obtain such a key, it SHOULD switch to operating as if the zones in
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the island of security are unsigned.

  SECTION: [Authenticating Referrals](#section-5.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    security-aware resolver MUST query the name servers for the parent
    TEXT[!MUST]:    zone for the DS RRset if the referral includes neither a DS RRset nor
    TEXT[!MUST]:    a NSEC RRset proving that the DS RRset does not exist (see Section
    TEXT[!MUST]:    4).
    TEXT[!MAY]: If the resolver has an initial
    TEXT[!MAY]:    DNSKEY or DS RR that belongs to the child zone or to any delegation
    TEXT[!MAY]:    below the child zone, this initial DNSKEY or DS RR MAY be used to
    TEXT[!MAY]:    re-establish an authentication path.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A security-aware resolver MUST use the parent NSEC RR when attempting
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to prove that a DS RRset does not exist.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: In this case, the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    resolver SHOULD treat the child zone as if it were unsigned.

  SECTION: [Checking the RRSIG RR Validity](#section-5.3.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  The RRSIG RR and the RRset MUST have the same owner name and the
    TEXT[!MUST]:       same class.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  The RRSIG RR's Signer's Name field MUST be the name of the zone
    TEXT[!MUST]:       that contains the RRset.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  The RRSIG RR's Type Covered field MUST equal the RRset's type.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  The number of labels in the RRset owner name MUST be greater than
    TEXT[!MUST]:       or equal to the value in the RRSIG RR's Labels field.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  The validator's notion of the current time MUST be less than or
    TEXT[!MUST]:       equal to the time listed in the RRSIG RR's Expiration field.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  The validator's notion of the current time MUST be greater than or
    TEXT[!MUST]:       equal to the time listed in the RRSIG RR's Inception field.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  The RRSIG RR's Signer's Name, Algorithm, and Key Tag fields MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:       match the owner name, algorithm, and key tag for some DNSKEY RR in
    TEXT[!MUST]:       the zone's apex DNSKEY RRset.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  The matching DNSKEY RR MUST be present in the zone's apex DNSKEY
    TEXT[!MUST]:       RRset, and MUST have the Zone Flag bit (DNSKEY RDATA Flag bit 7)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       set.
    TEXT[!MUST]: In this case, the validator cannot predetermine which DNSKEY
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RR to use to authenticate the signature, and it MUST try each
    TEXT[!MUST]:    matching DNSKEY RR until either the signature is validated or the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    validator has run out of matching public keys to try.

  SECTION: [Reconstructing the Signed Data](#section-5.3.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:                if rrsig_labels > fqdn_labels
    TEXT[!MUST]:                   the RRSIG RR did not pass the necessary validation
    TEXT[!MUST]:                   checks and MUST NOT be used to authenticate this
    TEXT[!MUST]:                   RRset.
    TEXT[!MUST]: When reconstructing the original NSEC
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRset for the delegation from the parent zone, the NSEC RRs MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be combined with NSEC RRs from the child zone.
    TEXT[!MUST]: When reconstructing
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the original NSEC RRset for the apex of the child zone, the NSEC RRs
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST NOT be combined with NSEC RRs from the parent zone.

  SECTION: [Checking the Signature](#section-5.3.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The resolver
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST verify that wildcard expansion was applied properly before
    TEXT[!MUST]:    considering the RRset to be authentic.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the resolver accepts the RRset as authentic, the validator MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    set the TTL of the RRSIG RR and each RR in the authenticated RRset to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    a value no greater than the minimum of:

  SECTION: [Authenticated Denial of Existence](#section-5.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In addition, security-aware resolvers MUST authenticate the NSEC
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRsets that comprise the non-existence proof as described in Section
    TEXT[!MUST]:    5.3.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the complete set of necessary NSEC
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRsets is not present in a response (perhaps due to message
    TEXT[!MUST]:    truncation), then a security-aware resolver MUST resend the query in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    order to attempt to obtain the full collection of NSEC RRs necessary
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to verify the non-existence of the requested RRset.
    TEXT[!MUST]: As with all DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    operations, however, the resolver MUST bound the work it puts into
    TEXT[!MUST]:    answering any particular query.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Since a validated NSEC RR proves the existence of both itself and its
    TEXT[!MUST]:    corresponding RRSIG RR, a validator MUST ignore the settings of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NSEC and RRSIG bits in an NSEC RR.

  SECTION: [Resolver Behavior When Signatures Do Not Validate](#section-5.5)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If for whatever reason none of the RRSIGs can be validated, the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    response SHOULD be considered BAD.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the validation was being done
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to service a recursive query, the name server MUST return RCODE 2 to
