    TEXT[!MUST]:    the originating client.
    TEXT[!MUST]: However, it MUST return the full response if
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and only if the original query had the CD bit set.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc4255
  SECTION: [Method](#section-2.1)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Upon connection to an SSH server, the SSH client MAY look up the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    SSHFP resource record(s) for the host it is connecting to.
    TEXT[!MAY]: If the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    algorithm and fingerprint of the key received from the SSH server
    TEXT[!MAY]:    match the algorithm and fingerprint of one of the SSHFP resource
    TEXT[!MAY]:    record(s) returned from DNS, the client MAY accept the identity of
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the server.

  SECTION: [Implementation Notes](#section-2.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Client implementors SHOULD provide a configurable policy used to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    select the order of methods used to verify a host key.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In this scenario, the implementation SHOULD verify the host key
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    against a local database before verifying the key via the fingerprint
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    returned from DNS.

  SECTION: [Fingerprint Matching](#section-2.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       The public key algorithm and the SSHFP algorithm number MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:       match.
    TEXT[!MUST]:       A message digest of the public key, using the message digest
    TEXT[!MUST]:       algorithm specified in the SSHFP fingerprint type, MUST match the
    TEXT[!MUST]:       SSHFP fingerprint.

  SECTION: [Authentication](#section-2.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A public key verified using this method MUST NOT be trusted if the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    SSHFP resource record (RR) used for verification was not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    authenticated by a trusted SIG RR.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Clients that do validate the DNSSEC signatures themselves SHOULD use
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    standard DNSSEC validation procedures.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Clients that do not validate the DNSSEC signatures themselves MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    use a secure transport (e.g., TSIG [9], SIG(0) [10], or IPsec [8])
    TEXT[!MUST]:    between themselves and the entity performing the signature
    TEXT[!MUST]:    validation.

    TEXT[!MUST]:    to say, a lookup string octet with a value in the inclusive range

    TEXT[!MUST]:    identical value and also match the corresponding value in the

    TEXT[!MUST]:    lookup string octet with a lowercase ASCII letter value MUST

    TEXT[!MUST]:    While ASCII label comparisons are case insensitive, [STD13] says case

    TEXT[!MAY]: For example, if an "A"

    TEXT[!MUST]: However, the key MUST be transformed
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to the format it would have as the public key portion of a DNSKEY RR

    TEXT[!MUST]: If it is not, the algorithm field MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    zero and the tag field is meaningless and SHOULD be zero.

  SECTION: [Certificate Type Values](#section-2.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The data is binary and MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be encoded into an ASCII armor.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: An implementation SHOULD process

    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    MAY handle additional OpenPGP packets.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    These types MUST be used when the content is too large to fit in the

    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    owner names (or other names), pointing to the purpose-based owner
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    name.

  SECTION: [Performance Considerations](#section-4)
    TEXT[!MUST]: This means that each CERT RR MUST NOT contain
    TEXT[!MUST]:    more than 64kb of payload, even if the corresponding certificate or
    TEXT[!MUST]:    certificate revocation list is larger.

  SECTION: [Implementing the SHA-256 Algorithm for DS Record Support](#section-2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The
    TEXT[!MUST]:    results of the digest algorithm MUST NOT be truncated, and the entire
    TEXT[!MUST]:    32 byte digest result is to be published in the DS record.

  SECTION: [Implementation Requirements](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Implementations MUST support the use of the SHA-256 algorithm in DS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRs.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Validator implementations SHOULD ignore DS RRs containing SHA-1
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    digests if DS RRs with SHA-256 digests are present in the DS RRset.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc4697
  SECTION: [Recommendation](#section-2.1.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    An iterative resolver MUST NOT send a query for the NS RRSet of a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    non-responsive zone to any of the name servers for that zone's parent
    TEXT[!MUST]:    zone.

  SECTION: [Recommendation](#section-2.2.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Iterative resolvers SHOULD cache name servers that they discover are
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    not authoritative for zones delegated to them (i.e., lame servers).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If this caching is performed, lame servers MUST be cached against the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specific query tuple <zone name, class, server IP address>.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Implementations that perform lame server caching MUST refrain from
    TEXT[!MUST]:    sending queries to known lame servers for a configurable time
    TEXT[!MUST]:    interval after the server is discovered to be lame.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: A minimum
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    interval of thirty minutes is RECOMMENDED.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: In that case, the iterative resolver SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    temporarily ignore the servers' lameness status and query one or more
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    servers.

  SECTION: [Recommendation](#section-2.3.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Iterative resolvers SHOULD be able to handle
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    arbitrary levels of indirection resulting from out-of-zone name
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Iterative resolvers SHOULD implement a level-of-effort
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    counter to avoid loops or otherwise performing too much work in
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    resolving pathological cases.

  SECTION: [Recommendation](#section-2.4.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Implementers whose name servers support glue fetching SHOULD take
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    care to avoid sending queries at excessive rates.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Implementations
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD support throttling logic to detect when queries are sent but
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    no responses are received.

  SECTION: [Recommendation](#section-2.5.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The most obvious recommendation is that administrators SHOULD take
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    care not to place iterative resolvers behind a firewall that allows
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    queries, but not the resulting replies, to pass through.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Iterative resolvers SHOULD take care to avoid sending queries at
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    excessive rates.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Implementations SHOULD support throttling logic to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    detect when queries are sent but no responses are received.

  SECTION: [Recommendation](#section-2.6.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    An authoritative name server SHOULD issue a warning when one of a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    zone's NS records references a name server below the zone's apex when
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    a corresponding address record does not exist in the zone AND there
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    are no delegated subzones where the address record could exist.

  SECTION: [Recommendation](#section-2.7.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Because of the additional load placed on a zone's parent's
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    authoritative servers resulting from a zero TTL on a zone's NS RRSet,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    under such circumstances authoritative name servers SHOULD issue a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    warning when loading a zone.

  SECTION: [Recommendation](#section-2.8.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Dynamic update agents SHOULD send SOA or NS queries to progressively
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    higher-level names to find the closest enclosing zone for a given
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    name to update.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Update clients SHOULD NOT "probe" using UPDATE messages by
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    walking up the tree to progressively higher-level zones.

  SECTION: [Recommendation](#section-2.10.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Error reporting SHOULD be throttled to avoid a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    notification or log message for every response from a non-recursive
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    server.

  SECTION: [Recommendation](#section-2.11.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    o  Do not make assumptions based on NS RRSet order: all NS RRs SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       be treated equally.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: An
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       iterative resolver SHOULD periodically check the performance of
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       all of a zone's name servers to adjust its determination of the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       best-performing one.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5001
  SECTION: [Resolver Behavior](#section-2.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The resolver MUST NOT include any NSID payload data in the query
    TEXT[!MUST]:    message.

  SECTION: [Name Server Behavior](#section-2.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The name server MUST ignore any NSID payload data that might be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    present in the query message.
    TEXT[!MUST]: A name server MUST NOT send an
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NSID option back to a resolver which did not request it.

  SECTION: [Presentation Format](#section-2.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    User interfaces MUST read and write the contents of the NSID option
    TEXT[!MUST]:    as a sequence of hexadecimal digits, two digits per payload octet.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Any comparison between NSID
    TEXT[!MUST]:    payloads MUST be a comparison of the raw binary data.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Copy
    TEXT[!MUST]:    operations MUST NOT assume that the raw NSID payload is null-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    terminated.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5011
  SECTION: [Revocation](#section-2.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: Once the resolver sees the REVOKE bit, it MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NOT use this key as a trust anchor or for any other purpose except to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    validate the RRSIG it signed over the DNSKEY RRSet specifically for
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the purpose of validating the revocation.

  SECTION: [Add Hold-Down](#section-2.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The resolver MUST NOT treat the new key as a trust anchor
    TEXT[!MUST]:    until the hold-down time expires AND it has retrieved and validated a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNSKEY RRSet after the hold-down time that contains the new key.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    N.B.: Once the resolver has accepted a key as a trust anchor, the key
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST be considered a valid trust anchor by that resolver until
    TEXT[!MUST]:    explicitly revoked as described above.

  SECTION: [Active Refresh](#section-2.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A resolver that has been configured for an automatic update of keys
    TEXT[!MUST]:    from a particular trust point MUST query that trust point (e.g., do a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    lookup for the DNSKEY RRSet and related RRSIG records) no less often
    TEXT[!MUST]:    than the lesser of 15 days, half the original TTL for the DNSKEY
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRSet, or half the RRSIG expiration interval and no more often than
    TEXT[!MUST]:    once per hour.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the query fails, the resolver MUST repeat the query until
    TEXT[!MUST]:    satisfied no more often than once an hour and no less often than the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    lesser of 1 day, 10% of the original TTL, or 10% of the original
    TEXT[!MUST]:    expiration interval.

  SECTION: [Add Hold-Down Time](#section-2.4.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: This ensures that at least two
    TEXT[!MUST]:    validated DNSKEY RRSets that contain the new key MUST be seen by the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    resolver prior to the key's acceptance.

  SECTION: [Minimum Trust Anchors per Trust Point](#section-2.4.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A compliant resolver MUST be able to manage at least five SEP keys
    TEXT[!MUST]:    per trust point.

  SECTION: [Changes to DNSKEY RDATA Wire Format](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If this bit is set to '1', AND the resolver sees an RRSIG(DNSKEY)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    signed by the associated key, then the resolver MUST consider this
    TEXT[!MUST]:    key permanently invalid for all purposes except for validating the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    revocation.

  SECTION: [States](#section-4.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the RRSet is seen and is validated (i.e.,
    TEXT[!MUST]:             verifies against an existing trust anchor), this key MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:             in the RRSet, otherwise a 'KeyRem' event is triggered.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Once in
    TEXT[!MUST]:             this state, this key MUST permanently be considered invalid
    TEXT[!MUST]:             as a trust anchor.
    TEXT[!MUST]: A key in the removed
    TEXT[!MUST]:             state MUST NOT be considered a valid trust anchor.

  SECTION: [Trust Point Deletion](#section-5)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Alternately, a trust point that is subordinate to another configured
    TEXT[!MAY]:    trust point MAY be deleted by a resolver after 180 days, where such a

  SECTION: [Key Ownership vs. Acceptance Policy](#section-8.1)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    The resolver owner (and resolver implementers) MAY choose to permit
    TEXT[!MAY]:    or prevent key status updates based on this mechanism for specific
    TEXT[!MAY]:    trust points.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5155
  SECTION: [Backwards Compatibility](#section-2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Zones signed according to this specification MUST only use these
    TEXT[!MUST]:    algorithm identifiers for their DNSKEY RRs.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Security aware resolvers that are aware of this specification MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    recognize the new algorithm identifiers and treat them as equivalent
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to the algorithms that they alias.

  SECTION: [The NSEC3 Resource Record](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The class MUST be the same as the class of the original owner name.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The NSEC3 RR SHOULD have the same TTL value as the SOA minimum TTL
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    field.

  SECTION: [Type Bit Maps Encoding](#section-3.2.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Since bit 0 in window block 0 refers to the non-existing RR type 0,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    it MUST be set to 0.
    TEXT[!MUST]: After verification, the validator MUST ignore
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the value of bit 0 in window block 0.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Bits representing Meta-TYPEs or QTYPEs as specified in Section 3.1 of
    TEXT[!MUST]:    [RFC2929] or within the range reserved for assignment only to QTYPEs
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and Meta-TYPEs MUST be set to 0, since they do not appear in zone
    TEXT[!MUST]:    data.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Blocks with no types present MUST NOT be included.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Trailing zero
    TEXT[!MUST]:    octets in the bitmap MUST be omitted.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Trailing octets not specified
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST be interpreted as zero octets.

  SECTION: [Presentation Format](#section-3.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: When the mnemonic is not known, the TYPE
    TEXT[!MUST]:       representation as described in Section 5 of [RFC3597] MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:       used.

  SECTION: [The NSEC3PARAM Resource Record](#section-4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If an NSEC3PARAM RR is present at the apex of a zone with a Flags
    TEXT[!MUST]:    field value of zero, then there MUST be an NSEC3 RR using the same
    TEXT[!MUST]:    hash algorithm, iterations, and salt parameters present at every
    TEXT[!MUST]:    hashed owner name in the zone.
    TEXT[!MUST]: That is, the zone MUST contain a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    complete set of NSEC3 RRs with the same hash algorithm, iterations,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and salt parameters.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The class MUST be the same as the NSEC3 RRs to which this RR refers.

  SECTION: [Flag Fields](#section-4.1.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NSEC3PARAM RRs with a Flags field value other than zero MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    ignored.

  SECTION: [Opt-Out](#section-6)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    An Opt-Out NSEC3 RR MAY have the same original owner name as an
    TEXT[!MAY]:    insecure delegation.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Zones using Opt-Out MAY contain a mixture of Opt-Out NSEC3 RRs and
    TEXT[!MAY]:    non-Opt-Out NSEC3 RRs.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If an NSEC3 RR is not Opt-Out, there MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be any hashed owner names of insecure delegations (nor any other RRs)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    between it and the name indicated by the next hashed owner name in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the NSEC3 RDATA.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If it is Opt-Out, it MUST only cover hashed owner
    TEXT[!MUST]:    names or hashed "next closer" names of insecure delegations.

  SECTION: [Zone Signing](#section-7.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  Each owner name within the zone that owns authoritative RRSets
    TEXT[!MUST]:       MUST have a corresponding NSEC3 RR.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Owner names that correspond
    TEXT[!MAY]:       to unsigned delegations MAY have a corresponding NSEC3 RR.
    TEXT[!MUST]:       However, if there is not a corresponding NSEC3 RR, there MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:       an Opt-Out NSEC3 RR that covers the "next closer" name to the
    TEXT[!MUST]:       delegation.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  Each empty non-terminal MUST have a corresponding NSEC3 RR, unless
    TEXT[!MUST]:       the empty non-terminal is only derived from an insecure delegation
    TEXT[!MUST]:       covered by an Opt-Out NSEC3 RR.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    o  The TTL value for any NSEC3 RR SHOULD be the same as the minimum
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       TTL value field in the zone SOA RR.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  The Type Bit Maps field of every NSEC3 RR in a signed zone MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:       indicate the presence of all types present at the original owner
    TEXT[!MUST]:       name, except for the types solely contributed by an NSEC3 RR
    TEXT[!MUST]:       itself.
    TEXT[!MAY]:        *  If Opt-Out is being used, owner names of unsigned delegations
    TEXT[!MAY]:           MAY be excluded.

  SECTION: [Zone Serving](#section-7.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When returning responses containing multiple NSEC3 RRs, all of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NSEC3 RRs MUST use the same hash algorithm, iteration, and salt
    TEXT[!MUST]:    values.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The Flags field value MUST be either zero or one.

  SECTION: [Name Error Responses](#section-7.2.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    To prove the nonexistence of QNAME, a closest encloser proof and an
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NSEC3 RR covering the (nonexistent) wildcard RR at the closest
    TEXT[!MUST]:    encloser MUST be included in the response.

  SECTION: [No Data Responses, QTYPE is not DS](#section-7.2.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The server MUST include the NSEC3 RR that matches QNAME.
    TEXT[!MUST]: This NSEC3
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RR MUST NOT have the bits corresponding to either the QTYPE or CNAME
    TEXT[!MUST]:    set in its Type Bit Maps field.

  SECTION: [No Data Responses, QTYPE is DS](#section-7.2.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If there is an NSEC3 RR that matches QNAME, the server MUST return it
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in the response.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The bits corresponding with DS and CNAME MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be set in the Type Bit Maps field of this NSEC3 RR.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If no NSEC3 RR matches QNAME, the server MUST return a closest
    TEXT[!MUST]:    provable encloser proof for QNAME.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The NSEC3 RR that covers the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    "next closer" name MUST have the Opt-Out bit set (note that this is
    TEXT[!MUST]:    true by definition -- if the Opt-Out bit is not set, something has
    TEXT[!MUST]:    gone wrong).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If a server is authoritative for both sides of a zone cut at QNAME,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the server MUST return the proof from the parent side of the zone
    TEXT[!MUST]:    cut.

  SECTION: [Wildcard No Data Responses](#section-7.2.5)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If there is a wildcard match for QNAME, but QTYPE is not present at
    TEXT[!MUST]:    that name, the response MUST include a closest encloser proof for
    TEXT[!MUST]:    QNAME and MUST include the NSEC3 RR that matches the wildcard.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Note that the closest
    TEXT[!MUST]:    encloser to QNAME MUST be the immediate ancestor of the wildcard RR
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (if this is not the case, then something has gone wrong).

  SECTION: [Wildcard Answer Responses](#section-7.2.6)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    To this end, the NSEC3 RR that covers the "next closer" name of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    immediate ancestor of the wildcard MUST be returned.

  SECTION: [Referrals to Unsigned Subzones](#section-7.2.7)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If there is an NSEC3 RR that matches the delegation name, then that
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NSEC3 RR MUST be included in the response.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The DS bit in the type
    TEXT[!MUST]:    bit maps of the NSEC3 RR MUST NOT be set.
    TEXT[!MUST]: In this case, the closest provable
    TEXT[!MUST]:    encloser proof MUST be included in the response.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The included NSEC3
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RR that covers the "next closer" name for the delegation MUST have
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the Opt-Out flag set to one.

  SECTION: [Responding to Queries for NSEC3 Owner Names](#section-7.2.8)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    then the response MUST be constructed as a Name Error response
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (Section 7.2.2).

  SECTION: [Server Response to a Run-Time Collision](#section-7.2.9)
    TEXT[!MUST]: In this case, the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    server MUST return a response with an RCODE of 2 (server failure).

  SECTION: [Zones Using Unknown Hash Algorithms](#section-7.4)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Such zones SHOULD be rejected when loading.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Servers SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    respond with RCODE=2 (server failure) responses when handling queries
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    that would fall under such zones.

  SECTION: [Dynamic Update](#section-7.5)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Adding and removing names in a zone MUST account for the creation or
    TEXT[!MUST]:    removal of empty non-terminals.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  When removing a name with a corresponding NSEC3 RR, any NSEC3 RRs
    TEXT[!MUST]:       corresponding to empty non-terminals created by that name MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:       removed.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  When adding a name that requires adding an NSEC3 RR, NSEC3 RRs
    TEXT[!MUST]:       MUST also be added for any empty non-terminals that are created.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    o  When adding a delegation RRSet, if the "next closer" name of the
    TEXT[!MAY]:       delegation is covered by an existing Opt-Out NSEC3 RR, then the
    TEXT[!MAY]:       delegation MAY be added without modifying the NSEC3 RRs in the
    TEXT[!MAY]:       zone.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Servers SHOULD follow this set of
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    basic rules to resolve the ambiguity.

  SECTION: [Responses with Unknown Hash Types](#section-8.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A validator MUST ignore NSEC3 RRs with unknown hash types.

  SECTION: [Verifying NSEC3 RRs](#section-8.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A validator MUST ignore NSEC3 RRs with a Flag fields value other than
    TEXT[!MUST]:    zero or one.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    A validator MAY treat a response as bogus if the response contains
    TEXT[!MAY]:    NSEC3 RRs that contain different values for hash algorithm,
    TEXT[!MAY]:    iterations, or salt from each other for that zone.

  SECTION: [Closest Encloser Proof](#section-8.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In order to verify a closest encloser proof, the validator MUST find
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the longest name, X, such that
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Once the closest encloser has been discovered, the validator MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    check that the NSEC3 RR that has the closest encloser as the original
    TEXT[!MUST]:    owner name is from the proper zone.

  SECTION: [Validating Name Error Responses](#section-8.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A validator MUST verify that there is a closest encloser proof for
    TEXT[!MUST]:    QNAME present in the response and that there is an NSEC3 RR that
    TEXT[!MUST]:    covers the wildcard at the closest encloser (i.e., the name formed by
    TEXT[!MUST]:    prepending the asterisk label to the closest encloser).

  SECTION: [Validating No Data Responses, QTYPE is not DS](#section-8.5)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The validator MUST verify that an NSEC3 RR that matches QNAME is
    TEXT[!MUST]:    present and that both the QTYPE and the CNAME type are not set in its
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Type Bit Maps field.

  SECTION: [Validating No Data Responses, QTYPE is DS](#section-8.6)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If there is an NSEC3 RR that matches QNAME present in the response,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    then that NSEC3 RR MUST NOT have the bits corresponding to DS and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    CNAME set in its Type Bit Maps field.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If there is no such NSEC3 RR, then the validator MUST verify that a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    closest provable encloser proof for QNAME is present in the response,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and that the NSEC3 RR that covers the "next closer" name has the Opt-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Out bit set.

  SECTION: [Validating Wildcard No Data Responses](#section-8.7)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The validator MUST verify a closest encloser proof for QNAME and MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    find an NSEC3 RR present in the response that matches the wildcard
    TEXT[!MUST]:    name generated by prepending the asterisk label to the closest
    TEXT[!MUST]:    encloser.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Furthermore, the bits corresponding to both QTYPE and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    CNAME MUST NOT be set in the wildcard matching NSEC3 RR.

  SECTION: [Validating Wildcard Answer Responses](#section-8.8)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Validators MUST verify that there is an NSEC3 RR that covers the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    "next closer" name to QNAME present in the response.

  SECTION: [Validating Referrals to Unsigned Subzones](#section-8.9)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If there is an NSEC3 RR present in the response that matches the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    delegation name, then the validator MUST ensure that the NS bit is
    TEXT[!MUST]:    set and that the DS bit is not set in the Type Bit Maps field of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NSEC3 RR.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The validator MUST also ensure that the NSEC3 RR is from
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the correct (i.e., parent) zone.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If there is no NSEC3 RR present that matches the delegation name,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    then the validator MUST verify a closest provable encloser proof for
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the delegation name.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The validator MUST verify that the Opt-Out bit
    TEXT[!MUST]:    is set in the NSEC3 RR that covers the "next closer" name to the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    delegation name.

  SECTION: [NSEC3 Resource Record Caching](#section-9.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Caching resolvers MUST be able to retrieve the appropriate NSEC3 RRs
    TEXT[!MUST]:    when returning responses that contain them.

  SECTION: [Use of the AD Bit](#section-9.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The AD bit, as defined by [RFC4035], MUST NOT be set when returning a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response containing a closest (provable) encloser proof in which the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NSEC3 RR that covers the "next closer" name has the Opt-Out bit set.

  SECTION: [DNAME at the Zone Apex](#section-10.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: If a DNAME RR is present at node N, there
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST be no data at any descendant of N.

  SECTION: [Iterations](#section-10.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A zone owner MUST NOT use a value higher than shown in the table
    TEXT[!MUST]:    below for iterations for the given key size.
    TEXT[!MAY]: A resolver MAY treat a
    TEXT[!MAY]:    response with a higher value as insecure, after the validator has
    TEXT[!MAY]:    verified that the signature over the NSEC3 RR is correct.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Therefore the values in the table MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    used independent of the key algorithm.

  SECTION: [Transitioning a Signed Zone from NSEC to NSEC3](#section-10.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]: However, the end result MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:        that all DS RRs in the parent use the specified algorithm
    TEXT[!MUST]:        aliases.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If adding incrementally, then the last RRSet added MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:        the NSEC3PARAM RRSet.

  SECTION: [IANA Considerations](#section-11)
    TEXT[!MUST]: When
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specifying a new hash algorithm for use with NSEC3, a transition
    TEXT[!MUST]:    mechanism MUST also be defined.

  SECTION: [Dictionary Attacks](#section-12.1.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The salt SHOULD be at least 64 bits long and unpredictable, so that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    an attacker cannot anticipate the value of the salt and compute the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    next set of dictionaries before the zone is published.

  SECTION: [Transitioning to a New Hash Algorithm](#section-12.1.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: When
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specifying a new hash algorithm for use with NSEC3, a transition
    TEXT[!MUST]:    mechanism MUST also be defined.

  SECTION: [Opt-Out Considerations](#section-12.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Therefore, it is strongly RECOMMENDED that Opt-Out be used sparingly.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In particular, zone signing tools SHOULD NOT default to using Opt-
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Out, and MAY choose to not support Opt-Out at all.

  SECTION: [Salting](#appendix-C.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    There MUST be at least one complete set of NSEC3 RRs for the zone
    TEXT[!MUST]:    using the same salt value.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The salt SHOULD be changed periodically to prevent pre-computation
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    using a single salt.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: It is RECOMMENDED that the salt be changed for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    every re-signing.
    TEXT[!MUST]: However, in order for authoritative servers to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be able to consistently find covering NSEC3 RRs, the authoritative
    TEXT[!MUST]:    server MUST choose a single set of parameters (algorithm, salt, and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    iterations) to use when selecting NSEC3 RRs.

  SECTION: [Avoiding Hash Collisions During Generation](#appendix-C.2.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In the (academic) case of a collision occurring, an alternative salt
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST be chosen and all hash values MUST be regenerated.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5452
  SECTION: [Query Matching Rules](#section-9.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A resolver implementation MUST match responses to all of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    following attributes of the query:
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A mismatch and the response MUST be considered invalid.

  SECTION: [Extending the Q-ID Space by Using Ports and Addresses](#section-9.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Resolver implementations MUST:
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Resolvers that have multiple IP addresses SHOULD use them in an
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    unpredictable manner for outgoing queries.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Resolver implementations SHOULD provide means to avoid usage of
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    certain ports.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Resolvers SHOULD favor authoritative nameservers with which a trust
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    relation has been established; stub-resolvers SHOULD be able to use
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Transaction Signature (TSIG) ([RFC2845]) or IPsec ([RFC4301]) when
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    communicating with their recursive resolver.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    In case a cryptographic verification of response validity is
    TEXT[!MAY]:    available (TSIG, SIG(0)), resolver implementations MAY waive above
    TEXT[!MAY]:    rules, and rely on this guarantee instead.

  SECTION: [Spoof Detection and Countermeasure](#section-9.3)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    If a resolver detects that an attempt is being made to spoof it,
    TEXT[!MAY]:    perhaps by discovering that many packets fail the criteria as
    TEXT[!MAY]:    outlined above, it MAY abandon the UDP query and re-issue it over
    TEXT[!MAY]:    TCP.

  SECTION: [Security Considerations](#section-10)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Nothing in this document specifies specific algorithms for operators
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to use; it does specify algorithms implementations SHOULD or MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    support.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5702
  SECTION: [RSA/SHA-256 DNSKEY Resource Records](#section-2.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    For interoperability, as in [RFC3110], the key size of RSA/SHA-256
    TEXT[!MUST]:    keys MUST NOT be less than 512 bits and MUST NOT be more than 4096
    TEXT[!MUST]:    bits.

  SECTION: [RSA/SHA-512 DNSKEY Resource Records](#section-2.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The key size of RSA/SHA-512 keys MUST NOT be less than 1024 bits and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST NOT be more than 4096 bits.

  SECTION: [RRSIG Resource Records](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The FF octet MUST be repeated the exact number of times
    TEXT[!MUST]:    so that the total length of the concatenated term in parentheses
    TEXT[!MUST]:    equals the length of the modulus of the signer's public key ("n").

  SECTION: [Support for SHA-2 Signatures](#section-5.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DNSSEC-aware implementations SHOULD be able to support RRSIG and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DNSKEY resource records created with the RSA/SHA-2 algorithms as
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    defined in this document.

  SECTION: [Support for NSEC3 Denial of Existence](#section-5.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A DNSSEC validator that implements RSA/SHA-2 MUST be able to validate
    TEXT[!MUST]:    negative answers in the form of both NSEC and NSEC3 with hash
    TEXT[!MUST]:    algorithm 1, as defined in [RFC5155].
    TEXT[!MAY]: An authoritative server that
    TEXT[!MAY]:    does not implement NSEC3 MAY still serve zones that use RSA/SHA-2
    TEXT[!MAY]:    with NSEC denial of existence.

  SECTION: [Signature Type Downgrade Attacks](#section-8.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Since each RRSet MUST be signed with each algorithm present in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNSKEY RRSet at the zone apex (see Section 2.2 of [RFC4035]), a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    malicious party cannot filter out the RSA/SHA-2 RRSIG and force the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    validator to use the RSA/SHA-1 signature if both are present in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    zone.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5936
  SECTION: [Header Values](#section-2.1.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       QR          MUST be 0 (Query)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       OPCODE      MUST be 0 (Standard Query)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       RCODE       MUST be 0 (No error)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       QDCOUNT     Number of entries in Question section;   MUST be 1
    TEXT[!MUST]:       ANCOUNT     Number of entries in Answer section;     MUST be 0
    TEXT[!MUST]:       NSCOUNT     Number of entries in Authority section;  MUST be 0
    TEXT[!MUST]:       A server MUST reply using messages that use the same message ID to
    TEXT[!MUST]:       allow a client to have multiple queries outstanding concurrently
    TEXT[!MUST]:       over the same TCP connection -- see Note a) in Section 2.2.1 for
    TEXT[!MUST]:       more details.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: For the client, it is RECOMMENDED that the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       value be zero.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The server MUST ignore this value.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    c) "mbz" -- The client MUST set this bit to 0; the server MUST ignore
    TEXT[!MUST]:       it.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    d) The client MUST set this field to the number of resource records
    TEXT[!MUST]:       it places into the Additional section.
    TEXT[!MAY]: In the absence of explicit
    TEXT[!MAY]:       specification of new RRs to be carried in the Additional section
    TEXT[!MAY]:       of AXFR queries, the value MAY be 0, 1, or 2.

  SECTION: [Question Section](#section-2.1.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Question section of the AXFR query MUST conform to Section 4.1.2
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of RFC 1035, and contain a single resource record with the following
    TEXT[!MUST]:    values:

  SECTION: [Answer Section](#section-2.1.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Answer section MUST be empty.

  SECTION: [Authority Section](#section-2.1.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Authority section MUST be empty.

  SECTION: [Additional Section](#section-2.1.5)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    The client MAY include one OPT resource record [RFC2671].
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    server does not support EDNS0, the client MUST send this section
    TEXT[!MUST]:    without an OPT resource record if there is a retry.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    The client MAY include one transaction integrity and authentication
    TEXT[!MAY]:    resource record, currently a choice of TSIG [RFC2845] or SIG(0)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    [RFC2931].
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In general, if an AXFR client is aware that an AXFR server does not
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    support a particular mechanism, the client SHOULD NOT attempt to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    engage the server using the mechanism (or engage the server at all).
    TEXT[!MAY]:    The range of permissible resource records that MAY appear in the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Additional section might change over time.

  SECTION: [AXFR Response](#section-2.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: In such a series, the first message MUST begin with the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    SOA resource record of the zone, and the last message MUST conclude
    TEXT[!MUST]:    with the same SOA resource record.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Intermediate messages MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    contain the SOA resource record.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The AXFR server MUST copy the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Question section from the corresponding AXFR query message into the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    first response message's Question section.
    TEXT[!MAY]: For subsequent messages,
    TEXT[!MAY]:    it MAY do the same or leave the Question section empty.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Although
    TEXT[!MUST]:    servers typically do attempt to send related RRs (such as the RRs
    TEXT[!MUST]:    forming an RRset, and the RRsets of a name) as a contiguous group or,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    when message space allows, in the same response message, they are not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    required to do so, and clients MUST accept any ordering and grouping
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of the non-SOA RRs.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Each RR SHOULD be transmitted only once, and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    AXFR clients MUST ignore any duplicate RRs received.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Each AXFR response message SHOULD contain a sufficient number of RRs
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    to reasonably amortize the per-message overhead, up to the largest
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    number that will fit within a DNS message (taking the required
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    content of the other sections into account, as described below).
    TEXT[!MAY]: To interoperate with such clients, the server MAY
    TEXT[!MAY]:    restrict response messages to a single RR.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Such a message terminates the AXFR session; it MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    contain a copy of the Question section from the AXFR query in its
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Question section, but the inclusion of the terminating SOA resource
    TEXT[!MUST]:    record is not necessary.

  SECTION: [Header Values](#section-2.2.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       ID          MUST be copied from request -- see Note a)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       QR          MUST be 1 (Response)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       OPCODE      MUST be 0 (Standard Query)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       Flags:
    TEXT[!MUST]:          AA       normally 1 -- see Note b)
    TEXT[!MUST]:          TC       MUST be 0 (Not truncated)
    TEXT[!MUST]:          RD       RECOMMENDED: copy request's value; MAY be set to 0
    TEXT[!MUST]:          RA       SHOULD be 0 -- see Note c)
    TEXT[!MUST]:          Z        "mbz" -- see Note d)
    TEXT[!MUST]:          AD       "mbz" -- see Note d)
    TEXT[!MUST]:          CD       "mbz" -- see Note d)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       QDCOUNT     MUST be 1 in the first message;
    TEXT[!MUST]:                   MUST be 0 or 1 in all following messages;
    TEXT[!MUST]:                   MUST be 1 if RCODE indicates an error
    TEXT[!MUST]:       NSCOUNT     MUST be 0
    TEXT[!MUST]: New
    TEXT[!MUST]:       DNS servers MUST set this field to the value of the AXFR query ID
    TEXT[!MUST]:       in each AXFR response message for the session.
    TEXT[!MUST]: AXFR clients MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:       be able to manage sessions resulting from the issuance of multiple
    TEXT[!MUST]:       outstanding queries, whether AXFR queries or other DNS queries.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       client SHOULD discard responses that do not correspond (via the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       message ID) to any outstanding queries.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       Unless the client is sure that the server will consistently set
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       the ID field to the query's ID, the client is NOT RECOMMENDED to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       issue any other queries until the end of the zone transfer.
    TEXT[!MAY]:       client MAY become aware of a server's abilities via a
    TEXT[!MAY]:       configuration setting.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    b) If the RCODE is 0 (no error), then the AA bit MUST be 1.
    TEXT[!MUST]: For any
    TEXT[!MUST]:       other value of RCODE, the AA bit MUST be set according to the
    TEXT[!MUST]:       rules for that error code.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If in doubt, it is RECOMMENDED that it
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       be set to 1.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: It is RECOMMENDED that the value be ignored by the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       AXFR client.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    c) It is RECOMMENDED that the server set the value to 0; the client
    TEXT[!MUST]:       MUST ignore this value.
    TEXT[!MAY]:       The server MAY set this value according to the local policy
    TEXT[!MAY]:       regarding recursive service, but doing so might confuse the
    TEXT[!MAY]:       interpretation of the response, as AXFR cannot be retrieved
    TEXT[!MAY]:       recursively.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: A client MAY note the server's policy regarding
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       recursive service from this value, but SHOULD NOT conclude that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       the AXFR response was obtained recursively, even if the RD bit was
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       1 in the query.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    d) "mbz" -- The server MUST set this bit to 0; the client MUST ignore
    TEXT[!MUST]:       it.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    e) In the absence of an error, the server MUST set the value of this
    TEXT[!MUST]:       field to NoError(0).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If a server is not authoritative for the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       queried zone, the server SHOULD set the value to NotAuth(9).
    TEXT[!MUST]:       (Reminder: Consult the appropriate IANA registry [DNSVALS].)  If a
    TEXT[!MUST]:       client receives any other value in response, it MUST act according
    TEXT[!MUST]:       to the error.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    f) The count of answer records MUST equal the number of resource
    TEXT[!MUST]:       records in the AXFR Answer section.
    TEXT[!MUST]: When a server is aware that a
    TEXT[!MUST]:       client will only accept response messages with a single resource
    TEXT[!MUST]:       record, then the value MUST be 1.
    TEXT[!MAY]: A server MAY be made aware of a
    TEXT[!MAY]:       client's limitations via configuration data.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    g) The server MUST set this field to the number of resource records
    TEXT[!MUST]:       it places into the Additional section.
    TEXT[!MAY]: In the absence of explicit
    TEXT[!MAY]:       specification of new RRs to be carried in the Additional section
    TEXT[!MAY]:       of AXFR response messages, the value MAY be 0, 1, or 2.

  SECTION: [Question Section](#section-2.2.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In the first response message, this section MUST be copied from the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    query.
    TEXT[!MAY]: In subsequent messages, this section MAY be copied from the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    query, or it MAY be empty.
    TEXT[!MUST]: However, in an error response message
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (see Section 2.2), this section MUST be copied as well.
    TEXT[!MAY]: The content
    TEXT[!MAY]:    of this section MAY be used to determine the context of the message,
    TEXT[!MAY]:    that is, the name of the zone being transferred.

  SECTION: [Answer Section](#section-2.2.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Answer section MUST be populated with the zone contents.

  SECTION: [Authority Section](#section-2.2.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Authority section MUST be empty.

  SECTION: [Additional Section](#section-2.2.5)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The contents of this section MUST follow the guidelines for the OPT,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    TSIG, and SIG(0) RRs, or whatever other future record is possible
    TEXT[!MUST]:    here.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If the client has supplied an EDNS OPT RR in the AXFR query and if
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the server supports EDNS as well, it SHOULD include one OPT RR in the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    first response message and MAY do so in subsequent response messages
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    (see Section 2.2); the specifications of EDNS options to be carried
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    in the OPT RR may impose stronger requirements.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the client has supplied a transaction security resource record
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (currently a choice of TSIG and SIG(0)) and the server supports the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    method chosen by the client, it MUST place the corresponding resource
    TEXT[!MUST]:    record into the AXFR response message(s), according to the rules
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specified for that method.

  SECTION: [TCP Connection Aborts](#section-2.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If an AXFR client sends a query on a TCP connection and the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    connection is closed at any point, the AXFR client MUST consider the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    AXFR session terminated.
    TEXT[!MAY]: The message ID MAY be used again on a new
    TEXT[!MAY]:    connection, even if the question and AXFR server are the same.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Facing a dropped connection, a client SHOULD try to make some
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    determination as to whether the connection closure was the result of
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    network activity or due to a decision by the AXFR server.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: It is up to the AXFR client
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    to react, but the implemented reaction SHOULD NOT be either an
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    endless cycle of retries or an increasing (in frequency) retry rate.

  SECTION: [Records to Include](#section-3.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In the Answer section of AXFR response messages, the resource records
    TEXT[!MUST]:    within a zone for the given serial number MUST appear.

  SECTION: [Delegation Records](#section-3.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The AXFR response MUST contain the cut point NS resource record set
    TEXT[!MUST]:    registered with the zone whether it agrees with the authoritative set
    TEXT[!MUST]:    or not.

  SECTION: [Glue Records](#section-3.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The AXFR response MUST contain the appropriate glue records as
    TEXT[!MUST]:    registered with the zone.

  SECTION: [Name Compression](#section-3.4)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Hence, name compression in an AXFR message SHOULD be performed in a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    case-preserving manner, unlike how it is done for "normal" DNS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    responses.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Rules governing name compression of RDATA in an AXFR message MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    abide by the specification in "Handling of Unknown DNS Resource
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Record (RR) Types" [RFC3597], specifically, Section 4 on "Domain Name
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Compression".

  SECTION: [Occluded Names](#section-3.5)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Occluded names MUST be included in AXFR responses.
    TEXT[!MUST]: An AXFR client
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST be able to identify and handle occluded names.

  SECTION: [AXFR Client TCP](#section-4.1.1)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    An AXFR client MAY request a connection to an AXFR server for any
    TEXT[!MAY]:    reason.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: An AXFR client SHOULD close the connection when there is no
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    apparent need to use the connection for some time period.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When a TCP connection is closed remotely (relative to the client),
    TEXT[!MUST]:    whether by the AXFR server or due to a network event, the AXFR client
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST cancel all outstanding sessions and non-AXFR transactions.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    An AXFR client MAY use an already opened TCP connection to start an
    TEXT[!MAY]:    AXFR session.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Using an existing open connection is RECOMMENDED over
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    opening a new connection.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: (Non-AXFR session traffic can also use an
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    open connection.)  If in doing so the AXFR client realizes that the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    responses cannot be properly differentiated (lack of matching query
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    IDs, for example) or the connection is terminated for a remote
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    reason, then the AXFR client SHOULD NOT attempt to reuse an open
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    connection with the specific AXFR server until the AXFR server is
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    updated (which is, of course, not an event captured in the DNS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    protocol).

  SECTION: [AXFR Server TCP](#section-4.1.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    An AXFR server MUST be able to handle multiple AXFR sessions on a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    single TCP connection, as well as to handle other query/response
    TEXT[!MUST]:    transactions over it.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If a TCP connection is closed remotely, the AXFR server MUST cancel
    TEXT[!MUST]:    all AXFR sessions in place.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Local policy MAY dictate that a TCP connection is to be closed.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Such
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    an action SHOULD be in reaction to limits such as those placed on the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    number of outstanding open connections.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Closing a connection in
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    response to a suspected security event SHOULD be done only in extreme
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    cases, when the server is certain the action is warranted.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: An
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    isolated request for a zone not on the AXFR server SHOULD receive a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    response with the appropriate response code and not see the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    connection broken.

  SECTION: [Authorization](#section-5)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A DNS implementation SHOULD provide means to restrict AXFR sessions
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    to specific clients.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    An implementation SHOULD allow access to be granted to Internet
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Protocol addresses and ranges, regardless of whether a source address
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    could be spoofed.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A general-purpose implementation is RECOMMENDED to implement access
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    controls based upon "Secret Key Transaction Authentication for DNS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    (TSIG)" [RFC2845] and/or "DNS Request and Transaction Signatures
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    ( SIG(0)s )" [RFC2931].
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A general-purpose implementation SHOULD allow access to be open to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    all AXFR requests.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A general-purpose implementation SHOULD NOT have a default policy for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    AXFR requests to be "open to all".

  SECTION: [Zone Integrity](#section-6)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    An AXFR client MUST ensure that only a successfully transferred copy
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of the zone data can be used to serve this zone.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Previous
    TEXT[!MUST]:    description and implementation practice has introduced a two-stage
    TEXT[!MUST]:    model of the whole zone synchronization procedure:  Upon a trigger
    TEXT[!MUST]:    event (e.g., when polling of a SOA resource record detects a change
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in the SOA serial number, or when a DNS NOTIFY request [RFC1996] is
    TEXT[!MUST]:    received), the AXFR session is initiated, whereby the zone data are
    TEXT[!MUST]:    saved in a zone file or database (this latter step is necessary
    TEXT[!MUST]:    anyway to ensure proper restart of the server); upon successful
    TEXT[!MUST]:    completion of the AXFR operation and some sanity checks, this data
    TEXT[!MUST]:    set is "loaded" and made available for serving the zone in an atomic
    TEXT[!MUST]:    operation, and flagged "valid" for use during the next restart of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNS server; if any error is detected, this data set MUST be deleted,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and the AXFR client MUST continue to serve the previous version of
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the zone, if it did before.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The externally visible behavior of an
    TEXT[!MUST]:    AXFR client implementation MUST be equivalent to that of this two-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    stage model.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If an AXFR client rejects data obtained in an AXFR session, it SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    remember the serial number and MAY attempt to retrieve the same zone
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    version again.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Besides best attempts at securing TCP connections, DNS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    implementations SHOULD provide means to make use of "Secret Key
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Transaction Authentication for DNS (TSIG)" [RFC2845] and/or "DNS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Request and Transaction Signatures ( SIG(0)s )" [RFC2931] to allow
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    AXFR clients to verify the contents.
    TEXT[!MAY]: These techniques MAY also be
    TEXT[!MAY]:    used for authorization.

  SECTION: [Backwards Compatibility](#section-7)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: An
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    implementation SHOULD, in its documentation, encourage operators to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    periodically review AXFR clients and servers it has made notes about
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    repeatedly, as old software gets updated from time to time.

  SECTION: [Server](#section-7.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    An implementation of an AXFR server MAY permit configuring, on a per
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    AXFR client basis, the necessity to revert to a single resource
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    record per message; in that case, the default SHOULD be to use
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    multiple records per message.

  SECTION: [Client](#section-7.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Attempting to issue multiple DNS queries over a TCP transport for an
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    AXFR session SHOULD be aborted if it interrupts the original request,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    and SHOULD take into consideration whether the AXFR server intends to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    close the connection immediately upon completion of the original
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    (connection-causing) zone transfer.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6604
  SECTION: [RCODE Clarification](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The RCODE in the ultimate DNS response
    TEXT[!MUST]:       MUST BE set based on the final query cycle leading to that
    TEXT[!MUST]:       response.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6605
  SECTION: [DNSKEY and RRSIG Resource Records for ECDSA](#section-4)
    TEXT[!MUST]: (Conversion of
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the integers to bit strings is described in Section C.2 of FIPS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    186-3.)  For P-256, each integer MUST be encoded as 32 octets; for
    TEXT[!MUST]:    P-384, each integer MUST be encoded as 48 octets.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Conformant implementations that create records to be put into the DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST implement signing and verification for both of the above
    TEXT[!MUST]:    algorithms.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Conformant DNSSEC verifiers MUST implement verification
    TEXT[!MUST]:    for both of the above algorithms.

  SECTION: [Support for NSEC3 Denial of Existence](#section-5)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A DNSSEC validator that implements the signing algorithms defined in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    this document MUST be able to validate negative answers in the form
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of both NSEC and NSEC3 with hash algorithm 1, as defined in RFC 5155.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    An authoritative server that does not implement NSEC3 MAY still serve
    TEXT[!MAY]:    zones that use the signing algorithms defined in this document with
    TEXT[!MAY]:    NSEC denial of existence.

  SECTION: [IANA Considerations](#section-7)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Value          4
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Digest Type    SHA-384
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Status         OPTIONAL

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6672
  SECTION: [Format](#section-2.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Its RDATA is comprised of a single field, <target>, which contains a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    fully qualified domain name that MUST be sent in uncompressed form
    TEXT[!MUST]:    [RFC1035] [RFC3597].
    TEXT[!MUST]: The <target> field MUST be present.

  SECTION: [DNAME Owner Name Matching the QNAME](#section-2.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNAME RRs MUST NOT appear at the same owner name as an NS RR unless
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the owner name is the zone apex; if it is not the zone apex, then the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NS RR signifies a delegation point, and the DNAME RR must in that
    TEXT[!MUST]:    case appear below the zone cut at the zone apex of the child zone.

  SECTION: [Names next to and below a DNAME Record](#section-2.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Resource records MUST NOT exist at any subdomain of the owner of a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNAME RR.
    TEXT[!MAY]: A server MAY refuse to load a zone that has data at a
    TEXT[!MAY]:    subdomain of a domain name owning a DNAME RR.

  SECTION: [Compression of the DNAME Record](#section-2.5)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The DNAME RDATA target name MUST NOT be sent out in compressed form
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and MUST be downcased for DNS Security Extensions (DNSSEC)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    validation.

  SECTION: [CNAME Synthesis](#section-3.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Servers MUST be able to answer a query for a synthesized CNAME.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    server in question is a cache, the synthesized CNAME's TTL SHOULD be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    equal to the decremented TTL of the cached DNAME.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Resolvers MUST be able to handle a synthesized CNAME TTL of zero or a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    value equal to the TTL of the corresponding DNAME record (as some
    TEXT[!MUST]:    older, authoritative server implementations set the TTL of
    TEXT[!MUST]:    synthesized CNAMEs to zero).

  SECTION: [Server Algorithm](#section-3.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The server MUST

  SECTION: [Wildcards](#section-3.3)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Thus, records of the form "*.example.com DNAME
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    example.net" SHOULD NOT be used.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    A server MAY give a warning that the behavior is unspecified if such
    TEXT[!MAY]:    a wildcarded DNAME is loaded.
    TEXT[!MAY]: The server MAY refuse it, refuse to
    TEXT[!MAY]:    load the zone, or refuse dynamic updates.

  SECTION: [Acceptance and Intermediate Storage](#section-3.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Recursive caching name servers MUST perform CNAME synthesis on behalf
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of clients.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If a recursive caching name server encounters a DNSSEC validated
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DNAME RR that contradicts information already in the cache (excluding
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    CNAME records), it SHOULD cache the DNAME RR, but it MAY cache the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    CNAME record received along with it, subject to the rules for CNAME.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If the DNAME RR cannot be validated via DNSSEC (i.e., not BOGUS, but
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    not able to validate), the recursive caching server SHOULD NOT cache
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the DNAME RR but MAY cache the CNAME record received along with it,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    subject to the rules for CNAME.

  SECTION: [Dynamic Update and DNAME](#section-5.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If a dynamic update message attempts to add a DNAME with a given
    TEXT[!MUST]:    owner name, but a CNAME is associated with that name, then the server
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST ignore the DNAME.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    associated with that name, then the CNAME MUST be ignored.

  SECTION: [DNAME Bit in NSEC Type Map](#section-5.3.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In any negative response, the NSEC or NSEC3 [RFC5155] record type
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    bitmap SHOULD be checked to see that there was no DNAME that could
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    have been applied.

  SECTION: [Validators Must Understand DNAME](#section-5.3.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Below are examples of why DNSSEC validators MUST understand DNAME.

  SECTION: [Security Considerations](#section-8)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A validating resolver MUST understand DNAME, according to [RFC4034].

  SECTION: [Changes to Server Behavior](#appendix-A.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  Recursive caching servers MUST perform CNAME synthesis on behalf
    TEXT[!MUST]:       of clients (Section 3.4).

  SECTION: [Changes to Client Behavior](#appendix-A.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  Clients MUST be able to accept synthesized CNAME RR's with a TTL
    TEXT[!MUST]:       of either zero or the TTL of the DNAME RR that accompanies the
    TEXT[!MUST]:       CNAME RR.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    o  DNSSEC-aware clients SHOULD cache DNAME RRs and MAY cache
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       synthesized CNAME RRs they receive in the same response.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: DNSSEC-
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       aware clients SHOULD also check the NSEC/NSEC3 type bitmap to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       verify that DNAME redirection is to be done.
    TEXT[!MUST]: DNSSEC validators
    TEXT[!MUST]:       MUST understand DNAME (Section 5.3).

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6698
  SECTION: [The Certificate Usage Field](#section-2.1.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       0 -- Certificate usage 0 is used to specify a CA certificate, or
    TEXT[!MUST]:       the public key of such a certificate, that MUST be found in any of
    TEXT[!MUST]:       the PKIX certification paths for the end entity certificate given
    TEXT[!MUST]:       by the server in TLS.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The
    TEXT[!MUST]:       presented certificate MUST pass PKIX certification path
    TEXT[!MUST]:       validation, and a CA certificate that matches the TLSA record MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:       be included as part of a valid certification path.
    TEXT[!MUST]:       1 -- Certificate usage 1 is used to specify an end entity
    TEXT[!MUST]:       certificate, or the public key of such a certificate, that MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:       matched with the end entity certificate given by the server in
    TEXT[!MUST]:       TLS.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The target
    TEXT[!MUST]:       certificate MUST pass PKIX certification path validation and MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:       match the TLSA record.
    TEXT[!MUST]:       2 -- Certificate usage 2 is used to specify a certificate, or the
    TEXT[!MUST]:       public key of such a certificate, that MUST be used as the trust
    TEXT[!MUST]:       anchor when validating the end entity certificate given by the
    TEXT[!MUST]:       server in TLS.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The target
    TEXT[!MUST]:       certificate MUST pass PKIX certification path validation, with any
    TEXT[!MUST]:       certificate matching the TLSA record considered to be a trust
    TEXT[!MUST]:       anchor for this certification path validation.
    TEXT[!MUST]:       3 -- Certificate usage 3 is used to specify a certificate, or the
    TEXT[!MUST]:       public key of such a certificate, that MUST match the end entity
    TEXT[!MUST]:       certificate given by the server in TLS.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The target certificate
    TEXT[!MUST]:       MUST match the TLSA record.

  SECTION: [TLSA RR Presentation Format](#section-2.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  The certificate usage field MUST be represented as an 8-bit
    TEXT[!MUST]:       unsigned integer.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  The selector field MUST be represented as an 8-bit unsigned
    TEXT[!MUST]:       integer.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  The matching type field MUST be represented as an 8-bit unsigned
    TEXT[!MUST]:       integer.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  The certificate association data field MUST be represented as a
    TEXT[!MUST]:       string of hexadecimal characters.

  SECTION: [Domain Names for TLSA Certificate Associations](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The base domain name is the
    TEXT[!MUST]:        fully qualified DNS domain name [RFC1035] of the TLS server, with
    TEXT[!MUST]:        the additional restriction that every label MUST meet the rules
    TEXT[!MUST]:        of [RFC0952].
    TEXT[!MUST]: The latter restriction means that, if the query is
    TEXT[!MUST]:        for an internationalized domain name, it MUST use the A-label
    TEXT[!MUST]:        form as defined in [RFC5890].

  SECTION: [Use of TLSA Records in TLS](#section-4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The TLS session that is to be set up MUST be for the specific port
    TEXT[!MUST]:    number and transport name that was given in the TLSA query.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If a TLSA record has certificate usage 2, the corresponding TLS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    server SHOULD send the certificate that is referenced just like it
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    currently sends intermediate certificates.

  SECTION: [Usable Certificate Associations](#section-4.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Determining whether a TLSA RRSet can be used MUST be based on the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNSSEC validation state (as defined in [RFC4033]).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  A TLSA RRSet whose DNSSEC validation state is secure MUST be used
    TEXT[!MUST]:       as a certificate association for TLS unless a local policy would
    TEXT[!MUST]:       prohibit the use of the specific certificate association in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:       secure TLSA RRSet.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  If the DNSSEC validation state on the response to the request for
    TEXT[!MUST]:       the TLSA RRSet is bogus, this MUST cause TLS not to be started or,
    TEXT[!MUST]:       if the TLS negotiation is already in progress, MUST cause the
    TEXT[!MUST]:       connection to be aborted.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  A TLSA RRSet whose DNSSEC validation state is indeterminate or
    TEXT[!MUST]:       insecure cannot be used for TLS and MUST be considered unusable.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Clients that validate the DNSSEC signatures themselves MUST use
    TEXT[!MUST]:    standard DNSSEC validation procedures.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Clients that rely on another
    TEXT[!MUST]:    entity to perform the DNSSEC signature validation MUST use a secure
    TEXT[!MUST]:    mechanism between themselves and the validator.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If a certificate association contains a certificate usage, selector,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    or matching type that is not understood by the TLS client, that
    TEXT[!MUST]:    certificate association MUST be considered unusable.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    comparison data for a certificate is malformed, the certificate
    TEXT[!MUST]:    association MUST be considered unusable.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If a certificate association contains a matching type or certificate
    TEXT[!MUST]:    association data that uses a cryptographic algorithm that is
    TEXT[!MUST]:    considered too weak for the TLS client's policy, the certificate
    TEXT[!MUST]:    association MUST be considered unusable.
    TEXT[!MUST]: During the TLS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    handshake, if none of the certificate associations matches the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    certificate given by the TLS server, the TLS client MUST abort the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    handshake.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If a request for a TLSA record
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    does not meet one of those two criteria but the application continues
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    with the TLS handshake anyway, the application has gotten no benefit
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    from TLSA and SHOULD NOT make any internal or external indication
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    that TLSA was applied.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If an application has a configuration setting
    TEXT[!MUST]:    that has turned on TLSA use, or has any indication that TLSA is in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    use (regardless of whether or not this is configurable), that
    TEXT[!MUST]:    application either MUST NOT start a TLS connection or it MUST abort a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    TLS handshake if both of the two criteria above are not met.

  SECTION: [Mandatory-to-Implement Features](#section-6)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    TLS clients conforming to this specification MUST be able to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    correctly interpret TLSA records with certificate usages 0, 1, 2,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and 3.
    TEXT[!MUST]: TLS clients conforming to this specification MUST be able to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    compare a certificate association with a certificate from the TLS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    handshake using selector types 0 and 1, and matching type 0 (no hash
    TEXT[!MUST]:    used) and matching type 1 (SHA-256), and SHOULD be able to make such
    TEXT[!MUST]:    comparisons with matching type 2 (SHA-512).

  SECTION: [DNS Caching](#section-8.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In particular, implementations SHOULD rely on their DNS resolver for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    confirmation of an association between a TLSA record and a DNS name,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    rather than caching the result of previous domain name lookups.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Many
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    platforms already can cache domain name lookups locally when
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    appropriate, and they SHOULD be configured to do so.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If implementations cache the results of domain name lookups in order
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to achieve a performance improvement, they MUST observe the TTL
    TEXT[!MUST]:    information reported by DNS.

  SECTION: [Creating TLSA Records](#appendix-A.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: Section 4 of this document states that a TLSA
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRSet whose validation state is secure MUST be used.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6761
  SECTION: [Procedure](#section-4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If it is determined that special handling of a name is required in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    order to implement some desired new functionality, then an IETF
    TEXT[!MUST]:    "Standards Action" or "IESG Approval" specification [RFC5226] MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    published describing the new functionality.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The specification MUST state how implementations determine that the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    special handling is required for any given name.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The specification also MUST state, in each of the seven "Domain Name
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Reservation Considerations" categories below, what special treatment,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    if any, is to be applied.

  SECTION: [Domain Name Reservation Considerations for Private Addresses](#section-6.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: However, since there is no central
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        authority responsible for use of private addresses, users SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        be aware that these names are likely to yield different results
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        on different networks.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Application software SHOULD NOT recognize these names as special,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        and SHOULD use these names as they would other reverse-mapping
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        names.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Name resolution APIs and libraries SHOULD NOT recognize these
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        names as special and SHOULD NOT treat them differently.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Name
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        resolution APIs SHOULD send queries for these names to their
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        configured caching DNS server(s).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Caching DNS servers SHOULD recognize these names as special and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        SHOULD NOT, by default, attempt to look up NS records for them,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        or otherwise query authoritative DNS servers in an attempt to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        resolve these names.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Instead, caching DNS servers SHOULD, by
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        default, generate immediate (positive or negative) responses for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        all such queries.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Caching DNS servers SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        offer a configuration option (disabled by default) to enable
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        upstream resolution of such names, for use in private networks
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        where private-address reverse-mapping names are known to be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        handled by an authoritative DNS server in said private network.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Authoritative DNS servers SHOULD recognize these names as special
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        and SHOULD, by default, generate immediate negative responses for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        all such queries, unless explicitly configured by the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        administrator to give positive answers for private-address
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        reverse-mapping names.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: DNS server operators SHOULD, if they are using private addresses,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        configure their authoritative DNS servers to act as authoritative
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        for these names.
    TEXT[!MUST]: DNS Registries/Registrars MUST NOT grant requests to register any
    TEXT[!MUST]:        of these names in the normal way to any person or entity.

  SECTION: [Domain Name Reservation Considerations for "test."](#section-6.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: However, since there is no central authority
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        responsible for use of test names, users SHOULD be aware that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        these names are likely to yield different results on different
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        networks.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Application software SHOULD NOT recognize test names as special,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        and SHOULD use test names as they would other domain names.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Name resolution APIs and libraries SHOULD NOT recognize test
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        names as special and SHOULD NOT treat them differently.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Name
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        resolution APIs SHOULD send queries for test names to their
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        configured caching DNS server(s).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Caching DNS servers SHOULD recognize test names as special and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        SHOULD NOT, by default, attempt to look up NS records for them,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        or otherwise query authoritative DNS servers in an attempt to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        resolve test names.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Instead, caching DNS servers SHOULD, by
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        default, generate immediate negative responses for all such
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        queries.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Caching DNS servers SHOULD offer
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        a configuration option (disabled by default) to enable upstream
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        resolving of test names, for use in networks where test names are
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        known to be handled by an authoritative DNS server in said
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        private network.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Authoritative DNS servers SHOULD recognize test names as special
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        and SHOULD, by default, generate immediate negative responses for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        all such queries, unless explicitly configured by the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        administrator to give positive answers for test names.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: DNS server operators SHOULD, if they are using test names,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        configure their authoritative DNS servers to act as authoritative
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        for test names.
    TEXT[!MUST]: DNS Registries/Registrars MUST NOT grant requests to register
    TEXT[!MUST]:        test names in the normal way to any person or entity.

  SECTION: [Domain Name Reservation Considerations for "localhost."](#section-6.3)
    TEXT[!MAY]: Application software MAY recognize localhost names as special, or
    TEXT[!MAY]:        MAY pass them to name resolution APIs as they would for other
    TEXT[!MAY]:        domain names.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Name resolution APIs and libraries SHOULD recognize localhost
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        names as special and SHOULD always return the IP loopback address
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        for address queries and negative responses for all other query
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        types.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Name resolution APIs SHOULD NOT send queries for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        localhost names to their configured caching DNS server(s).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Caching DNS servers SHOULD recognize localhost names as special
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        and SHOULD NOT attempt to look up NS records for them, or
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        otherwise query authoritative DNS servers in an attempt to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        resolve localhost names.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Instead, caching DNS servers SHOULD,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        for all such address queries, generate an immediate positive
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        response giving the IP loopback address, and for all other query
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        types, generate an immediate negative response.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Authoritative DNS servers SHOULD recognize localhost names as
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        special and handle them as described above for caching DNS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        servers.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: DNS server operators SHOULD be aware that the effective RDATA for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        localhost names is defined by protocol specification and cannot
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        be modified by local configuration.
    TEXT[!MUST]: DNS Registries/Registrars MUST NOT grant requests to register
    TEXT[!MUST]:        localhost names in the normal way to any person or entity.

  SECTION: [Domain Name Reservation Considerations for "invalid."](#section-6.4)
    TEXT[!MAY]: Users MAY assume that queries for "invalid" names
    TEXT[!MAY]:        will always return NXDOMAIN responses.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Application software MAY recognize "invalid" names as special or
    TEXT[!MAY]:        MAY pass them to name resolution APIs as they would for other
    TEXT[!MAY]:        domain names.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Name resolution APIs and libraries SHOULD recognize "invalid"
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        names as special and SHOULD always return immediate negative
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        responses.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Name resolution APIs SHOULD NOT send queries for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        "invalid" names to their configured caching DNS server(s).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Caching DNS servers SHOULD recognize "invalid" names as special
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        and SHOULD NOT attempt to look up NS records for them, or
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        otherwise query authoritative DNS servers in an attempt to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        resolve "invalid" names.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Instead, caching DNS servers SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        generate immediate NXDOMAIN responses for all such queries.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Authoritative DNS servers SHOULD recognize "invalid" names as
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        special and handle them as described above for caching DNS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        servers.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: DNS server operators SHOULD be aware that the effective RDATA for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        "invalid" names is defined by protocol specification to be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        nonexistent and cannot be modified by local configuration.
    TEXT[!MUST]: DNS Registries/Registrars MUST NOT grant requests to register
    TEXT[!MUST]:        "invalid" names in the normal way to any person or entity.

  SECTION: [Domain Name Reservation Considerations for Example Domains](#section-6.5)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Users SHOULD understand that example names are reserved for use
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        in documentation.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Application software SHOULD NOT recognize example names as
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        special and SHOULD use example names as they would other domain
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        names.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Name resolution APIs and libraries SHOULD NOT recognize example
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        names as special and SHOULD NOT treat them differently.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Name
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        resolution APIs SHOULD send queries for example names to their
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        configured caching DNS server(s).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Caching DNS servers SHOULD NOT recognize example names as special
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        and SHOULD resolve them normally.
