    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Authoritative DNS servers SHOULD NOT recognize example names as
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        special.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: DNS server operators SHOULD be aware that example names are
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        reserved for use in documentation.
    TEXT[!MUST]: DNS Registries/Registrars MUST NOT grant requests to register
    TEXT[!MUST]:        example names in the normal way to any person or entity.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6762
  SECTION: [Conventions and Terminology Used in This Document](#section-2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: Before claiming ownership of a unique
    TEXT[!MUST]:       resource record set, a responder MUST probe to verify that no
    TEXT[!MUST]:       other responder already claims ownership of that set, as described
    TEXT[!MUST]:       in Section 8.1, "Probing".
    TEXT[!MUST]: (For fault-tolerance and other
    TEXT[!MUST]:       reasons, sometimes it is permissible to have more than one
    TEXT[!MUST]:       responder answering for a particular "unique" resource record set,
    TEXT[!MUST]:       but such cooperating responders MUST give answers containing
    TEXT[!MUST]:       identical rdata for these records.

  SECTION: [Multicast DNS Names](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: If this happens, the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    computer (or its human user) MUST cease using the name, and SHOULD
    TEXT[!MUST]:    attempt to allocate a new unique name for use on that link.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Any DNS query for a name ending with ".local." MUST be sent to the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    mDNS IPv4 link-local multicast address 224.0.0.251 (or its IPv6
    TEXT[!MUST]:    equivalent FF02::FB).
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Implementers MAY choose to look up such names concurrently via other
    TEXT[!MAY]:    mechanisms (e.g., Unicast DNS) and coalesce the results in some
    TEXT[!MAY]:    fashion.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    DNS queries for names that do not end with ".local." MAY be sent to
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the mDNS multicast address, if no other conventional DNS server is
    TEXT[!MAY]:    available.

  SECTION: [Reverse Address Mapping](#section-4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       Any DNS query for a name ending with "254.169.in-addr.arpa." MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:       be sent to the mDNS IPv4 link-local multicast address 224.0.0.251
    TEXT[!MUST]:       or the mDNS IPv6 multicast address FF02::FB.
    TEXT[!MUST]:       Likewise, any DNS query for a name within the reverse mapping
    TEXT[!MUST]:       domains for IPv6 link-local addresses ("8.e.f.ip6.arpa.",
    TEXT[!MUST]:       "9.e.f.ip6.arpa.", "a.e.f.ip6.arpa.", and "b.e.f.ip6.arpa.") MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:       be sent to the mDNS IPv6 link-local multicast address FF02::FB or
    TEXT[!MUST]:       the mDNS IPv4 link-local multicast address 224.0.0.251.

  SECTION: [Querying](#section-5)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Except in the rare case of a Multicast DNS responder that is
    TEXT[!MUST]:    advertising only shared resource records and no unique records, a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Multicast DNS responder MUST also implement a Multicast DNS querier
    TEXT[!MUST]:    so that it can first verify the uniqueness of those records before it
    TEXT[!MUST]:    begins answering queries for them.

  SECTION: [One-Shot Multicast DNS Queries](#section-5.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: These queries are typically
    TEXT[!MUST]:    done using a high-numbered ephemeral UDP source port, but regardless
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of whether they are sent from a dynamic port or from a fixed port,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    these queries MUST NOT be sent using UDP source port 5353, since
    TEXT[!MUST]:    using UDP source port 5353 signals the presence of a fully compliant
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Multicast DNS querier, as described below.

  SECTION: [Continuous Multicast DNS Querying](#section-5.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Therefore, when retransmitting Multicast DNS queries to implement
    TEXT[!MUST]:    this kind of continuous monitoring, the interval between the first
    TEXT[!MUST]:    two queries MUST be at least one second, the intervals between
    TEXT[!MUST]:    successive queries MUST increase by at least a factor of two, and the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    querier MUST implement Known-Answer Suppression, as described below
    TEXT[!MAY]:    When the interval between queries reaches or exceeds 60 minutes, a
    TEXT[!MAY]:    querier MAY cap the interval to a maximum of 60 minutes, and perform
    TEXT[!MAY]:    subsequent queries at a steady-state rate of one query per hour.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: To
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    avoid accidental synchronization when, for some reason, multiple
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    clients begin querying at exactly the same moment (e.g., because of
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    some common external trigger event), a Multicast DNS querier SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    also delay the first query of the series by a randomly chosen amount
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    in the range 20-120 ms.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    After this interval has passed, the answer will no longer be valid
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    and SHOULD be deleted from the cache.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Before the record expiry time
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    is reached, a Multicast DNS querier that has local clients with an
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    active interest in the state of that record (e.g., a network browsing
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    window displaying a list of discovered services to the user) SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    reissue its query to determine whether the record is still valid.
    TEXT[!MUST]: A Multicast DNS querier MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    perform this cache maintenance for records for which it has no local
    TEXT[!MUST]:    clients with an active interest.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    An additional efficiency optimization SHOULD be performed when a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Multicast DNS response is received containing a unique answer (as
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    indicated by the cache-flush bit being set, described in Section
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    10.2, "Announcements to Flush Outdated Cache Entries").
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: In this case, the Multicast DNS querier SHOULD plan to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    issue its next query for this record at 80-82% of the record's TTL,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    as described above.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A compliant Multicast DNS querier, which implements the rules
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specified in this document, MUST send its Multicast DNS queries from
    TEXT[!MUST]:    UDP source port 5353 (the well-known port assigned to mDNS), and MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    listen for Multicast DNS replies sent to UDP destination port 5353 at
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the mDNS link-local multicast address (224.0.0.251 and/or its IPv6
    TEXT[!MUST]:    equivalent FF02::FB).

  SECTION: [Questions Requesting Unicast Responses](#section-5.4)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Multicast DNS querier sending its initial batch of questions
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    immediately on wake from sleep or interface activation SHOULD set the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    unicast-response bit in those questions.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    When a question is retransmitted (as described in Section 5.2), the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    unicast-response bit SHOULD NOT be set in subsequent retransmissions
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    of that question.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Subsequent retransmissions SHOULD be usual "QM"
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    questions.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: In addition, the unicast-response bit SHOULD be set
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    only for questions that are active and ready to be sent the moment of
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    wake from sleep or interface activation.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: New questions created by
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    local clients afterwards should be treated as normal "QM" questions
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    and SHOULD NOT have the unicast-response bit set on the first
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    question of the series.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    When receiving a question with the unicast-response bit set, a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    responder SHOULD usually respond with a unicast packet directed back
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    to the querier.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: However, if the responder has not multicast that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    record recently (within one quarter of its TTL), then the responder
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD instead multicast the response so as to keep all the peer
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    caches up to date, and to permit passive conflict detection.

  SECTION: [Direct Unicast Queries to Port 5353](#section-5.5)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: When a Multicast DNS responder receives a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    query via direct unicast, it SHOULD respond as it would for "QU"
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    questions, as described above in Section 5.4.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Since it is possible
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    for a unicast query to be received from a machine outside the local
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    link, responders SHOULD check that the source address in the query
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    packet matches the local subnet for that link (or, in the case of
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    IPv6, the source address has an on-link prefix) and silently ignore
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the packet if not.

  SECTION: [Responding](#section-6)
    TEXT[!MUST]: A Multicast DNS responder MUST NOT place
    TEXT[!MUST]:    records from its cache, which have been learned from other responders
    TEXT[!MUST]:    on the network, in the Resource Record Sections of outgoing response
    TEXT[!MUST]:    messages.
    TEXT[!MUST]: As with Unicast DNS, generally only DNS class 1 ("Internet")
    TEXT[!MUST]:    is used, but should client software use classes other than 1, the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    matching rules described above MUST be used.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A Multicast DNS responder MUST only respond when it has a positive,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    non-null response to send, or it authoritatively knows that a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    particular record does not exist.
    TEXT[!MUST]: For unique records, where the host
    TEXT[!MUST]:    has already established sole ownership of the name, it MUST return
    TEXT[!MUST]:    negative answers to queries for records that it knows not to exist.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    For example, a host with no IPv6 address, that has claimed sole
    TEXT[!MUST]:    ownership of the name "host.local." for all rrtypes, MUST respond to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    AAAA queries for "host.local." by sending a negative answer
    TEXT[!MUST]:    indicating that no AAAA records exist for that name.
    TEXT[!MUST]: For shared records, NXDOMAIN and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    other error responses MUST NOT be sent.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Multicast DNS responses MUST NOT contain any questions in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Question Section.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Any questions in the Question Section of a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    received Multicast DNS response MUST be silently ignored.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A Multicast DNS responder on Ethernet [IEEE.802.3] and similar shared
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    multiple access networks SHOULD have the capability of delaying its
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    responses by up to 500 ms, as described below.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In the case where a Multicast DNS responder has good reason to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    believe that it will be the only responder on the link that will send
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    a response (i.e., because it is able to answer every question in the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    query message, and for all of those answer records it has previously
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    verified that the name, rrtype, and rrclass are unique on the link),
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    it SHOULD NOT impose any random delay before responding, and SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    normally generate its response within at most 10 ms.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In any case where there may be multiple responses, such as queries
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    where the answer is a member of a shared resource record set, each
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    responder SHOULD delay its response by a random amount of time
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    selected with uniform random distribution in the range 20-120 ms.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In the case where the query has the TC (truncated) bit set,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    indicating that subsequent Known-Answer packets will follow,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    responders SHOULD delay their responses by a random amount of time
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    selected with uniform random distribution in the range 400-500 ms, to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    allow enough time for all the Known-Answer packets to arrive, as
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    described in Section 7.2, "Multipacket Known-Answer Suppression".
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The source UDP port in all Multicast DNS responses MUST be 5353 (the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    well-known port assigned to mDNS).
    TEXT[!MUST]: Multicast DNS implementations
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST silently ignore any Multicast DNS responses they receive where
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the source UDP port is not 5353.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The destination UDP port in all Multicast DNS responses MUST be 5353,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and the destination address MUST be the mDNS IPv4 link-local
    TEXT[!MUST]:    multicast address 224.0.0.251 or its IPv6 equivalent FF02::FB, except
    TEXT[!MUST]:    when generating a reply to a query that explicitly requested a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    unicast response:
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Except for these three specific cases, responses MUST NOT be sent via
    TEXT[!MUST]:    unicast, because then the "Passive Observation of Failures"
    TEXT[!MUST]:    mechanisms described in Section 10.5 would not work correctly.
    TEXT[!MUST]: A Multicast DNS querier MUST only accept unicast responses if
    TEXT[!MUST]:    they answer a recently sent query (e.g., sent within the last two
    TEXT[!MUST]:    seconds) that explicitly requested unicast responses.
    TEXT[!MUST]: A Multicast
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNS querier MUST silently ignore all other unicast responses.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    To protect the network against excessive packet flooding due to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    software bugs or malicious attack, a Multicast DNS responder MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (except in the one special case of answering probe queries) multicast
    TEXT[!MUST]:    a record on a given interface until at least one second has elapsed
    TEXT[!MUST]:    since the last time that record was multicast on that particular
    TEXT[!MUST]:    interface.
    TEXT[!MUST]: In the special case of answering
    TEXT[!MUST]:    probe queries, because of the limited time before the probing host
    TEXT[!MUST]:    will make its decision about whether or not to use the name, a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Multicast DNS responder MUST respond quickly.

  SECTION: [Negative Responses](#section-6.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Any time a responder receives a query for a name for which it has
    TEXT[!MUST]:    verified exclusive ownership, for a type for which that name has no
    TEXT[!MUST]:    records, the responder MUST (except as allowed in (a) below) respond
    TEXT[!MUST]:    asserting the nonexistence of that record using a DNS NSEC record
    TEXT[!MUST]:    [RFC4034].
    TEXT[!MAY]:    On receipt of a question for a particular name, rrtype, and rrclass,
    TEXT[!MAY]:    for which a responder does have one or more unique answers, the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    responder MAY also include an NSEC record in the Additional Record
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Section indicating the nonexistence of other rrtypes for that name
    TEXT[!MAY]:    and rrclass.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Implementers working with devices with sufficient memory and CPU
    TEXT[!MAY]:    resources MAY choose to implement code to handle the full generality
    TEXT[!MAY]:    of the DNS NSEC record [RFC4034], including bitmaps up to 65,536 bits
    TEXT[!MAY]:    long.
    TEXT[!MUST]: To facilitate use by devices with limited memory and CPU
    TEXT[!MUST]:    resources, Multicast DNS queriers are only REQUIRED to be able to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    parse a restricted form of the DNS NSEC record.
    TEXT[!MUST]: All compliant
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Multicast DNS implementations MUST at least correctly generate and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    parse the restricted DNS NSEC record format described below:
    TEXT[!MUST]: Consequently, if a Multicast DNS responder were
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to have records with rrtypes above 255, it MUST NOT generate these
    TEXT[!MUST]:    restricted-form NSEC records for those names, since to do so would
    TEXT[!MUST]:    imply that the name has no records with rrtypes above 255, which
    TEXT[!MUST]:    would be false.
    TEXT[!MUST]: In such cases a Multicast DNS responder MUST either
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (a) emit no NSEC record for that name, or (b) emit a full NSEC record
    TEXT[!MUST]:    containing the appropriate Type Bit Map block(s) with the correct
    TEXT[!MUST]:    bits set for all the record types that exist.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If a Multicast DNS implementation receives an NSEC record where the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    'Next Domain Name' field is not the record's own name, then the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    implementation SHOULD ignore the 'Next Domain Name' field and process
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the remainder of the NSEC record as usual.
    TEXT[!MUST]: In Multicast DNS the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    'Next Domain Name' field is not currently used, but it could be used
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in a future version of this protocol, which is why a Multicast DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    implementation MUST NOT reject or ignore an NSEC record it receives
    TEXT[!MUST]:    just because it finds an unexpected value in the 'Next Domain Name'
    TEXT[!MUST]:    field.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    If a Multicast DNS implementation receives an NSEC record containing
    TEXT[!MAY]:    more than one Type Bit Map, or where the Type Bit Map block number is
    TEXT[!MAY]:    not zero, or where the block length is not in the range 1-32, then
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the Multicast DNS implementation MAY silently ignore the entire NSEC
    TEXT[!MAY]:    record.
    TEXT[!MUST]: A Multicast DNS implementation MUST NOT ignore an entire
    TEXT[!MUST]:    message just because that message contains one or more NSEC record(s)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    that the Multicast DNS implementation cannot parse.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    To help differentiate these synthesized NSEC records (generated
    TEXT[!MUST]:    programmatically on-the-fly) from conventional Unicast DNS NSEC
    TEXT[!MUST]:    records (which actually exist in a signed DNS zone), the synthesized
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Multicast DNS NSEC records MUST NOT have the NSEC bit set in the Type
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Bit Map, whereas conventional Unicast DNS NSEC records do have the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NSEC bit set.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: In general, the TTL given for an NSEC record
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD be the same as the TTL that the record would have had, had it
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    existed.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A responder MUST only generate negative responses to queries for
    TEXT[!MUST]:    which it has legitimate ownership of the name, rrtype, and rrclass in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    question, and can legitimately assert that no record with that name,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    rrtype, and rrclass exists.

  SECTION: [Responding to Address Queries](#section-6.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When a Multicast DNS responder sends a Multicast DNS response message
    TEXT[!MUST]:    containing its own address records, it MUST include all addresses
    TEXT[!MUST]:    that are valid on the interface on which it is sending the message,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and MUST NOT include addresses that are not valid on that interface
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (such as addresses that may be configured on the host's other
    TEXT[!MUST]:    interfaces).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    When a Multicast DNS responder places an IPv4 or IPv6 address record
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    (rrtype "A" or "AAAA") into a response message, it SHOULD also place
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    any records of the other address type with the same name into the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    additional section, if there is space in the message.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In the event that a device has only IPv4 addresses but no IPv6
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    addresses, or vice versa, then the appropriate NSEC record SHOULD be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    placed into the additional section, so that queriers can know with
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    certainty that the device has no addresses of that kind.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Other Multicast DNS responders may treat this case as logically two
    TEXT[!MUST]:    interfaces (one with one or more IPv4 addresses, and the other with
    TEXT[!MUST]:    one or more IPv6 addresses), but responders that operate this way
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST NOT put the corresponding automatic NSEC records in replies they
    TEXT[!MUST]:    send (i.e., a negative IPv4 assertion in their IPv6 responses, and a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    negative IPv6 assertion in their IPv4 responses) because this would
    TEXT[!MUST]:    cause incorrect operation in responders on the network that work the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    former way.

  SECTION: [Responding to Multiquestion Queries](#section-6.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Multicast DNS responders MUST correctly handle DNS query messages
    TEXT[!MUST]:    containing more than one question, by answering any or all of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    questions to which they have answers.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    queries, where responding without delay is allowed in appropriate
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    cases, for query messages containing more than one question, all
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    (non-defensive) answers SHOULD be randomly delayed in the range
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    20-120 ms, or 400-500 ms if the TC (truncated) bit is set.

  SECTION: [Response Aggregation](#section-6.4)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    When possible, a responder SHOULD, for the sake of network
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    efficiency, aggregate as many responses as possible into a single
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Multicast DNS response message.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: For example, when a responder has
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    several responses it plans to send, each delayed by a different
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    interval, then earlier responses SHOULD be delayed by up to an
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    additional 500 ms if that will permit them to be aggregated with
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    other responses scheduled to go out a little later.

  SECTION: [Wildcard Queries (qtype "ANY" and qclass "ANY")](#section-6.5)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When responding to queries using qtype "ANY" (255) and/or qclass
    TEXT[!MUST]:    "ANY" (255), a Multicast DNS responder MUST respond with *ALL* of its
    TEXT[!MUST]:    records that match the query.

  SECTION: [Cooperating Multicast DNS Responders](#section-6.6)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       o If A's resource record is intended to be a member of a unique
    TEXT[!MUST]:         resource record set owned solely by that responder, then this is
    TEXT[!MUST]:         a conflict and MUST be handled as described in Section 9,
    TEXT[!MUST]:         "Conflict Resolution".
    TEXT[!MUST]:       o If the TTL of B's resource record given in the message is less
    TEXT[!MUST]:         than half the true TTL from A's point of view, then A MUST mark
    TEXT[!MUST]:         its record to be announced via multicast.

  SECTION: [Legacy Unicast Responses](#section-6.7)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In this case, the Multicast DNS responder MUST send a UDP response
    TEXT[!MUST]:    directly back to the querier, via unicast, to the query packet's
    TEXT[!MUST]:    source IP address and port.
    TEXT[!MUST]: This unicast response MUST be a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    conventional unicast response as would be generated by a conventional
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Unicast DNS server; for example, it MUST repeat the query ID and the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    question given in the query message.
    TEXT[!MUST]: In addition, the cache-flush
    TEXT[!MUST]:    bit described in Section 10.2, "Announcements to Flush Outdated Cache
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Entries", MUST NOT be set in legacy unicast responses.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The resource record TTL given in a legacy unicast response SHOULD NOT
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    be greater than ten seconds, even if the true TTL of the Multicast
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DNS resource record is higher.

  SECTION: [Known-Answer Suppression](#section-7.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A Multicast DNS responder MUST NOT answer a Multicast DNS query if
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the answer it would give is already included in the Answer Section
    TEXT[!MUST]:    with an RR TTL at least half the correct value.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the RR TTL of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    answer as given in the Answer Section is less than half of the true
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RR TTL as known by the Multicast DNS responder, the responder MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    send an answer so as to update the querier's cache before the record
    TEXT[!MUST]:    becomes in danger of expiration.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Therefore, a Multicast DNS querier SHOULD NOT include
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    records in the Known-Answer list whose remaining TTL is less than
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    half of their original TTL.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A Multicast DNS querier MUST NOT cache resource records observed in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the Known-Answer Section of other Multicast DNS queries.

  SECTION: [Multipacket Known-Answer Suppression](#section-7.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: It MUST then set the TC
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (Truncated) bit in the header before sending the query.
    TEXT[!MUST]: It MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    immediately follow the packet with another query packet containing no
    TEXT[!MUST]:    questions and as many more Known-Answer records as will fit.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the responder sees any of its answers listed in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Known-Answer lists of subsequent packets from the querying host, it
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST delete that answer from the list of answers it is planning to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    give (provided that no other host on the network has also issued a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    query for that record and is waiting to receive an answer).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If the responder receives additional Known-Answer packets with the TC
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    bit set, it SHOULD extend the delay as necessary to ensure a pause of
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    400-500 ms after the last such packet before it sends its answer.

  SECTION: [Duplicate Question Suppression](#section-7.3)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If a host is planning to transmit (or retransmit) a query, and it
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    sees another host on the network send a query containing the same
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    "QM" question, and the Known-Answer Section of that query does not
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    contain any records that this host would not also put in its own
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Known-Answer Section, then this host SHOULD treat its own query as
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    having been sent.

  SECTION: [Duplicate Answer Suppression](#section-7.4)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If a host is planning to send an answer, and it sees another host on
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the network send a response message containing the same answer
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    record, and the TTL in that record is not less than the TTL this host
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    would have given, then this host SHOULD treat its own answer as
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    having been sent, and not also send an identical answer itself.

  SECTION: [Probing and Announcing on Startup](#section-8)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Whenever a Multicast DNS responder starts up, wakes up from sleep,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    receives an indication of a network interface "Link Change" event, or
    TEXT[!MUST]:    has any other reason to believe that its network connectivity may
    TEXT[!MUST]:    have changed in some relevant way, it MUST perform the two startup
    TEXT[!MUST]:    steps below: Probing (Section 8.1) and Announcing (Section 8.3).

  SECTION: [Probing](#section-8.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The first startup step is that, for all those resource records that a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Multicast DNS responder desires to be unique on the local link, it
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST send a Multicast DNS query asking for those resource records, to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    see if any of them are already in use.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: All probe queries SHOULD be done
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    using the desired resource record name and class (usually class 1,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    "Internet"), and query type "ANY" (255), to elicit answers for all
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    types of records with that name.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When sending probe queries, a host MUST NOT consult its cache for
    TEXT[!MUST]:    potential answers.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Hence, it is important that when a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    device receives a probe query for a name that it is currently using,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    it SHOULD generate its response to defend that name immediately and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    send it as quickly as possible.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    rules, the probes SHOULD be sent as "QU" questions with the unicast-
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    response bit set, to allow a defending host to respond immediately
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    via unicast, instead of potentially having to wait before replying
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    via multicast.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    During probing, from the time the first probe packet is sent until
    TEXT[!MUST]:    250 ms after the third probe, if any conflicting Multicast DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response is received, then the probing host MUST defer to the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    existing host, and SHOULD choose new names for some or all of its
    TEXT[!MUST]:    resource records as appropriate.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Apparently conflicting Multicast
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNS responses received *before* the first probe packet is sent MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be silently ignored (see discussion of stale probe packets in Section
    TEXT[!MUST]:    8.2, "Simultaneous Probe Tiebreaking", below).
    TEXT[!MUST]: In the case of a host
    TEXT[!MUST]:    probing using query type "ANY" as recommended above, any answer
    TEXT[!MUST]:    containing a record with that name, of any type, MUST be considered a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    conflicting response and handled accordingly.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If fifteen conflicts occur within any ten-second period, then the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    host MUST wait at least five seconds before each successive
    TEXT[!MUST]:    additional probe attempt.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If a responder knows by other means that its unique resource record
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    set name, rrtype, and rrclass cannot already be in use by any other
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    responder on the network, then it SHOULD skip the probing step for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    that resource record set.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Similarly, if a responder is acting as a proxy,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    taking over from another Multicast DNS responder that has already
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    verified the uniqueness of the record, then the proxy SHOULD NOT
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    repeat the probing step for those records.

  SECTION: [Simultaneous Probe Tiebreaking](#section-8.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In the case of resource records containing rdata that is subject to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    name compression [RFC1035], the names MUST be uncompressed before
    TEXT[!MUST]:    comparison.

  SECTION: [Announcing](#section-8.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The second startup step is that the Multicast DNS responder MUST send
    TEXT[!MUST]:    an unsolicited Multicast DNS response containing, in the Answer
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Section, all of its newly registered resource records (both shared
    TEXT[!MUST]:    records, and unique records that have completed the probing step).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Multicast DNS responder MUST send at least two unsolicited
    TEXT[!MUST]:    responses, one second apart.
    TEXT[!MAY]: To provide increased robustness against
    TEXT[!MAY]:    packet loss, a responder MAY send up to eight unsolicited responses,
    TEXT[!MAY]:    provided that the interval between unsolicited responses increases by
    TEXT[!MAY]:    at least a factor of two with every response sent.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A Multicast DNS responder MUST NOT send announcements in the absence
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of information that its network connectivity may have changed in some
    TEXT[!MUST]:    relevant way.
    TEXT[!MUST]: In particular, a Multicast DNS responder MUST NOT send
    TEXT[!MUST]:    regular periodic announcements as a matter of course.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Whenever a Multicast DNS responder receives any Multicast DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response (solicited or otherwise) containing a conflicting resource
    TEXT[!MUST]:    record, the conflict MUST be resolved as described in Section 9,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    "Conflict Resolution".

  SECTION: [Updating](#section-8.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    At any time, if the rdata of any of a host's Multicast DNS records
    TEXT[!MUST]:    changes, the host MUST repeat the Announcing step described above to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    update neighboring caches.
    TEXT[!MUST]: For example, if any of a host's IP
    TEXT[!MUST]:    addresses change, it MUST re-announce those address records.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In the case of shared records, a host MUST send a "goodbye"
    TEXT[!MUST]:    announcement with RR TTL zero (see Section 10.1, "Goodbye Packets")
    TEXT[!MUST]:    for the old rdata, to cause it to be deleted from peer caches, before
    TEXT[!MUST]:    announcing the new rdata.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: In the case of unique records, a host
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD omit the "goodbye" announcement, since the cache-flush bit on
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the newly announced records will cause old rdata to be flushed from
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    peer caches anyway.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A host may update the contents of any of its records at any time,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    though a host SHOULD NOT update records more frequently than ten
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    times per minute.

  SECTION: [Conflict Resolution](#section-9)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Whenever a Multicast DNS responder receives any Multicast DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response (solicited or otherwise) containing a conflicting resource
    TEXT[!MUST]:    record in any of the Resource Record Sections, the Multicast DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    responder MUST immediately reset its conflicted unique record to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    probing state, and go through the startup steps described above in
    TEXT[!MUST]: The protocol used in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the Probing phase will determine a winner and a loser, and the loser
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST cease using the name, and reconfigure.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    It is very important that any host receiving a resource record that
    TEXT[!MUST]:    conflicts with one of its own MUST take action as described above.

  SECTION: [Resource Record TTL Values and Cache Coherency](#section-10)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    As a general rule, the recommended TTL value for Multicast DNS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    resource records with a host name as the resource record's name
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    (e.g., A, AAAA, HINFO) or a host name contained within the resource
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    record's rdata (e.g., SRV, reverse mapping PTR record) SHOULD be 120
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    seconds.

  SECTION: [Goodbye Packets](#section-10.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In the case where a host knows that certain resource record data is
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    about to become invalid (for example, when the host is undergoing a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    clean shutdown), the host SHOULD send an unsolicited Multicast DNS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Queriers receiving a Multicast DNS response with a TTL of zero SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    NOT immediately delete the record from the cache, but instead record
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    a TTL of 1 and then delete the record one second later.

  SECTION: [Announcements to Flush Outdated Cache Entries](#section-10.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: In cases where the host
    TEXT[!MUST]:    has not been continuously connected and participating on the network
    TEXT[!MUST]:    link, it MUST first probe to re-verify uniqueness of its unique
    TEXT[!MUST]:    records, as described above in Section 8.1, "Probing".
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Having completed the Probing step, if necessary, the host MUST then
    TEXT[!MUST]:    send a series of unsolicited announcements to update cache entries in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    its neighbor hosts.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Any time a host sends a response packet containing some members of a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    unique RRSet, it MUST send the entire RRSet, preferably in a single
    TEXT[!MUST]:    packet, or if the entire RRSet will not fit in a single packet, in a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    quick burst of packets sent as close together as possible.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The host
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST set the cache-flush bit on all members of the unique RRSet.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The cache-flush bit MUST NOT be set in any resource records in a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response message sent in legacy unicast responses to UDP ports other
    TEXT[!MUST]:    than 5353.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The cache-flush bit MUST NOT be set in any resource records in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Known-Answer list of any query message.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The cache-flush bit MUST NOT ever be set in any shared resource
    TEXT[!MUST]:    record.

  SECTION: [Cache Flush on Failure Indication](#section-10.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When the cache receives this hint that it should reconfirm some
    TEXT[!MUST]:    record, it MUST issue two or more queries for the resource record in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    dispute.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If no response is received within ten seconds, then, even
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    though its TTL may indicate that it is not yet due to expire, that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    record SHOULD be promptly flushed from the cache.

  SECTION: [Passive Observation Of Failures (POOF)](#section-10.5)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    After seeing two or more of these queries, and seeing no multicast
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    response containing the expected answer within ten seconds, then even
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    though its TTL may indicate that it is not yet due to expire, that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    record SHOULD be flushed from the cache.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The host SHOULD NOT perform
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    its own queries to reconfirm that the record is truly gone.

  SECTION: [Source Address Check](#section-11)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    All Multicast DNS responses (including responses sent via unicast)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD be sent with IP TTL set to 255.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A host sending Multicast DNS queries to a link-local destination
    TEXT[!MUST]:    address (including the 224.0.0.251 and FF02::FB link-local multicast
    TEXT[!MUST]:    addresses) MUST only accept responses to that query that originate
    TEXT[!MUST]:    from the local link, and silently discard any other response packets.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Since queriers will ignore responses apparently originating outside
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the local subnet, a responder SHOULD avoid generating responses that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    it can reasonably predict will be ignored.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If a responder receives a query
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    addressed to the mDNS IPv4 link-local multicast address 224.0.0.251,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    from a source address not apparently on the same subnet as the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    responder (or, in the case of IPv6, from a source IPv6 address for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    which the responder does not have any address with the same prefix on
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    that interface), then even if the query indicates that a unicast
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    response is preferred (see Section 5.4, "Questions Requesting Unicast
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Responses"), the responder SHOULD elect to respond by multicast
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    anyway, since it can reasonably predict that a unicast response with
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    an apparently non-local source address will probably be ignored.

  SECTION: [Enabling and Disabling Multicast DNS](#section-13)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The option to fail-over to Multicast DNS for names not ending in
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    ".local." SHOULD be a user-configured option, and SHOULD be disabled
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    by default because of the possible security issues related to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    unintended local resolution of apparently global names.

  SECTION: [Considerations for Multiple Interfaces](#section-14)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A host SHOULD defend its dot-local host name on all active interfaces
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    on which it is answering Multicast DNS queries.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Except in the case of proxying and other similar specialized uses,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    addresses in IPv4 or IPv6 address records in Multicast DNS responses
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST be valid for use on the interface on which the response is being
    TEXT[!MUST]:    sent.

  SECTION: [Receiving Unicast Responses](#section-15.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    For this reason, all Multicast DNS implementations SHOULD use the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SO_REUSEPORT and/or SO_REUSEADDR options (or equivalent as
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    appropriate for the operating system in question) so they will all be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    able to bind to UDP port 5353 and receive incoming multicast packets
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    addressed to that port.

  SECTION: [Multicast DNS Character Set](#section-16)
    TEXT[!MUST]: Accordingly,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    it adopts the simple obvious elegant solution: all names in Multicast
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNS MUST be encoded as precomposed UTF-8 [RFC3629] "Net-Unicode"
    TEXT[!MUST]:    [RFC5198] text.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Multicast DNS names MUST NOT contain a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    "Byte Order Mark".
    TEXT[!MUST]: Any occurrence of the Unicode character U+FEFF at
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the start or anywhere else in a Multicast DNS name MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    interpreted as being an actual intended part of the name,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    representing (just as for any other legal unicode value) an actual
    TEXT[!MUST]:    literal instance of that character (in this case a zero-width non-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    breaking space character).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Multicast DNS implementations MUST NOT use any other encodings apart
    TEXT[!MUST]:    from precomposed UTF-8 (US-ASCII being considered a compatible subset
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of UTF-8).

  SECTION: [Multicast DNS Message Size](#section-17)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In the case of a single Multicast DNS resource record that is too
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    large to fit in a single MTU-sized multicast response packet, a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Multicast DNS responder SHOULD send the resource record alone, in a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    single IP datagram, using multiple IP fragments.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Resource records
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    this large SHOULD be avoided, except in the very rare cases where
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    they really are the appropriate solution to the problem at hand.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Implementers should be aware that many simple devices do not
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    reassemble fragmented IP datagrams, so large resource records SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    NOT be used except in specialized cases where the implementer knows
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A Multicast DNS packet larger than the interface MTU, which is sent
    TEXT[!MUST]:    using fragments, MUST NOT contain more than one resource record.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Even when fragmentation is used, a Multicast DNS packet, including IP
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and UDP headers, MUST NOT exceed 9000 bytes.

  SECTION: [ID (Query Identifier)](#section-18.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Multicast DNS implementations SHOULD listen for unsolicited responses
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    issued by hosts booting up (or waking up from sleep or otherwise
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    joining the network).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Since these unsolicited responses may contain
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    a useful answer to a question for which the querier is currently
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    awaiting an answer, Multicast DNS implementations SHOULD examine all
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    received Multicast DNS response messages for useful answers, without
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    regard to the contents of the ID field or the Question Section.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Multicast DNS implementations MAY cache data from any or all
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Multicast DNS response messages they receive, for possible future
    TEXT[!MAY]:    use, provided of course that normal TTL aging is performed on these
    TEXT[!MAY]:    cached resource records.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In multicast query messages, the Query Identifier SHOULD be set to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    zero on transmission.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In multicast responses, including unsolicited multicast responses,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the Query Identifier MUST be set to zero on transmission, and MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    ignored on reception.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In legacy unicast response messages generated specifically in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response to a particular (unicast or multicast) query, the Query
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Identifier MUST match the ID from the query message.

  SECTION: [QR (Query/Response) Bit](#section-18.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In query messages the QR bit MUST be zero.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In response messages the QR bit MUST be one.

  SECTION: [OPCODE](#section-18.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In both multicast query and multicast response messages, the OPCODE
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST be zero on transmission (only standard queries are currently
    TEXT[!MUST]:    supported over multicast).
    TEXT[!MUST]: Multicast DNS messages received with an
    TEXT[!MUST]:    OPCODE other than zero MUST be silently ignored.

  SECTION: [AA (Authoritative Answer) Bit](#section-18.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In query messages, the Authoritative Answer bit MUST be zero on
    TEXT[!MUST]:    transmission, and MUST be ignored on reception.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In response messages for Multicast domains, the Authoritative Answer
    TEXT[!MUST]:    bit MUST be set to one (not setting this bit would imply there's some
    TEXT[!MUST]:    other place where "better" information may be found) and MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    ignored on reception.

  SECTION: [TC (Truncated) Bit](#section-18.5)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: A responder SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    record this fact, and wait for those additional Known-Answer records,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    before deciding whether to respond.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In multicast response messages, the TC bit MUST be zero on
    TEXT[!MUST]:    transmission, and MUST be ignored on reception.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In legacy unicast response messages, the TC bit has the same meaning
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    as in conventional Unicast DNS: it means that the response was too
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    large to fit in a single packet, so the querier SHOULD reissue its
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    query using TCP in order to receive the larger response.

  SECTION: [RD (Recursion Desired) Bit](#section-18.6)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In both multicast query and multicast response messages, the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Recursion Desired bit SHOULD be zero on transmission, and MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    ignored on reception.

  SECTION: [RA (Recursion Available) Bit](#section-18.7)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In both multicast query and multicast response messages, the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Recursion Available bit MUST be zero on transmission, and MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    ignored on reception.

  SECTION: [Z (Zero) Bit](#section-18.8)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In both query and response messages, the Zero bit MUST be zero on
    TEXT[!MUST]:    transmission, and MUST be ignored on reception.

  SECTION: [AD (Authentic Data) Bit](#section-18.9)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In both multicast query and multicast response messages, the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Authentic Data bit [RFC2535] MUST be zero on transmission, and MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be ignored on reception.

  SECTION: [CD (Checking Disabled) Bit](#section-18.10)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In both multicast query and multicast response messages, the Checking
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Disabled bit [RFC2535] MUST be zero on transmission, and MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    ignored on reception.

  SECTION: [RCODE (Response Code)](#section-18.11)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In both multicast query and multicast response messages, the Response
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Code MUST be zero on transmission.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Multicast DNS messages received
    TEXT[!MUST]:    with non-zero Response Codes MUST be silently ignored.

  SECTION: [Name Compression](#section-18.14)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    When generating Multicast DNS messages, implementations SHOULD use
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    name compression wherever possible to compress the names of resource
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    records, by replacing some or all of the resource record name with a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    compact two-byte reference to an appearance of that data somewhere
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    earlier in the message [RFC1035].
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: When a query contains more than one question, successive
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    questions in the same message often contain similar names, and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    consequently name compression SHOULD be used, to save bytes.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: In
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    addition, queries may also contain Known Answers in the Answer
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Section, or probe tiebreaking data in the Authority Section, and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    these names SHOULD similarly be compressed for network efficiency.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In addition to compressing the *names* of resource records, names
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    that appear within the *rdata* of the following rrtypes SHOULD also
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    be compressed in all Multicast DNS messages:
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Until future IETF Standards Action [RFC5226] specifying that names in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the rdata of other types should be compressed, names that appear
    TEXT[!MUST]:    within the rdata of any type not listed above MUST NOT be compressed.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Implementations receiving Multicast DNS messages MUST correctly
    TEXT[!MUST]:    decode compressed names appearing in the Question Section, and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    compressed names of resource records appearing in other sections.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In addition, implementations MUST correctly decode compressed names
    TEXT[!MUST]:    appearing within the *rdata* of the rrtypes listed above.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Where
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    possible, implementations SHOULD also correctly decode compressed
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    names appearing within the *rdata* of other rrtypes known to the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    implementers at the time of implementation, because such forward-
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    thinking planning helps facilitate the deployment of future
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    implementations that may have reason to compress those rrtypes.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Since all Multicast DNS implementations were
    TEXT[!MUST]:    created after 1996, all Multicast DNS implementations are REQUIRED to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    decode compressed SRV records correctly.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In legacy unicast responses generated to answer legacy queries, name
    TEXT[!MUST]:    compression MUST NOT be performed on SRV records.

  SECTION: [Security Considerations](#section-21)
    TEXT[!MUST]: To
    TEXT[!MUST]:    avoid this, a host MUST NOT append the search suffix ".local.", if
    TEXT[!MUST]:    present, to any relative (partially qualified) host name containing
    TEXT[!MUST]:    two or more labels.

  SECTION: [Domain Name Reservation Considerations](#section-22.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          Since there is no central authority responsible for assigning
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          dot-local names, and all devices on the local network are
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          equally entitled to claim any dot-local name, users SHOULD be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          aware of this and SHOULD exercise appropriate caution.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: In an
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          untrusted or unfamiliar network environment, users SHOULD be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          aware that using a name like "www.local" may not actually
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          connect them to the web site they expected, and could easily
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          connect them to a different web page, or even a fake or spoof
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          of their intended web site, designed to trick them into
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          revealing confidential information.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Name resolution APIs and libraries SHOULD recognize these names
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          as special and SHOULD NOT send queries for these names to their
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          configured (unicast) caching DNS server(s).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Caching DNS servers SHOULD recognize these names as special and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          SHOULD NOT attempt to look up NS records for them, or otherwise
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          query authoritative DNS servers in an attempt to resolve these
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          names.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Instead, caching DNS servers SHOULD generate immediate
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          NXDOMAIN responses for all such queries they may receive (from
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          misbehaving name resolver libraries).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Authoritative DNS servers SHOULD NOT by default be configurable
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          to answer queries for these names, and, like caching DNS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          servers, SHOULD generate immediate NXDOMAIN responses for all
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          such queries they may receive.
    TEXT[!MAY]: DNS server software MAY provide
    TEXT[!MAY]:          a configuration option to override this default, for testing
    TEXT[!MAY]:          purposes or other specialized uses.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: DNS server operators SHOULD NOT attempt to configure
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          authoritative DNS servers to act as authoritative for any of
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          these names.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Since name resolver libraries and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          caching DNS servers SHOULD NOT send queries for those names
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          (see 3 and 4 above), such queries SHOULD be suppressed before
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          they even reach the authoritative DNS server in question, and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          consequently it will not even get an opportunity to answer
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          them.
    TEXT[!MUST]: DNS Registrars MUST NOT allow any of these names to be
    TEXT[!MUST]:          registered in the normal way to any person or entity.

  SECTION: [Design Rationale for Maximum Multicast DNS Name Length](#appendix-C)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Compliant Multicast DNS implementations MUST support names up to 255
    TEXT[!MUST]:    bytes plus a terminating zero, i.e., 256 bytes total.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6763
  SECTION: [Instance Names](#section-4.1.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: It
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST NOT contain ASCII control characters (byte values 0x00-0x1F and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    0x7F) [RFC20] but otherwise is allowed to contain any characters,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    without restriction, including spaces, uppercase, lowercase,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    punctuation -- including dots -- accented characters, non-Roman text,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and anything else that may be represented using Net-Unicode.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The <Instance> portion of the name of a service being offered on the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    network SHOULD be configurable by the user setting up the service, so
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    that he or she may give it an informative name.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: However, the device
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    or service SHOULD NOT require the user to configure a name before it
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    can be used.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The default name should be short and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    descriptive, and SHOULD NOT include the device's Media Access Control
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    (MAC) address, serial number, or any similar incomprehensible
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    hexadecimal string in an attempt to make the name globally unique.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    For discussion of why <Instance> names don't need to be (and SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    NOT be) made unique at the factory, see Appendix D, "Choice of
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Factory-Default Names".

  SECTION: [Domain Names](#section-4.1.3)
    TEXT[!MAY]: In cases where the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    DNS server returns a negative response for the name in question,
    TEXT[!MAY]:    client software MAY choose to retry the query using the "Punycode"
    TEXT[!MAY]:    algorithm [RFC3492] to convert the UTF-8 name to an IDNA "A-label"
    TEXT[!MAY]:    [RFC5890], beginning with the top-level label, then issuing the query

  SECTION: [Internal Handling of Names](#section-4.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If client software takes the <Instance>, <Service>, and <Domain>
    TEXT[!MUST]:    portions of a Service Instance Name and internally concatenates them
    TEXT[!MUST]:    together into a single string, then because the <Instance> portion is
    TEXT[!MUST]:    allowed to contain any characters, including dots, appropriate
    TEXT[!MUST]:    precautions MUST be taken to ensure that DNS label boundaries are
    TEXT[!MUST]:    properly preserved.

  SECTION: [Service Instance Resolution](#section-5)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In the event that more than one SRV is returned, clients MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    correctly interpret the priority and weight fields -- i.e., lower-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    numbered priority servers should be used in preference to higher-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    numbered priority servers, and servers with equal priority should be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    selected randomly in proportion to their relative weights.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: However,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    in the overwhelmingly common case, a single advertised DNS-SD service
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    instance is described by exactly one SRV record, and in this common
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    case the priority and weight fields of the SRV record SHOULD both be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    set to zero.

  SECTION: [Data Syntax for DNS-SD TXT Records](#section-6)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Every DNS-SD service MUST have a TXT record in addition to its SRV
    TEXT[!MUST]:    record, with the same name, even if the service has no additional
    TEXT[!MUST]:    data to store and the TXT record contains no more than a single zero
    TEXT[!MUST]:    byte.

  SECTION: [General Format Rules for DNS TXT Records](#section-6.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNS-SD implementations MUST NOT emit empty TXT records.
    TEXT[!MUST]: DNS-SD
    TEXT[!MUST]:    clients MUST treat the following as equivalent:

  SECTION: [DNS-SD TXT Record Size](#section-6.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Using TXT records larger than 1300 bytes is NOT RECOMMENDED at this
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    time.

  SECTION: [DNS TXT Record Format Rules for Use in DNS-SD](#section-6.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: If an implementation sees unknown keys
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in a service TXT record, it MUST silently ignore them.
    TEXT[!MUST]: This information -- target host name and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    port number -- MUST NOT be duplicated using key/value attributes in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the TXT record.

  SECTION: [Rules for Keys in DNS-SD Key/Value Pairs](#section-6.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The key MUST be at least one character.
    TEXT[!MUST]: DNS-SD TXT record strings
    TEXT[!MUST]:    beginning with an '=' character (i.e., the key is missing) MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    silently ignored.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The key SHOULD be no more than nine characters long.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The characters of a key MUST be printable US-ASCII values (0x20-0x7E)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    [RFC20], excluding '=' (0x3D).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A given key SHOULD NOT appear more than once in a TXT record.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If a client receives a TXT record containing the same key more than
    TEXT[!MUST]:    once, then the client MUST silently ignore all but the first
    TEXT[!MUST]:    occurrence of that attribute.

  SECTION: [Rules for Values in DNS-SD Key/Value Pairs](#section-6.5)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The value MUST NOT
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Authors defining DNS-SD profiles SHOULD NOT generically convert
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    binary attribute data types into printable text using hexadecimal
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    representation, Base-64 [RFC4648], or Unix-to-Unix (UU) encoding,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    merely for the sake of making the data appear to be printable text
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    when seen in a generic debugging tool.

  SECTION: [Version Tag](#section-6.7)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Clients SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    ignore TXT records with a txtvers number higher (or lower) than the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    version(s) they know how to interpret.

  SECTION: [Flagship Naming](#section-8)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Note: When used with Multicast DNS [RFC6762], the target host field
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of the placeholder SRV record MUST NOT be the empty root label.

  SECTION: [Discovery of Browsing and Registration Domains (Domain Enumeration)](#section-11)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Address-derived Domain Enumeration queries SHOULD NOT be done for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    IPv4 link-local addresses [RFC3927] or IPv6 link-local addresses
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    [RFC4862].

  SECTION: [DNS Additional Record Generation](#section-12)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    This section recommends which additional records SHOULD be generated
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    to improve network efficiency, for both Unicast and Multicast DNS-SD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    responses.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Note that while servers SHOULD add these additional records for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    efficiency purposes, as with all DNS additional records, it is the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    client's responsibility to determine whether or not to trust them.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Clients MUST be capable of functioning correctly with DNS servers
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (and Multicast DNS Responders) that fail to generate these additional
    TEXT[!MUST]:    records automatically, by issuing subsequent queries for any further
    TEXT[!MUST]:    record(s) they require.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The additional-record generation rules in
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    this section are RECOMMENDED for improving network efficiency, but
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    are not required for correctness.

    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    server/responder SHOULD include the following additional records:

    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    When including an SRV record in a response packet, the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    server/responder SHOULD include the following additional records:

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6781
  SECTION: [Algorithm Rollovers](#section-4.1.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       There MUST be an RRSIG for each RRset using at least one DNSKEY
    TEXT[!MUST]:       of each algorithm in the zone apex DNSKEY RRset.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The apex
    TEXT[!MUST]:       DNSKEY RRset itself MUST be signed by each algorithm appearing
    TEXT[!MUST]:       in the DS RRset located at the delegating parent (if any).

  SECTION: [Single Signing Type Algorithm Rollover, RFC 5011 Style](#section-4.1.4.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       Once the resolver sees the REVOKE bit, it MUST NOT use this key
    TEXT[!MUST]:       as a trust anchor or for any other purpose except to validate
    TEXT[!MUST]:       the RRSIG it signed over the DNSKEY RRset specifically for the
    TEXT[!MUST]:       purpose of validating the revocation.

  SECTION: [NSEC3 Algorithm](#section-5.3.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: [RFC5155] specifically states: "When specifying a new hash
    TEXT[!MUST]:    algorithm for use with NSEC3, a transition mechanism MUST also be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    defined".

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6840
  SECTION: [NSEC3 Support](#section-2.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The zone
    TEXT[!MUST]:    may be using either, and validators supporting these algorithms MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    support both NSEC3 and NSEC responses.

  SECTION: [Implement a BAD Cache](#section-3.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: That guidance has changed: security-aware
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    resolvers SHOULD implement a BAD cache as described in [RFC4035].

  SECTION: [Clarifications on Nonexistence Proofs](#section-4.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Ancestor delegation NSEC or NSEC3 RRs MUST NOT be used to assume
    TEXT[!MUST]:    nonexistence of any RRs below that zone cut, which include all RRs at
    TEXT[!MUST]:    that (original) owner name other than DS RRs, and all RRs below that
    TEXT[!MUST]:    owner name regardless of type.
    TEXT[!MUST]: An NSEC or NSEC3 RR with the DNAME bit set MUST NOT be used
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to assume the nonexistence of any subdomain of that NSEC/NSEC3 RR's
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (original) owner name.

  SECTION: [Validating Responses to an ANY Query](#section-4.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When validating a response to QTYPE=*, all received RRsets that match
    TEXT[!MUST]:    QNAME and QCLASS MUST be validated.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If there are no RRsets
    TEXT[!MUST]:    matching QNAME and QCLASS, that fact MUST be validated according to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the rules in Section 5.4 of [RFC4035] (as clarified in this
    TEXT[!MUST]:    document).

  SECTION: [Check for CNAME](#section-4.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: When
    TEXT[!MUST]:    validating a NOERROR/NODATA response, validators MUST check the CNAME
    TEXT[!MUST]:    bit in the matching NSEC or NSEC3 RR's type bitmap in addition to the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    bit for the query type.

  SECTION: [Insecure Delegation Proofs](#section-4.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The validator also
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST check for the presence of the NS bit in the matching NSEC (or
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NSEC3) RR (proving that there is, indeed, a delegation), or
    TEXT[!MUST]:    alternately make sure that the delegation is covered by an NSEC3 RR
    TEXT[!MUST]:    with the Opt-Out flag set.

  SECTION: [Unknown DS Message Digest Algorithms](#section-5.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: In brief, DS records
    TEXT[!MUST]:    using unknown or unsupported message digest algorithms MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    treated the same way as DS records referring to DNSKEY RRs of unknown
    TEXT[!MUST]:    or unsupported public key algorithms.

  SECTION: [Private Algorithms](#section-5.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: In these
    TEXT[!MUST]:    cases, the resolver MUST retrieve the corresponding DNSKEY for each
    TEXT[!MUST]:    private algorithm DS record and examine the public key field to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    determine the algorithm in use.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The security-aware resolver MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    ensure that the hash of the DNSKEY RR's owner name and RDATA matches
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the digest in the DS RR as described in Section 5.2 of [RFC4035],
    TEXT[!MUST]:    authenticating the DNSKEY.

  SECTION: [Caution about Local Policy and Multiple RRSIGs](#section-5.4)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    This document specifies that a resolver SHOULD accept any valid RRSIG
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    as sufficient, and only determine that an RRset is Bogus if all
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    RRSIGs fail validation.

  SECTION: [Setting the DO Bit on Replies](#section-5.6)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    As stated in Section 3 of [RFC3225], the DNSSEC OK (DO) bit of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    query MUST be copied in the response.
    TEXT[!MUST]: However, in order to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    interoperate with implementations that ignore this rule on sending,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    resolvers MUST ignore the DO bit in responses.

  SECTION: [Setting the AD Bit on Replies](#section-5.8)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: In
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    order to interoperate with legacy stub resolvers and middleboxes that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    neither understand nor ignore the AD bit, validating resolvers SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    only set the AD bit when a response both meets the conditions listed
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    in Section 3.2.3 of [RFC4035], and the request contained either a set
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DO bit or a set AD bit.

  SECTION: [Always Set the CD Bit on Queries](#section-5.9)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    When processing a request with the Checking Disabled (CD) bit set, a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    resolver SHOULD attempt to return all response data, even data that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    has failed DNSSEC validation.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    This document further specifies that validating resolvers SHOULD set
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the CD bit on every upstream query.

  SECTION: [Mandatory Algorithm Rules](#section-5.11)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       A signed zone MUST include a DNSKEY for each algorithm present in
    TEXT[!MUST]:       the zone's DS RRset and expected trust anchors for the zone.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The
    TEXT[!MUST]:       zone MUST also be signed with each algorithm (though not each key)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       present in the DNSKEY RRset.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Validators
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD accept any single valid path.
    TEXT[!MUST]: They SHOULD NOT insist that all
    TEXT[!MUST]:    algorithms signaled in the DS RRset work, and they MUST NOT insist
    TEXT[!MUST]:    that all algorithms signaled in the DNSKEY RRset work.
    TEXT[!MAY]: A validator
    TEXT[!MAY]:    MAY have a configuration option to perform a signature completeness
    TEXT[!MAY]:    test to support troubleshooting.

  SECTION: [Ignore Extra Signatures from Unknown Keys](#section-5.12)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Validating resolvers MUST disregard RRSIGs in a zone that do not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (currently) have a corresponding DNSKEY in the zone.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Similarly, a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    validating resolver MUST disregard RRSIGs with algorithm types that
    TEXT[!MUST]:    don't exist in the DNSKEY RRset.

  SECTION: [Errors in RFC 5155](#section-6.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       Blocks with no types present MUST NOT be included.

  SECTION: [Discussion of Setting the CD Bit](#appendix-B)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Using this model is NOT
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    RECOMMENDED.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6891
  SECTION: [Introduction](#section-1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Extended labels remain defined, but their use is discouraged due to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    practical difficulties with deployment; their use in the future
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD only be considered after careful evaluation of the deployment
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    hindrances.

  SECTION: [EDNS Support Requirement](#section-3)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Flags SHOULD be used
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    only when necessary for DNS resolution to function.

  SECTION: [Extended Label Types](#section-5)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: As such, proposals
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    that contemplate extended labels SHOULD weigh this deployment cost
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    against the possibility of implementing functionality in other ways.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Finally, implementations MUST NOT generate or pass Binary Labels in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    their communications, as they are now deprecated.

  SECTION: [Basic Elements](#section-6.1.1)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    An OPT pseudo-RR (sometimes called a meta-RR) MAY be added to the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    additional data section of a request.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If an OPT record is present in a received request, compliant
    TEXT[!MUST]:    responders MUST include an OPT record in their respective responses.
    TEXT[!MUST]: OPT RRs MUST NOT be cached,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    forwarded, or stored in or loaded from master files.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    The OPT RR MAY be placed anywhere within the additional data section.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When an OPT RR is included within any DNS message, it MUST be the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    only OPT RR in that message.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If a query message with more than one
    TEXT[!MUST]:    OPT RR is received, a FORMERR (RCODE=1) MUST be returned.

  SECTION: [Wire Format](#section-6.1.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:        +------------+--------------+------------------------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:        | Field Name | Field Type   | Description                  |
    TEXT[!MUST]:        +------------+--------------+------------------------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:        | NAME       | domain name  | MUST be 0 (root domain)      |
    TEXT[!MUST]:        | TYPE       | u_int16_t    | OPT (41)                     |
    TEXT[!MUST]:        | CLASS      | u_int16_t    | requestor's UDP payload size |
    TEXT[!MUST]:        | TTL        | u_int32_t    | extended RCODE and flags     |
    TEXT[!MUST]:        | RDLEN      | u_int16_t    | length of all RDATA          |
    TEXT[!MUST]:        | RDATA      | octet stream | {attribute,value} pairs      |
    TEXT[!MUST]:        +------------+--------------+------------------------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]: Each option MUST be treated as a bit field.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Any OPTION-CODE values not understood by a responder or requestor
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST be ignored.
    TEXT[!MUST]: For example, an
    TEXT[!MUST]:    option specification might say that if a responder sees and supports
    TEXT[!MUST]:    option XYZ, it MUST include option XYZ in its response.

  SECTION: [OPT Record TTL Field Use](#section-6.1.3)
    TEXT[!MAY]:       requestor's version numbering strategy MAY ideally be a run-time
    TEXT[!MAY]:       configuration option.
    TEXT[!MUST]:       If a responder does not implement the VERSION level of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:       request, then it MUST respond with RCODE=BADVERS.
    TEXT[!MUST]: All responses
    TEXT[!MUST]:       MUST be limited in format to the VERSION level of the request, but
    TEXT[!MUST]:       the VERSION of each response SHOULD be the highest implementation
    TEXT[!MUST]:       level of the responder.

  SECTION: [Cache Behaviour](#section-6.2.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The OPT record MUST NOT be cached.

  SECTION: [Fallback](#section-6.2.2)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    If a requestor detects that the remote end does not support EDNS(0),
    TEXT[!MAY]:    it MAY issue queries without an OPT record.
    TEXT[!MAY]: It MAY cache this
    TEXT[!MAY]:    knowledge for a brief time in order to avoid fallback delays in the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    future.
    TEXT[!MAY]: If an implementation detects that some
    TEXT[!MAY]:    servers for the zone support EDNS(0) while others would force the use
    TEXT[!MAY]:    of TCP to fetch all data, preference MAY be given to servers that
    TEXT[!MAY]:    support EDNS(0).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Implementers SHOULD analyse this choice and the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    impact on both endpoints.

  SECTION: [Requestor's Payload Size](#section-6.2.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Values lower than 512 MUST be treated as equal to 512.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The requestor SHOULD place a value in this field that it can actually
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    receive.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: For example, if a requestor sits behind a firewall that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    will block fragmented IP packets, a requestor SHOULD NOT choose a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    value that will cause fragmentation.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Where fragmentation is not a concern, use of bigger values SHOULD be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    considered by implementers.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Implementations SHOULD use their largest
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    configured or implemented values as a starting point in an EDNS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    transaction in the absence of previous knowledge about the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    destination server.
    TEXT[!MUST]: It MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NOT be cached for use beyond the transaction in which it is
    TEXT[!MUST]:    advertised.

  SECTION: [Payload Size Selection](#section-6.2.5)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    A requestor MAY choose to implement a fallback to smaller advertised
    TEXT[!MAY]:    sizes to work around firewall or other network limitations.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    requestor SHOULD choose to use a fallback mechanism that begins with
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    a large size, such as 4096.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If that fails, a fallback around the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    range of 1280-1410 bytes SHOULD be tried, as it has a reasonable
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    chance to fit within a single Ethernet frame.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Failing that, a
    TEXT[!MAY]:    requestor MAY choose a 512-byte packet, which with large answers may
    TEXT[!MAY]:    cause a TCP retry.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Values of less than 512 bytes MUST be treated as equal to 512 bytes.

  SECTION: [Support in Middleboxes](#section-6.2.6)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Conformant middleboxes MUST NOT limit DNS messages over UDP to 512
    TEXT[!MUST]:    bytes.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Middleboxes that simply forward requests to a recursive resolver MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NOT modify and MUST NOT delete the OPT record contents in either
    TEXT[!MUST]:    direction.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Middleboxes that have additional functionality, such as answering
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    queries or acting as intelligent forwarders, SHOULD be able to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    process the OPT record and act based on its contents.
    TEXT[!MUST]: These
    TEXT[!MUST]:    middleboxes MUST consider the incoming request and any outgoing
    TEXT[!MUST]:    requests as separate transactions if the characteristics of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    messages are different.

  SECTION: [Transport Considerations](#section-7)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Lack of presence of an OPT record in a request MUST be taken as an
    TEXT[!MUST]:    indication that the requestor does not implement any part of this
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specification and that the responder MUST NOT include an OPT record
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in its response.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Extended agents MUST be prepared for handling interactions with
    TEXT[!MUST]:    unextended clients in the face of new protocol elements and fall back
    TEXT[!MUST]:    gracefully to unextended DNS when needed.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Responders that choose not to implement the protocol extensions
    TEXT[!MUST]:    defined in this document MUST respond with a return code (RCODE) of
    TEXT[!MUST]:    FORMERR to messages containing an OPT record in the additional
    TEXT[!MUST]:    section and MUST NOT include an OPT record in the response.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If there is a problem with processing the OPT record itself, such as
    TEXT[!MUST]:    an option value that is badly formatted or that includes out-of-range
    TEXT[!MUST]:    values, a FORMERR MUST be returned.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If this occurs, the response
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST include an OPT record.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The minimal response MUST be the DNS header, question section, and an
    TEXT[!MUST]:    OPT record.
    TEXT[!MUST]: This MUST also occur when a truncated response (using
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the DNS header's TC bit) is returned.

  SECTION: [IANA Considerations](#section-9)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Flags SHOULD be used only when necessary for DNS resolution
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    to function.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6975
  SECTION: [Introduction](#section-1)
    TEXT[!MAY]: These three new
    TEXT[!MAY]:    EDNS0 option codes are all OPTIONAL to implement and use.

  SECTION: [Signaling DNSSEC Algorithm Understood (DAU), DS Hash Understood](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MAY]: These options
    TEXT[!MAY]:    can be used independently of each other and MAY appear in any order
    TEXT[!MAY]:    in the OPT RR.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The order of the code values can be arbitrary and MUST NOT be used to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    infer preference.

  SECTION: [Client Considerations](#section-4)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The validating end-system resolver MUST also set the DNSSEC
    TEXT[!MUST]:    OK bit [RFC4035] to indicate that it wishes to receive DNSSEC RRs in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the response.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Likewise,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    clients MUST NOT include RESERVED codes in any of the options.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Additionally, a client is under no obligation to list every algorithm
    TEXT[!MAY]:    it implements and MAY choose to only list algorithms the client
    TEXT[!MAY]:    wishes to signal as understood.
