    TEXT[!MUST]:    Since the DAU, DHU, and/or N3U options are only set in the query, if
    TEXT[!MUST]:    a client sees these options in the response, no action needs to be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    taken and the client MUST ignore the option values.

  SECTION: [Validating Stub Resolvers](#section-4.1.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Such validating resolvers SHOULD include the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DAU, DHU, and/or the N3U option(s) in the OPT RR when sending a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    query.

  SECTION: [Non-validating Stub Resolvers](#section-4.1.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The DAU, DHU, and N3U EDNS0 options MUST NOT be included by
    TEXT[!MUST]:    non-validating stub resolvers.

  SECTION: [Validating Recursive Resolvers](#section-4.2.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When the recursive server receives a query with one or more of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    options set, the recursive server MUST set the algorithm list for any
    TEXT[!MUST]:    outgoing iterative queries for that resolution chain to a union of
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the stub client's list and the validating recursive resolver's list.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    If the client included the DO and Checking Disabled (CD) bits, but
    TEXT[!MAY]:    did not include the DAU, DHU, and/or N3U option(s) in the query, the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    validating recursive resolver MAY include the option(s) with its own
    TEXT[!MAY]:    list in full.
    TEXT[!MAY]: If one or more of the options are missing, the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    validating recursive resolver MAY include the missing options with
    TEXT[!MAY]:    its own list in full.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Validating recursive resolvers MUST NOT set the DAU, DHU, and/or N3U
    TEXT[!MUST]:    option(s) in the final response to the stub client.

  SECTION: [Non-validating Recursive Resolvers](#section-4.2.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Recursive resolvers that do not do validation MUST copy the DAU, DHU,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and/or N3U option(s) seen in received queries as they represent the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    wishes of the validating downstream resolver that issued the original
    TEXT[!MUST]:    query.

  SECTION: [Intermediate System Considerations](#section-5)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Intermediate proxies (see Section 4.4.2 of [RFC5625]) that understand
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DNS are RECOMMENDED to behave like a comparable recursive resolver
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    when dealing with the DAU, DHU, and N3U options.

  SECTION: [Server Considerations](#section-6)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The options MUST NOT trigger any special
    TEXT[!MUST]:    processing (e.g., RRSIG filtering in responses) on the server side.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    If the server sees one (or more) of the options set with RESERVED
    TEXT[!MAY]:    values, the server MAY ignore recoding of those values.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Authoritative servers MUST NOT set the DAU, DHU, and/or N3U option(s)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    on any responses.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7129
  SECTION: [Experimental and Deprecated Mechanisms: NO, NSEC2, and DNSNR](#section-4)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If there is another RR that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       proves the existence of the closest encloser, this SHOULD be used
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       instead of an EXIST record.

  SECTION: [Opt-Out](#section-5.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       The validator MUST verify that an NSEC3 RR that matches QNAME is
    TEXT[!MUST]:       present and that both the QTYPE and the CNAME type are not set in
    TEXT[!MUST]:       its Type Bit Maps field.

  SECTION: [Online Signing: Minimally Covering NSEC Records](#appendix-A)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       The generated NSEC record's type bitmap MUST have the RRSIG and
    TEXT[!MUST]:       NSEC bits set and SHOULD NOT have any other bits set.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7314
  SECTION: [Expire EDNS Option (Query)](#section-2)
    TEXT[!MAY]: The EDNS EXPIRE
    TEXT[!MAY]:    option MAY be included on any QUERY, though usually this is only done
    TEXT[!MAY]:    on SOA, AXFR, and IXFR queries involved in zone maintenance.

  SECTION: [Non-authoritative Server](#section-3.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If an EDNS EXPIRE option is sent to a server that is not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    authoritative for the zone, it MUST NOT add an EDNS EXPIRE option to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the response.

  SECTION: [Secondary Behaviour](#section-4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When a secondary server performs a zone-transfer request or a zone-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    refresh query, it SHALL add an EDNS EXPIRE option to the query
    TEXT[!MUST]:    message.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If a secondary receives an EDNS EXPIRE option in a response to an SOA
    TEXT[!MUST]:    query, it SHALL update its expire timer to be the maximum of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    value returned in the EDNS EXPIRE option and the current timer value.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Similarly, if a secondary receives an EDNS EXPIRE option in its
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response to an IXFR query that indicated the secondary is up to date
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (serial matches current serial), the secondary SHALL update the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    expire timer to be the maximum of the value returned in the EDNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    EXPIRE option and the current timer value.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If the zone is transferred or updated as the result of an AXFR or
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    IXFR query and there is an EDNS EXPIRE option with the response, then
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the value of the EDNS EXPIRE option SHOULD be used instead of the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    value of the SOA EXPIRE field to initialise the expire timer.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In all cases, if the value of the SOA EXPIRE field is less than the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    value of the EDNS EXPIRE option, then the value of the SOA EXPIRE
    TEXT[!MUST]:    field MUST be used and MUST be treated as a maximum when updating or
    TEXT[!MUST]:    initialising the expire timer.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7344
  SECTION: [Automating DS Maintenance with CDS/CDNSKEY Records](#section-4)
    TEXT[!MAY]: The use of CDS/CDNSKEY is OPTIONAL.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If the Child publishes either the CDS or the CDNSKEY resource record,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    it SHOULD publish both.
    TEXT[!MAY]: If the Child knows which the Parent
    TEXT[!MAY]:    consumes, it MAY choose to only publish that record type (for
    TEXT[!MAY]:    example, some Children wish the Parent to publish a DS, but they wish
    TEXT[!MAY]:    to keep the DNSKEY "hidden" until needed).
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the Child publishes
    TEXT[!MUST]:    both, the two RRsets MUST match in content.

  SECTION: [CDS and CDNSKEY Processing Rules](#section-4.1)
    TEXT[!MAY]: This means
    TEXT[!MAY]:    that, once the Child and Parent are in sync, the Child DNS Operator
    TEXT[!MAY]:    MAY remove all CDS and CDNSKEY resource records from the zone.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  Location: MUST be at the Child zone apex.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  Signer: MUST be signed with a key that is represented in both the
    TEXT[!MUST]:       current DNSKEY and DS RRsets, unless the Parent uses the CDS or
    TEXT[!MUST]:       CDNSKEY RRset for initial enrollment; in that case, the Parent
    TEXT[!MUST]:       validates the CDS/CDNSKEY through some other means (see
    TEXT[!MUST]:       Section 6.1 and the Security Considerations).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  Continuity: MUST NOT break the current delegation if applied to DS
    TEXT[!MUST]:       RRset.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If any these conditions fail, the CDS or CDNSKEY resource record MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be ignored, and this error SHOULD be logged.

  SECTION: [CDS/CDNSKEY Publication](#section-5)
    TEXT[!MUST]: In order to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be valid, the CDS/CDNSKEY RRset(s) MUST be compliant with the rules
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in Section 4.1.
    TEXT[!MAY]: When the Parent DS is in sync with the CDS/CDNSKEY
    TEXT[!MAY]:    RRset(s), the Child DNS Operator MAY delete the CDS/CDNSKEY RRset(s);
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the Child can determine if this is the case by querying for DS
    TEXT[!MAY]:    records in the Parent.

  SECTION: [Parent-Side CDS/CDNSKEY Consumption](#section-6)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The CDS/CDNSKEY RRset(s) SHOULD be used by the Parental Agent to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    update the DS RRset in the Parent zone.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Parent MUST choose to use either CDNSKEY or CDS resource records
    TEXT[!MUST]:    as its default updating mechanism.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The Parent MAY only accept either
    TEXT[!MUST]:    CDNSKEY or CDS, but it MAY also accept both so it can use the other
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in the absence of the default updating mechanism; it MUST NOT expect
    TEXT[!MUST]:    there to be both.

  SECTION: [Detecting a Changed CDS/CDNSKEY](#section-6.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          Parent zone does not contain DS for this delegation, then the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:          "push" SHOULD be ignored.
    TEXT[!MAY]: If the Parental Agent displays the
    TEXT[!MAY]:          contents of the CDS/CDNSKEY to the user and gets confirmation
    TEXT[!MAY]:          that this represents their key, the Parental Agent MAY use this
    TEXT[!MAY]:          for initial enrollment (when the Parent zone does not contain
    TEXT[!MAY]:          the DS for this delegation).
    TEXT[!MAY]:    In either case, the Parental Agent MAY apply additional rules that
    TEXT[!MAY]:    defer the acceptance of a CDS/CDNSKEY change.

  SECTION: [CDS/CDNSKEY Polling](#section-6.1.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the CDS/CDNSKEY RRset(s) do not exist, the Parental Agent MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    take no action.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Specifically, it MUST NOT delete or alter the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    existing DS RRset.

  SECTION: [Using the New CDS/CDNSKEY Records](#section-6.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Regardless of how the Parental Agent detected changes to a CDS/
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    CDNSKEY RRset, the Parental Agent SHOULD use a DNSSEC validator to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    obtain a validated CDS/CDNSKEY RRset from the Child zone.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: A NOT
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    RECOMMENDED exception to this is if the Parent performs some
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    additional validation on the data to confirm that it is the "correct"
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    key.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Parental Agent MUST ensure that previous versions of the CDS/
    TEXT[!MUST]:    CDNSKEY RRset do not overwrite more recent versions.
    TEXT[!MAY]: This MAY be
    TEXT[!MAY]:    accomplished by checking that the signature inception in the Resource
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Record Signature (RRSIG) for CDS/CDNSKEY RRset is later and/or that
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the serial number on the Child's Start of Authority (SOA) is greater.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    The Parental Agent MAY take extra security measures.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Once the Parental Agent has obtained a valid CDS/CDNSKEY RRset it
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST check the publication rules from Section 4.1.
    TEXT[!MUST]: In particular,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the Parental Agent MUST check the Continuity rule and do its best not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to invalidate the Child zone.

  SECTION: [Security Considerations](#section-9)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    While it may be tempting, the techniques specified in this document
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD NOT be used for initial enrollment of keys since there is no
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    way to ensure that the initial key is the correct one.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If it is
    TEXT[!MUST]:    used, strict rules for inclusion of keys -- such as hold-down times,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    challenge data inclusion, or similar -- MUST be used along with some
    TEXT[!MUST]:    kind of challenge mechanism.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    As this introduces a new mechanism to update information in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Parent, it MUST be clear who is fetching the records and creating the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    appropriate records in the Parent zone.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Therefore, this mechanism
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD NOT be used to bypass intermediaries that might cache
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    information and, because of that, get the wrong state.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7477
  SECTION: [Definition of the CSYNC RRType](#section-2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: Child DNS operators
    TEXT[!MUST]:    wanting a parental agent to perform the synchronization steps
    TEXT[!MUST]:    outlined in this document MUST publish a CSYNC record at the apex of
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the child zone.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Parental agent implementations MAY choose to query
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Parental agents MUST process the entire set of child data indicated
    TEXT[!MUST]:    by the Type Bit Map field (i.e., all record types indicated along
    TEXT[!MUST]:    with all of the necessary records to support processing of that type)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    or else parental agents MUST NOT make any changes to parental records
    TEXT[!MUST]:    at all.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Errors due to unsupported Type Bit Map bits, or otherwise
    TEXT[!MUST]:    nonpunishable data, SHALL result in no change to the parent zone's
    TEXT[!MUST]:    delegation information for the child.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Parental agents MUST ignore a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    child's CSYNC RDATA set if multiple CSYNC resource records are found;
    TEXT[!MUST]:    only a single CSYNC record should ever be present.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The parental agent MUST perform DNSSEC validation ([RFC4033]
    TEXT[!MUST]:    [RFC4034] [RFC4035]), of the CSYNC RRType data and MUST perform
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNSSEC validation of any data to be copied from the child to the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    parent.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Parents MUST NOT process any data from any of these records
    TEXT[!MUST]:    if any of the validation results indicate anything other than
    TEXT[!MUST]:    "Secure" [RFC4034] or if any the required data cannot be successfully
    TEXT[!MUST]:    retrieved.

  SECTION: [The SOA Serial Field](#section-2.1.1.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the soaminimum flag is set, parental agents
    TEXT[!MUST]:    querying children's authoritative servers MUST NOT act on data from
    TEXT[!MUST]:    zones advertising an SOA serial number less than this value.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    soaminimum flag is not set, parental agents MUST ignore the value in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the SOA Serial field.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: A child SHOULD update
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the SOA Serial field in the CSYNC record every time the data being
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    referenced by the CSYNC record is changed (e.g., an NS record or
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    associated address record is changed).
    TEXT[!MAY]: A child MAY choose to update
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the SOA Serial field to always match the current SOA Serial field.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Parental agents MAY cache SOA serial numbers from data they use and
    TEXT[!MAY]:    refuse to process data from zones older than the last instance from
    TEXT[!MAY]:    which they pulled data.

  SECTION: [The Flags Field](#section-2.1.1.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Undefined flags MUST be set to 0 by CSYNC publishers.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Parental
    TEXT[!MUST]:    agents MUST NOT process a CSYNC record if it contains a 1 value for a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    flag that is unknown to or unsupported by the parental agent.

  SECTION: [The Type Bit Map Field](#section-2.1.1.2.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: If
    TEXT[!MUST]:    a bit has been set that a parental agent implementation does not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    understand, the parental agent MUST NOT act upon the record.

  SECTION: [The CSYNC Presentation Format](#section-2.1.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: When the mnemonic is not known, the TYPE
    TEXT[!MUST]:       representation described in [RFC3597], Section 5, MUST be used.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       Implementations that support parsing of presentation format
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       records SHOULD be able to read and understand these TYPE
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       representations as well.

  SECTION: [CSYNC Data Processing](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: If a parental agent fails to successfully
    TEXT[!MUST]:    query for any of the required records, the whole operation MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    aborted.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Parental agents MAY:
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the "immediate" flag is not set, the parental agent MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:       NOT act until the zone administrator approves the operation
    TEXT[!MUST]:       through an out-of-band mechanism (such as through pushing a button
    TEXT[!MUST]:       via a web interface).

  SECTION: [Processing Procedure](#section-3.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The following shows a sequence of steps that SHOULD be used when
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    collecting and processing CSYNC records from a child zone.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: To ensure a single
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    host is being addressed, DNS over TCP SHOULD be used to avoid
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    conversing with multiple nodes at an anycast address.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Because
    TEXT[!MAY]:           of the additional operational complexity, parental agents MAY
    TEXT[!MAY]:           choose not to support this protocol with children making use
    TEXT[!MAY]:           of records that are authoritative in the grandchildren.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If the SOA records from the first, middle, and last steps for a given
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    zone have different serial numbers (for example, because the zone was
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    edited and republished during the interval between steps 1 and 4),
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    then the CSYNC record obtained in the second set SHOULD NOT be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    processed (rapidly changing child zones may need special
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    consideration or processing).
    TEXT[!MAY]: The operation MAY be restarted or
    TEXT[!MAY]:    retried in the future.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the soaminimum flag is set and the SOA serial numbers are equal
    TEXT[!MUST]:    but less than the CSYNC record's SOA Serial field [RFC1982], the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    record MUST NOT be processed.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If state is being kept by the parental
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    agent and the SOA serial number is less than the last time a CSYNC
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    record was processed, this CSYNC record SHOULD NOT be processed.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Similarly, if state is being kept by the parental agent and the SOA
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Serial field of the CSYNC record is less than the SOA Serial field of
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the CSYNC record from last time, then this CSYNC record SHOULD NOT be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    processed.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If a failure of any kind occurs while trying to obtain any of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    required data, or if DNSSEC fails to validate all of the data
    TEXT[!MUST]:    returned for these queries as "secure", then this CSYNC record MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NOT be processed.

  SECTION: [The NS type](#section-3.2.1)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    NS records found within the child's zone should be copied verbatim
    TEXT[!MAY]:    (with the exception of the Time to Live (TTL) field, for which the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    parent MAY want to select a different value) and the result published
    TEXT[!MAY]:    within the parent zone should be a set of NS records that match
    TEXT[!MAY]:    exactly.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Parental agents MAY refuse to perform NS updates if the replacement
    TEXT[!MAY]:    records fail to meet NS record policies required by the parent zone
    TEXT[!MAY]:    (e.g., "every child zone must have at least two NS records").
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Parental agents MUST NOT perform NS updates if there are no NS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    records returned in a query, as verified by DNSSEC denial-of-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    existence protection.

  SECTION: [The A and AAAA Types](#section-3.2.2)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    The A and AAAA type flags indicates that the A and AAAA address glue
    TEXT[!MAY]:    records for in-bailiwick NS records within the child zone should be
    TEXT[!MAY]:    copied verbatim (with the exception of the TTL field, for which the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    parent MAY want to select a different value) into the parent's
    TEXT[!MAY]:    delegation information.
    TEXT[!MUST]: However, if
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the end result of processing would leave no glue records present in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the parent zone for any of the of the in-bailiwick NS records, then
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the parent MUST NOT update the glue address records.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The procedure for querying for A and AAAA records MUST occur after
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the procedure, if required, for querying for NS records as defined in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Section 3.2.1.

  SECTION: [Child Nameserver Selection](#section-4.2)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Parental agents MAY perform best-possible verification by querying
    TEXT[!MAY]:    all NS records for available data to determine which has the most
    TEXT[!MAY]:    recent SOA and CSYNC version (in an ideal world, they would all be
    TEXT[!MAY]:    equal, but this is not possible in practice due to synchronization
    TEXT[!MAY]:    delays and transfer failures).

  SECTION: [Out-of-Bailiwick NS Records](#section-4.3)
    TEXT[!MAY]: Thus, the child DNS
    TEXT[!MAY]:    operator MAY indicate that the NS records should be synchronized, and
    TEXT[!MAY]:    MAY set any glue record flags (A, AAAA) as well, but the parent will
    TEXT[!MAY]:    only update those glue records that are below the child's delegation
    TEXT[!MAY]:    point.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Children deploying NS records pointing to domain names within their
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    own children (the "grandchildren") SHOULD ensure the grandchildren's
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    associated glue records are properly set before publishing the CSYNC
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    record.

  SECTION: [Documented Parental Agent Type Support](#section-4.4)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Parental agents that support processing CSYNC records SHOULD publicly
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    document the following minimum processing characteristics:

  SECTION: [Removal of the CSYNC Records](#section-4.5)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Children MAY remove the CSYNC record upon noticing that the parent
    TEXT[!MAY]:    zone has published the required records, thus eliminating the need
    TEXT[!MAY]:    for the parent to continually query for the CSYNC record and all
    TEXT[!MAY]:    corresponding records.

  SECTION: [Security Considerations](#section-5)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Parental agents implementing CSYNC processing MUST ensure all DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    transactions are validated by DNSSEC as "secure".
    TEXT[!MUST]: Clients deploying
    TEXT[!MUST]:    CSYNC MUST ensure their zones are signed, current and properly linked
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to the parent zone with a DS record that points to an appropriate
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNSKEY of the child's zone.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Thus, implementations of this protocol
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST NOT use it to synchronize DS records, DNSKEY materials, CDS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    records, CDNSKEY records, or CSYNC records.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Similarly, future
    TEXT[!MUST]:    documents extending this protocol MUST NOT offer the ability to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    synchronize DS, DNSKEY materials, CDS records, CDNSKEY records, or
    TEXT[!MUST]:    CSYNC records.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    To ensure that an older CSYNC record making use of the soaminimum
    TEXT[!MUST]:    flag cannot be replayed to revert values, the SOA serial number MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NOT be incremented by more than 2^16 during the lifetime of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    signature window of the associated RRSIGs signing the SOA and CSYNC
    TEXT[!MUST]:    records.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7686
  SECTION: [The ".onion" Special-Use Domain Name](#section-2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: Application Software: Applications (including proxies) that
    TEXT[!MUST]:        implement the Tor protocol MUST recognize .onion names as special
    TEXT[!MUST]:        by either accessing them directly or using a proxy (e.g., SOCKS
    TEXT[!MUST]:        [RFC1928]) to do so.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Applications that do not implement the Tor
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        protocol SHOULD generate an error upon the use of .onion and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        SHOULD NOT perform a DNS lookup.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Name Resolution APIs and Libraries: Resolvers MUST either respond
    TEXT[!MUST]:        to requests for .onion names by resolving them according to
    TEXT[!MUST]:        [tor-rendezvous] or by responding with NXDOMAIN [RFC1035].
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Caching DNS Servers: Caching servers, where not explicitly
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        adapted to interoperate with Tor, SHOULD NOT attempt to look up
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:        records for .onion names.
    TEXT[!MUST]: They MUST generate NXDOMAIN for all
    TEXT[!MUST]:        such queries.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Authoritative DNS Servers: Authoritative servers MUST respond to
    TEXT[!MUST]:        queries for .onion with NXDOMAIN.
    TEXT[!MUST]: DNS Server Operators: Operators MUST NOT configure an
    TEXT[!MUST]:        authoritative DNS server to answer queries for .onion.
    TEXT[!MUST]: DNS Registries/Registrars: Registrars MUST NOT register .onion
    TEXT[!MUST]:        names; all such requests MUST be denied.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7766
  SECTION: [Introduction](#section-1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       DNS resolvers and recursive servers MUST support UDP, and SHOULD
    TEXT[!MUST]:       support TCP, for sending (non-zone-transfer) queries.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    This document therefore updates the core DNS protocol specifications
    TEXT[!MUST]:    such that support for TCP is henceforth a REQUIRED part of a full DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    protocol implementation.

  SECTION: [Transport Protocol Selection](#section-5)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Section 6.1.3.2 of [RFC1123] is updated: All general-purpose DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    implementations MUST support both UDP and TCP transport.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  Authoritative server implementations MUST support TCP so that they
    TEXT[!MUST]:       do not limit the size of responses to what fits in a single UDP
    TEXT[!MUST]:       packet.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  Recursive server (or forwarder) implementations MUST support TCP
    TEXT[!MUST]:       so that they do not prevent large responses from a TCP-capable
    TEXT[!MUST]:       server from reaching its TCP-capable clients.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  Stub resolver implementations (e.g., an operating system's DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:       resolution library) MUST support TCP since to do otherwise would
    TEXT[!MUST]:       limit the interoperability between their own clients and upstream
    TEXT[!MUST]:       servers.
    TEXT[!MUST]: a DNS resolver or server that is sending a non-zone-transfer
    TEXT[!MUST]:       query MUST send a UDP query first.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Stub resolvers and recursive
    TEXT[!MAY]:    resolvers MAY elect to send either TCP or UDP queries depending on
    TEXT[!MAY]:    local operational reasons.
    TEXT[!MAY]: TCP MAY be used before sending any UDP
    TEXT[!MAY]:    queries.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If the resolver already has an open TCP connection to the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    server, it SHOULD reuse this connection.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In addition, it is noted that all recursive and authoritative servers
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST send responses using the same transport as the query arrived on.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In the case of TCP, this MUST also be the same connection.

  SECTION: [Connection Reuse](#section-6.2.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: To amortise connection
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    setup costs, both clients and servers SHOULD support connection reuse
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    by sending multiple queries and responses over a single persistent
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    TCP connection.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When sending multiple queries over a TCP connection, clients MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    reuse the DNS Message ID of an in-flight query on that connection in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    order to avoid Message ID collisions.

  SECTION: [Query Pipelining](#section-6.2.1.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In order to achieve performance on par with UDP, DNS clients SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    pipeline their queries.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: When a DNS client sends multiple queries to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    a server, it SHOULD NOT wait for an outstanding reply before sending
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the next query.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Clients SHOULD treat TCP and UDP equivalently when
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    considering the time at which to send a particular query.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNS servers (especially recursive) MUST expect to receive pipelined
    TEXT[!MUST]:    queries.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The server SHOULD process TCP queries concurrently, just as
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    it would for UDP.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The server SHOULD answer all pipelined queries,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    even if they are received in quick succession.

  SECTION: [Concurrent Connections](#section-6.2.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    To mitigate the risk of unintentional server overload, DNS clients
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST take care to minimize the number of concurrent TCP connections
    TEXT[!MUST]:    made to any individual server.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: It is RECOMMENDED that for any given
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    client/server interaction there SHOULD be no more than one connection
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    for regular queries, one for zone transfers, and one for each
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    protocol that is being used on top of TCP (for example, if the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    resolver was using TLS).
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Similarly, servers MAY impose limits on the number of concurrent TCP
    TEXT[!MAY]:    connections being handled for any particular client IP address or
    TEXT[!MAY]:    subnet.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: These limits SHOULD be much looser than the client
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    guidelines above, because the server does not know, for example, if a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    client IP address belongs to a single client, is multiple resolvers
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    on a single machine, or is multiple clients behind a device
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    performing Network Address Translation (NAT).

  SECTION: [Idle Timeouts](#section-6.2.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    To mitigate the risk of unintentional server overload, DNS clients
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST take care to minimise the idle time of established DNS-over-TCP
    TEXT[!MUST]:    sessions made to any individual server.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: DNS clients SHOULD close the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    TCP connection of an idle session, unless an idle timeout has been
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    established using some other signalling mechanism, for example,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    [edns-tcp-keepalive].
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    To mitigate the risk of unintentional server overload, it is
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    RECOMMENDED that the default server application-level idle period be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    on the order of seconds, but no particular value is specified.
    TEXT[!MAY]: In
    TEXT[!MAY]:    practice, the idle period can vary dynamically, and servers MAY allow
    TEXT[!MAY]:    idle connections to remain open for longer periods as resources
    TEXT[!MAY]:    permit.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Servers MAY use zero timeouts when they are
    TEXT[!MAY]:    experiencing heavy load or are under attack.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: For this
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    reason, servers SHOULD reset the idle timeout on the receipt of a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    full DNS message, rather than on receipt of any part of a DNS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    message.

  SECTION: [Teardown](#section-6.2.4)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DNS clients SHOULD retry unanswered queries if the connection closes
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    before receiving all outstanding responses.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If a DNS server finds that a DNS client has closed a TCP session (or
    TEXT[!MUST]:    if the session has been otherwise interrupted) before all pending
    TEXT[!MUST]:    responses have been sent, then the server MUST NOT attempt to send
    TEXT[!MUST]:    those responses.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Of course, the DNS server MAY cache those
    TEXT[!MAY]:    responses.

  SECTION: [Response Reordering](#section-7)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Authoritative servers and recursive resolvers are RECOMMENDED to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    support the preparing of responses in parallel and sending them out
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    of order, regardless of the transport protocol in use.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Stub and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    recursive resolvers MUST be able to process responses that arrive in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    a different order than that in which the requests were sent,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    regardless of the transport protocol in use.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In order to achieve performance on par with UDP, recursive resolvers
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD process TCP queries in parallel and return individual
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    responses as soon as they are available, possibly out of order.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Since pipelined responses can arrive out of order, clients MUST match
    TEXT[!MUST]:    responses to outstanding queries on the same TCP connection using the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Message ID.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the response contains a question section, the client
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST match the QNAME, QCLASS, and QTYPE fields.

  SECTION: [TCP Message Length Field](#section-8)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DNS clients and servers SHOULD pass the two-octet length field, and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the message described by that length field, to the TCP layer at the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    same time (e.g., in a single "write" system call) to make it more
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    likely that all the data will be transmitted in a single TCP segment.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    To clarify, DNS servers MUST NOT close a connection simply because
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the first "read" from the TCP layer does not contain the entire DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    message, and servers SHOULD apply the connection timeouts as
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specified in Section 6.2.3.

  SECTION: [Changes to RFC 5966](#appendix-B)
    TEXT[!MAY]: TCP MAY be used before sending any UDP queries.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Section 6.2.1 adds a new recommendation that TCP connection
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:         reuse SHOULD be supported.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Section 6.2.1.1 adds a new recommendation that DNS clients
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:         SHOULD pipeline their queries and DNS servers SHOULD process
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:         pipelined queries concurrently.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Section 6.2.3 adds a new recommendation that DNS clients SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:         close idle sessions unless using a signalling mechanism.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Section 7 clarifies that servers are RECOMMENDED to prepare TCP
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:         responses in parallel and send answers out of order.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7828
  SECTION: [Sending Queries](#section-3.2.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNS clients MUST NOT include the edns-tcp-keepalive option in queries
    TEXT[!MUST]:    sent using UDP transport.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    DNS clients MAY include the edns-tcp-keepalive option in the first
    TEXT[!MAY]:    query sent to a server using TCP transport to signal their desire to
    TEXT[!MAY]:    keep the connection open when idle.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    DNS clients MAY include the edns-tcp-keepalive option in subsequent
    TEXT[!MAY]:    queries sent to a server using TCP transport to signal their
    TEXT[!MAY]:    continued desire to keep the connection open when idle.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Clients MUST specify an OPTION-LENGTH of 0 and omit the TIMEOUT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    value.

  SECTION: [Receiving Responses](#section-3.2.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A DNS client that receives a response using UDP transport that
    TEXT[!MUST]:    includes the edns-tcp-keepalive option MUST ignore the option.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    A DNS client that receives a response using TCP transport that
    TEXT[!MAY]:    includes the edns-tcp-keepalive option MAY keep the existing TCP
    TEXT[!MAY]:    session open when it is idle.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: It SHOULD honour the timeout received
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    in that response (overriding any previous timeout) and initiate close
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    of the connection before the timeout expires.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A DNS client that receives a response that includes the edns-tcp-
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    keepalive option with a TIMEOUT value of 0 SHOULD send no more
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    queries on that connection and initiate closing the connection as
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    soon as it has received all outstanding responses.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A DNS client that sent a query containing the edns-keepalive-option
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    but receives a response that does not contain the edns-keepalive-
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    option SHOULD assume the server does not support keepalive and behave
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    following the guidance in [RFC7766].

  SECTION: [Receiving Queries](#section-3.3.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A DNS server that receives a query using UDP transport that includes
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the edns-tcp-keepalive option MUST ignore the option.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    A DNS server that receives a query using TCP transport that includes
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the edns-tcp-keepalive option MAY modify the local idle timeout
    TEXT[!MAY]:    associated with that TCP session if resources permit.

  SECTION: [Sending Responses](#section-3.3.2)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    A DNS server that receives a query sent using TCP transport that
    TEXT[!MAY]:    includes an OPT RR (with or without the edns-tcp-keepalive option)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    MAY include the edns-tcp-keepalive option in the response to signal
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the expected idle timeout on a connection.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Servers MUST specify the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    TIMEOUT value that is currently associated with the TCP session.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The DNS server SHOULD send an edns-tcp-keepalive option
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    with a timeout of 0 if it deems its local resources are too low to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    service more TCP keepalive sessions or if it wants clients to close
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    currently open connections.

  SECTION: [TCP Session Management](#section-3.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       Lack of presence of an OPT record in a request MUST be taken as an
    TEXT[!MUST]:       indication that the requestor does not implement any part of this
    TEXT[!MUST]:       specification and that the responder MUST NOT include an OPT
    TEXT[!MUST]:       record in its response.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If a client includes the edns-tcp-keepalive option in the first
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    query, it SHOULD include an EDNS0 OPT RR periodically in any further
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    messages it sends during the TCP session.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    DNS clients and servers MAY close a TCP session at any time in order
    TEXT[!MAY]:    to manage local resource constraints.

  SECTION: [Non-clean Paths](#section-3.5)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: A fallback
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    strategy similar to that described in [RFC6891], Section 6.2.2 SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    be employed to avoid persistent interference due to non-clean paths.

  SECTION: [Intermediary Considerations](#section-4)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    It is RECOMMENDED that DNS intermediaries that terminate TCP
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    connections implement edns-tcp-keepalive.

  SECTION: [Security Considerations](#section-5)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: When a DNS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    server detects abusive behaviour, it SHOULD immediately close the TCP
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    connection and free the resources used.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7830
  SECTION: [The "Padding" Option](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The
    TEXT[!MUST]:    "Padding" option MUST occur at most, once per OPT meta-RR (and hence,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    at most once per message).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The PADDING octets SHOULD be set to 0x00.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Other values MAY be used,
    TEXT[!MAY]:    for example, in cases where there is a concern that the padded
    TEXT[!MAY]:    message could be subject to compression before encryption.
    TEXT[!MUST]: PADDING
    TEXT[!MUST]:    octets of any value MUST be accepted in the messages received.

  SECTION: [Usage Considerations](#section-4)
    TEXT[!MUST]: However, padded DNS messages MUST NOT exceed the number of
    TEXT[!MUST]:    octets specified in the Requestor's Payload Size field encoded in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RR Class Field (see Sections 6.2.3 and 6.2.4 of [RFC6891]).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Responders MUST pad DNS responses when the respective DNS query
    TEXT[!MUST]:    included the "Padding" option, unless doing so would violate the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    maximum UDP payload size.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Responders MAY pad DNS responses when the respective DNS query
    TEXT[!MAY]:    indicated EDNS(0) support of the Requestor and the "Padding" option
    TEXT[!MAY]:    was not included.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Responders MUST NOT pad DNS responses when the respective DNS query
    TEXT[!MUST]:    did not indicate EDNS(0) support.

  SECTION: [Security Considerations](#section-6)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Therefore, implementations MUST NOT use this option if the DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    transport is not encrypted.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Therefore (as described in Section 3.3 of [RFC7525]), implementations
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    and deployments SHOULD disable compression at the Transport Layer
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Security (TLS) level.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7858
  SECTION: [Session Initiation](#section-3.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    By default, a DNS server that supports DNS over TLS MUST listen for
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and accept TCP connections on port 853, unless it has mutual
    TEXT[!MUST]:    agreement with its clients to use a port other than 853 for DNS over
    TEXT[!MUST]:    TLS.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    By default, a DNS client desiring privacy from DNS over TLS from a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    particular server MUST establish a TCP connection to port 853 on the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    server, unless it has mutual agreement with its server to use a port
    TEXT[!MUST]:    other than port 853 for DNS over TLS.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Such another port MUST NOT be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    port 53 but MAY be from the "first-come, first-served" port range.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The first data exchange on this TCP
    TEXT[!MUST]:    connection MUST be the client and server initiating a TLS handshake
    TEXT[!MUST]:    using the procedure described in [RFC5246].
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNS clients and servers MUST NOT use port 853 to transport cleartext
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNS messages.
    TEXT[!MUST]: DNS clients MUST NOT send and DNS servers MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    respond to cleartext DNS messages on any port used for DNS over TLS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (including, for example, after a failed TLS handshake).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DNS clients SHOULD remember server IP addresses that don't support
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DNS over TLS, including timeouts, connection refusals, and TLS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    handshake failures, and not request DNS over TLS from them for a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    reasonable period (such as one hour per server).
    TEXT[!MAY]: DNS clients
    TEXT[!MAY]:    following an out-of-band key-pinned privacy profile (Section 4.2) MAY
    TEXT[!MAY]:    be more aggressive about retrying DNS-over-TLS connection failures.

  SECTION: [Transmitting and Receiving Messages](#section-3.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    All messages (requests and responses) in the established TLS session
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST use the two-octet length field described in Section 4.2.2 of
    TEXT[!MUST]:    [RFC1035].
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: For reasons of efficiency, DNS clients and servers SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    pass the two-octet length field, and the message described by that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    length field, to the TCP layer at the same time (e.g., in a single
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    "write" system call) to make it more likely that all the data will be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    transmitted in a single TCP segment ([RFC7766], Section 8).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In order to minimize latency, clients SHOULD pipeline multiple
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    queries over a TLS session.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Since pipelined responses can arrive out of order, clients MUST match
    TEXT[!MUST]:    responses to outstanding queries on the same TLS connection using the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Message ID.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the response contains a Question Section, the client
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST match the QNAME, QCLASS, and QTYPE fields.

  SECTION: [Connection Reuse, Close, and Reestablishment](#section-3.4)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: To avoid excess TCP
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    connections, each with a single query, clients SHOULD reuse a single
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    TCP connection to the recursive resolver.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In order to amortize TCP and TLS connection setup costs, clients and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    servers SHOULD NOT immediately close a connection after each
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    response.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Instead, clients and servers SHOULD reuse existing
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    connections for subsequent queries as long as they have sufficient
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    resources.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: An implementor of DNS over
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    TLS SHOULD follow best practices for DNS over TCP, as described in
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    [RFC7766].
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Clients and servers that keep idle connections open MUST be robust to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    termination of idle connection by either party.
    TEXT[!MAY]: As with current DNS
    TEXT[!MAY]:    over TCP, DNS servers MAY close the connection at any time (perhaps
    TEXT[!MAY]:    due to resource constraints).
    TEXT[!MUST]: As with current DNS over TCP, clients
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST handle abrupt closes and be prepared to reestablish connections
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and/or retry queries.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Underlining the requirement for sending only encrypted DNS data on a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNS-over-TLS port (Section 3.2), when using TCP Fast Open, the client
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and server MUST immediately initiate or resume a TLS handshake
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (cleartext DNS MUST NOT be exchanged).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: DNS servers SHOULD enable
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    fast TLS session resumption [RFC5077], and this SHOULD be used when
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    reestablishing connections.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    When closing a connection, DNS servers SHOULD use the TLS close-
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    notify request to shift TCP TIME-WAIT state to the clients.

  SECTION: [Out-of-Band Key-Pinned Privacy Profile](#section-4.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: With this out-of-band key-pinned privacy profile, client
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    administrators SHOULD deploy a backup pin along with the primary pin,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    for the reasons explained in [RFC7469].
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: After a change of keys on the server, an updated pin
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    set SHOULD be distributed to all clients in some secure way in
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    preparation for future key rollover.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Techniques such as those
    TEXT[!MAY]:    used by DNSSEC-trigger [DNSSEC-TRIGGER] MAY be used during network
    TEXT[!MAY]:    configuration, with the intent to transition to the designated DNS
    TEXT[!MAY]:    provider after authentication.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The user MUST be alerted whenever
    TEXT[!MUST]:    possible that the DNS is not private during such bootstrap.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Otherwise, the client MUST treat the SPKI validation failure as a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    non-recoverable error.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Implementations of this privacy profile MUST support the calculation
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of a fingerprint as the SHA-256 [RFC6234] hash of the DER-encoded
    TEXT[!MUST]:    ASN.1 representation of the SPKI of an X.509 certificate.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Implementations MUST support the representation of a SHA-256
    TEXT[!MUST]:    fingerprint as a base64-encoded character string [RFC4648].
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Additional fingerprint types MAY also be supported.

  SECTION: [Performance Considerations](#section-5)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Number of connections:  To minimize state on DNS servers and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       connection startup time, clients SHOULD minimize the creation of
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       new TCP connections.

  SECTION: [Security Considerations](#section-8)
    TEXT[!MUST]: Clients and servers MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:        adhere to the TLS implementation recommendations and security
    TEXT[!MUST]:        considerations of [BCP195].
    TEXT[!MAY]: For this reason, clients MAY

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7871
  SECTION: [Option Format](#section-6)
    TEXT[!MUST]:       In queries, it MUST be set to 0.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  ADDRESS, variable number of octets, contains either an IPv4 or
    TEXT[!MUST]:       IPv6 address, depending on FAMILY, which MUST be truncated to the
    TEXT[!MUST]:       number of bits indicated by the SOURCE PREFIX-LENGTH field,
    TEXT[!MUST]:       padding with 0 bits to pad to the end of the last octet needed.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    o  A server receiving an ECS option that uses either too few or too
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       many ADDRESS octets, or that has non-zero ADDRESS bits set beyond
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       SOURCE PREFIX-LENGTH, SHOULD return FORMERR to reject the packet,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       as a signal to the software developer making the request to fix
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       their implementation.

  SECTION: [Recursive Resolvers](#section-7.1.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: For
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    privacy reasons, and because the whole IP address is rarely required
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    to determine a tailored response, this length SHOULD be shorter than
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the full address, as described in Section 11.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the triggering query included an ECS option itself, it MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    examined for its SOURCE PREFIX-LENGTH.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The Recursive Resolver's
    TEXT[!MUST]:    outgoing query MUST then set SOURCE PREFIX-LENGTH to the shorter of
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the incoming query's SOURCE PREFIX-LENGTH or the server's maximum
    TEXT[!MUST]:    cacheable prefix length.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The total
    TEXT[!MUST]:    number of octets used MUST only be enough to cover SOURCE PREFIX-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    LENGTH bits, rather than the full width that would normally be used
    TEXT[!MUST]:    by addresses in FAMILY.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    FAMILY and ADDRESS information MAY be used from the ECS option in the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    incoming query.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the Recursive Resolver will not forward FAMILY and ADDRESS data from
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the incoming ECS option, it SHOULD return a REFUSED response.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Subsequent queries to refresh the data MUST, if unrestricted by an
    TEXT[!MUST]:    incoming SOURCE PREFIX-LENGTH, specify the longest SOURCE PREFIX-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    LENGTH that the Recursive Resolver is willing to cache, even if a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    previous response indicated that a shorter prefix length was
    TEXT[!MUST]:    sufficient.

  SECTION: [Stub Resolvers](#section-7.1.2)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    A Stub Resolver MAY generate DNS queries with an ECS option that sets
    TEXT[!MAY]:    SOURCE PREFIX-LENGTH to limit how network information should be
    TEXT[!MAY]:    revealed.
    TEXT[!MUST]: An Intermediate Nameserver that receives such a query MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NOT make queries that include more bits of client address than in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    originating query.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A SOURCE PREFIX-LENGTH value of 0 means that the Recursive Resolver
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST NOT add the client's address information to its queries.
    TEXT[!MAY]: The
    TEXT[!MAY]:    subsequent Recursive Resolver query to the Authoritative Nameserver
    TEXT[!MAY]:    will then either not include an ECS option or MAY optionally include
    TEXT[!MAY]:    its own address information, which is what the Authoritative
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Nameserver will almost certainly use to generate any Tailored
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Response in lieu of an option.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A Stub Resolver MUST set SCOPE PREFIX-LENGTH to 0.
    TEXT[!MAY]: It MAY include
    TEXT[!MAY]:    FAMILY and ADDRESS data, but should be prepared to handle a REFUSED
    TEXT[!MAY]:    response if the Intermediate Nameserver that it queries has a policy
    TEXT[!MAY]:    that denies forwarding of ADDRESS.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If there is no ADDRESS set, i.e.,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SOURCE PREFIX-LENGTH is set to 0, then FAMILY SHOULD be set to the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    transport over which the query is sent.

  SECTION: [Forwarding Resolvers](#section-7.1.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: A Forwarding
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Resolver using this option MUST prepare it as described in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Section 7.1.1, "Recursive Resolvers".
    TEXT[!MUST]: In particular, a Forwarding
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Resolver that implements this protocol MUST honor SOURCE PREFIX-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    LENGTH restrictions indicated in the incoming query from its client.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the Forwarding Resolver receives a REFUSED response when it sends
    TEXT[!MUST]:    a query that includes a non-zero ADDRESS, it MUST retry with no
    TEXT[!MUST]:    ADDRESS.

  SECTION: [Authoritative Nameserver](#section-7.2.1)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    When a query containing an ECS option is received, an Authoritative
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Nameserver supporting ECS MAY use the address information specified
    TEXT[!MAY]:    in the option to generate a tailored response.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Such a server MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    include an ECS option within replies to indicate lack of support for
    TEXT[!MUST]:    it.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A query with a wrongly formatted option (e.g., an unknown FAMILY)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST be rejected and a FORMERR response MUST be returned to the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    sender, as described in [RFC6891], "Transport Considerations".
    TEXT[!MUST]:    An Authoritative Nameserver that implements this protocol and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    receives an ECS option MUST include an ECS option in its response to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    indicate that it SHOULD be cached accordingly, regardless of whether
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the client information was needed to formulate an answer.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the requirement in [RFC6891] to reserve space for the OPT record
    TEXT[!MUST]:    could mean that the Answer section of the response will be truncated
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and fall back to TCP indicated accordingly.)  If an ECS option was
    TEXT[!MUST]:    not included in a query, one MUST NOT be included in the response
    TEXT[!MUST]:    even if the server is providing a Tailored Response -- presumably
    TEXT[!MUST]:    based on the address from which it received the query.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    FAMILY, SOURCE PREFIX-LENGTH, and ADDRESS in the response MUST match
    TEXT[!MUST]:    those in the query.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Future queries for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the name within the specified network SHOULD use the longer SCOPE
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    PREFIX-LENGTH.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    response SHOULD therefore, include the longest relevant PREFIX-LENGTH
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    of any RRset in the answer, which could have the unfortunate side
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    effect of redundantly caching some data that could be cached more
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    broadly.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: For the specific case of a Canonical Name (CNAME) chain,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the Authoritative Nameserver SHOULD only place the initial CNAME
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    record in the Answer section, to have it cached unambiguously and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    appropriately.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Because it can't be guaranteed that queries for all
    TEXT[!MUST]:    longer prefix lengths would arrive before one that would be answered
    TEXT[!MUST]:    by the shorter prefix length, an Authoritative Nameserver MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    overlap prefixes.

  SECTION: [Intermediate Nameserver](#section-7.2.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: Because a client that did not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    use an ECS option might not be able to understand it, the server MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the client query did include the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    option, the server MUST include one in its response, especially as it
    TEXT[!MUST]:    could be talking to a Forwarding Resolver, which would need the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    information for its own caching.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If an Intermediate Nameserver receives a response that has a longer
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SCOPE PREFIX-LENGTH than SOURCE PREFIX-LENGTH that it provided in its
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    query, it SHOULD still provide the result as the answer to the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    triggering client request even if the client is in a different
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    address range.
    TEXT[!MAY]: The Intermediate Nameserver MAY instead opt to retry
    TEXT[!MAY]:    with a longer SOURCE PREFIX-LENGTH to get a better reply before
    TEXT[!MAY]:    responding to its client, as long as it does not exceed a SOURCE
    TEXT[!MAY]:    PREFIX-LENGTH specified in the query that triggered resolution, but
    TEXT[!MAY]:    this obviously has implications for the latency of the overall
    TEXT[!MAY]:    lookup.

  SECTION: [Handling ECS Responses and Caching](#section-7.3)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    When an Intermediate Nameserver receives a response containing an ECS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    option and without the TC bit set, it SHOULD cache the result based
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    on the data in the option.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If the TC bit was set, the Intermediate
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Resolver SHOULD retry the query over TCP to get the complete Answer
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    section for caching.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If FAMILY, SOURCE PREFIX-LENGTH, and SOURCE PREFIX-LENGTH bits of
    TEXT[!MUST]:    ADDRESS in the response don't match the non-zero fields in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    corresponding query, the full response MUST be dropped, as described
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in Section 11.
    TEXT[!MUST]: In a response to a query that specified only SOURCE
    TEXT[!MUST]:    PREFIX-LENGTH for privacy masking, the FAMILY and ADDRESS fields MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    contain the appropriate non-zero information that the Authoritative
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Nameserver used to generate the answer, so that it can be cached
    TEXT[!MUST]:    accordingly.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If no ECS option is contained in the response, the Intermediate
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Nameserver SHOULD treat this as being equivalent to having received a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SCOPE PREFIX-LENGTH of 0, which is an answer suitable for all client
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    addresses.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If a REFUSED response is received from an Authoritative Nameserver,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    an ECS-aware resolver MUST retry the query without ECS to distinguish
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the response from one where the Authoritative Nameserver is not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    responsible for the name, which is a common convention for the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    REFUSED status.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Similarly, a client of a Recursive Resolver SHOULD

  SECTION: [Caching the Response](#section-7.3.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In the cache, all resource records in the Answer section MUST be tied
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to the network specified in the response.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: A Resource
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Record Signature (RRSIG) must obviously be tied to the RRset that it
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    signs, but it is RECOMMENDED that all other DNSSEC records be scoped
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    at /0.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Any records from these
    TEXT[!MUST]:    sections MUST NOT be tied to a network.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Records that are cached as /0 because of a query's SOURCE PREFIX-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    LENGTH of 0 MUST be distinguished from those that are cached as /0
    TEXT[!MUST]:    because of a response's SCOPE PREFIX-LENGTH of 0.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Therefore,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    implementing full caching support as described in this section is
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    strongly RECOMMENDED.

  SECTION: [Answering from Cache](#section-7.3.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: Then, the appropriate RRset MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be chosen based on the longest prefix matching.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    o  If there was an ECS option with an ADDRESS, the ADDRESS from it
    TEXT[!MAY]:       MAY be used if the local policy allows.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If the policy does not allow it, a REFUSED response
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       SHOULD be sent.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If no matching network is found, the Intermediate Nameserver MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    perform resolution as usual.

  SECTION: [Delegations and Negative Answers](#section-7.4)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: It is RECOMMENDED that no specific behavior regarding
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    negative answers be relied upon, but that Authoritative Nameservers
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    should conservatively expect that Intermediate Nameservers will treat
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    all negative answers as /0; therefore, they SHOULD set SCOPE PREFIX-
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    LENGTH accordingly.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Addresses in the Additional
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    section SHOULD therefore ignore ECS data, and the Authoritative
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Nameserver SHOULD return a zero SCOPE PREFIX-LENGTH on delegations.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A Recursive Resolver SHOULD treat a non-zero SCOPE PREFIX LENGTH in a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    delegation as though it were zero.

  SECTION: [Transitivity](#section-7.5)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Any Intermediate Nameserver that forwards ECS options received from
    TEXT[!MUST]:    its clients MUST fully implement the caching behavior described in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Section 7.3.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    An Intermediate Nameserver MAY forward ECS options with address
    TEXT[!MAY]:    information.
    TEXT[!MAY]: This information MAY match the source IP address of the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    incoming query, and MAY have more or fewer address bits than the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    nameserver would normally include in a locally originated ECS option.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If an Intermediate Nameserver receives a query with SOURCE PREFIX-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    LENGTH set to 0, it MUST NOT include client address information in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    queries made to resolve that client's request (see Section 7.1.2).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If, for any reason, the Intermediate Nameserver does not want to use
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the information in an ECS option it receives (too little address
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    information, network address from a range not authorized to use the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    server, private/unroutable address space, etc.), it SHOULD drop the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    query and return a REFUSED response.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Note again that a query MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NOT be refused solely because it provides 0 address bits.

  SECTION: [DNSSEC Considerations](#section-9)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Most DNSSEC records SHOULD be scoped at /0, except for the RRSIG
    TEXT[!MUST]:    records, which MUST be tied to the RRset that they sign in a Tailored
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Response.

  SECTION: [NAT Considerations](#section-10)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The client's network address SHOULD NOT
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    be added, and existing ECS options, if present, SHOULD NOT be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    modified by NAT devices.
    TEXT[!MAY]: In such cases, the Intermediate Nameserver MAY use
    TEXT[!MAY]:    that information when originating ECS options.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In other cases, if a Recursive Resolver knows that it is situated
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    behind a NAT device, it SHOULD NOT originate ECS options with their
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    external IP address and instead rely on downstream Intermediate
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Nameservers to do so.
    TEXT[!MAY]: It MAY, however, choose to include the option
    TEXT[!MAY]:    with their internal address for the purposes of signaling its own
    TEXT[!MAY]:    limit for SOURCE PREFIX-LENGTH.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: As a general
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    guideline, if an Authoritative Nameserver on the publicly routed
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Internet receives a query that specifies an ADDRESS in [RFC1918] or
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    [RFC4193] private address space, it SHOULD ignore ADDRESS and look up
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    its answer based on the address of the Recursive Resolver.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: In the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    response, it SHOULD set SCOPE PREFIX-LENGTH to cover all of the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    relevant private space.
    TEXT[!MAY]: The Intermediate Nameserver MAY elect to cache the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    answer under one entry for special-purpose addresses [RFC6890]; see
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Section 11.3 of this document.

  SECTION: [Privacy](#section-11.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: In those cases, for optimal cache utilization and improved
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    privacy, the ISP's Recursive Resolver SHOULD truncate IP addresses in
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    this /20 to just 20 bits, instead of 24 as recommended above.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    As described in previous sections, this option will be forwarded
    TEXT[!MUST]:    across all the Recursive Resolvers supporting ECS, which MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    modify it to include the network address of the client.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Recursive
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Resolvers or Authoritative Nameservers MAY use the source IP address
    TEXT[!MAY]:    of queries to return a cached entry or to generate a Tailored
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Response that best matches the query.

  SECTION: [Birthday Attacks](#section-11.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    To counter this, the ECS option in a response packet MUST contain the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    full FAMILY, ADDRESS, and SOURCE PREFIX-LENGTH fields from the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    corresponding query.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Intermediate Nameservers processing a response
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST verify that these match, and they SHOULD discard the entire
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response if they do not.

  SECTION: [Cache Pollution](#section-11.3)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Due to the high cache
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       pressure introduced by ECS, the feature SHOULD be disabled in all
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       default configurations.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    o  Recursive Resolvers SHOULD limit the number of networks and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       answers they keep in the cache for any given query.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    o  Recursive Resolvers SHOULD limit the total number of different
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       networks that they keep in cache.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    o  Recursive Resolvers MUST NOT send an ECS option with SOURCE
    TEXT[!MUST]:       PREFIX-LENGTH providing more bits in ADDRESS than they are willing
    TEXT[!MUST]:       to cache responses for.
    TEXT[!MAY]:       Recursive Resolvers MAY, for example, decide to discard more-
    TEXT[!MAY]:       specific cache entries first.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: They SHOULD at least treat unroutable addresses, such
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       as some of the address blocks defined in [RFC6890], as equivalent
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       to the Recursive Resolver's own identity.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: They SHOULD ignore and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       never forward ECS options specifying other routable addresses that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       are known not to be served by the query source.

  SECTION: [Probing](#section-12.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: However, it is RECOMMENDED that resolvers remember which
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Authoritative Nameservers did not return the option with their
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    response and omit client address information from subsequent queries
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    to those nameservers.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Additionally, Recursive Resolvers SHOULD be configured never to send
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the option when querying root, top-level, and effective top-level
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    (i.e., "public suffix" [Public_Suffix_List]) domain servers.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Probing, if implemented, MUST be repeated periodically, e.g., daily.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Likewise, an Authoritative Nameserver that uses ECS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    information for one of its zones MUST indicate support for the option
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in all of its responses to ECS queries.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the option is supported
    TEXT[!MUST]:    but not actually used for generating a response, its SCOPE PREFIX-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    LENGTH MUST be set to 0.

  SECTION: [Whitelist](#section-12.2)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Implementations MAY also allow additional configuring of this based
    TEXT[!MAY]:    on other criteria, such as zone or query type.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8020
  SECTION: [Terminology](#section-1.1)
    TEXT[!MAY]: The implementation of a DNS resolver/cache MAY use a tree
    TEXT[!MAY]:    or other data structures.

  SECTION: [Rules](#section-2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    When an iterative caching DNS resolver receives an NXDOMAIN response,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    it SHOULD store it in its cache and then all names and resource
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    record sets (RRsets) at or below that node SHOULD be considered
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    unreachable.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Subsequent queries for such names SHOULD elicit an
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    NXDOMAIN response.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    But, if a resolver has cached data under the NXDOMAIN cut, it MAY
    TEXT[!MAY]:    continue to send it as a reply (until the TTL of this cached data
    TEXT[!MAY]:    expires), since this may avoid additional processing when a query is
    TEXT[!MAY]:    received.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Another exception is that a validating resolver MAY decide to
    TEXT[!MAY]:    implement the "NXDOMAIN cut" behavior (described in the first
    TEXT[!MAY]:    paragraph of this section) only when the NXDOMAIN response has been
    TEXT[!MAY]:    validated with DNSSEC.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The
    TEXT[!MUST]:    iterative, caching resolver MUST return these NSEC or NSEC3 records
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in the response to the triggering query if the query had the DNSSEC
    TEXT[!MUST]:    OK (DO) bit set.

  SECTION: [Implementation Considerations](#section-6)
    TEXT[!MUST]: So these rules use SHOULD and not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8078
  SECTION: [Accept Policy via Authenticated Channel](#section-3.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Parents SHOULD NOT refuse CDS/
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    CDNSKEY updates that do not (yet) have a matching DNSKEY in the child
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    zone.

  SECTION: [DNSSEC Delete Algorithm](#section-4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The contents of the CDS or CDNSKEY RRset MUST contain one RR and only
    TEXT[!MUST]:    contain the exact fields as shown below.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Once the parent has verified the CDS/CDNSKEY RRset and it has passed
    TEXT[!MUST]:    other acceptance tests, the parent MUST remove the DS RRset.

  SECTION: [Security Considerations](#section-5)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A parent SHOULD ensure that when it is allowing a child to become
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    securely delegated, it has a reasonable assurance that the CDS/
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    CDNSKEY RRset used to bootstrap the security is visible from a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    geographically and topologically diverse view.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: It SHOULD also ensure
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    that the zone validates correctly if the parent publishes the DS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    record.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8080
  SECTION: [Security Considerations](#section-8)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A private key used for a DNSSEC zone MUST NOT be used for any other
    TEXT[!MUST]:    purpose than for that zone.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8145
  SECTION: [Introduction](#section-1)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Each of these new signaling mechanisms is OPTIONAL to implement and
    TEXT[!MAY]:    use.

  SECTION: [Use by Queriers](#section-4.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The validating resolver SHOULD also set the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DNSSEC OK bit (also known as the DO bit) [RFC4035] to indicate that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    it wishes to receive DNSSEC RRs in the response.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A DNS client MUST NOT include the edns-key-tag option for non-DNSKEY
    TEXT[!MUST]:    queries.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A DNS client SHOULD include the edns-key-tag option when issuing a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DNSKEY query for a zone corresponding to a trust anchor.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    A DNS client MAY include the edns-key-tag option when issuing a
    TEXT[!MAY]:    DNSKEY query for a non-trust anchor zone (i.e., Key Tags learned via
    TEXT[!MAY]:    DS records).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A DNS client MUST NOT include Key Tag(s) for keys that are not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    learned via either a trust anchor or DS records.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Since the edns-key-tag option is only set in the query, if a client
    TEXT[!MUST]:    sees these options in the response, no action needs to be taken and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the client MUST ignore the option values.

  SECTION: [Validating Stub Resolvers](#section-4.2.1.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Such validating resolvers SHOULD include the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    edns-key-tag option in the OPT RR when sending a DNSKEY query.

  SECTION: [Non-validating Stub Resolvers](#section-4.2.1.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The edns-key-tag option MUST NOT be included by non-validating stub
    TEXT[!MUST]:    resolvers.

  SECTION: [Validating Recursive Resolvers](#section-4.2.2.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Thus, a recursive resolver SHOULD include
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the edns-key-tag option in its DNSKEY queries as described above.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: When a validating recursive resolver receives a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    query that includes the edns-key-tag option with a Key Tag list that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    differs from its own, it SHOULD forward both the client's Key Tag
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    list and its own list.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: When doing so, the recursive resolver SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    transmit the two Key Tag lists using separate instances of the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    edns-key-tag option code in the OPT RR.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    A validating recursive resolver MAY combine stub/client Key Tag
    TEXT[!MAY]:    values from multiple incoming queries into a single outgoing query.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    It is RECOMMENDED that implementations place reasonable limits on the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    number of Key Tags to include in the outgoing edns-key-tag option.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    If the client included the DNSSEC OK and Checking Disabled (CD) bits
    TEXT[!MAY]:    but did not include the edns-key-tag option in the query, the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    validating recursive resolver MAY include the option with its own
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Key Tag values in full.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Validating recursive resolvers MUST NOT set the edns-key-tag option
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in the final response to the stub client.

  SECTION: [Non-validating Recursive Resolvers](#section-4.2.2.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Recursive resolvers that do not validate responses SHOULD copy the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    edns-key-tag option seen in received queries, as they represent the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    wishes of the validating downstream resolver that issued the original
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    query.

  SECTION: [Use by Responders](#section-4.3)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    An authoritative name server receiving queries with the edns-key-tag
    TEXT[!MAY]:    option MAY log or otherwise collect the Key Tag values to provide
    TEXT[!MAY]:    information to the zone operator.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A responder MUST NOT include the edns-key-tag option in any DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response.

  SECTION: [Query Format](#section-5.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Hexadecimal values MUST be zero-padded to four hexadecimal digits.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When representing multiple Key Tag values, they MUST be sorted in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    order from smallest to largest.

  SECTION: [Use by Queriers](#section-5.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A validating DNS resolver (stub or recursive) SHOULD originate a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Key Tag query whenever it also originates a DNSKEY query for a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    trust anchor zone.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A validating DNS resolver SHOULD NOT originate Key Tag queries when
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    also originating DNSKEY queries for non-trust anchor zones.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A non-validating DNS resolver MUST NOT originate Key Tag queries.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DNS resolvers with caches SHOULD cache and reuse the response to a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Key Tag query just as it would any other response.

  SECTION: [Use by Responders](#section-5.3)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    An authoritative name server receiving Key Tag queries MAY log or
    TEXT[!MAY]:    otherwise collect the Key Tag values to provide information to the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    zone operator.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    An authoritative name server MUST generate an appropriate response to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the Key Tag query.

  SECTION: [Interaction with Aggressive Negative Caching](#section-5.3.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Recall that when multiple Key Tags are present, the originating
    TEXT[!MUST]:    client MUST sort them from smallest to largest in the query name.

  SECTION: [Security Considerations](#section-7)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Zone operators relying
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    on the edns-key-tag mechanism SHOULD take care to ensure that new
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    keys have unique Key Tag values.

  SECTION: [Privacy Considerations](#section-8)
    TEXT[!MAY]: Due to privacy concerns, such a resolver MAY
    TEXT[!MAY]:    choose to transmit the Key Tags for a subset of queries (e.g., every
    TEXT[!MAY]:    25th time) or by random chance with a certain probability (e.g., 5%).
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Implementations of this specification MAY be administratively
    TEXT[!MAY]:    configured to only transmit the Key Tags for certain zones.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Since the primary motivation for this specification is to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    provide operational measurement data for root zone key rollovers, it
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    is RECOMMENDED that implementations at least include the edns-key-tag
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    option for root zone DNSKEY queries.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8482
  SECTION: [Behavior of DNS Responders](#section-4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Except as described below in this section, the DNS responder MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    follow the standard algorithms when constructing a response.

  SECTION: [Answer with a Subset of Available RRsets](#section-4.1)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    A DNS responder that receives an ANY query MAY decline to provide a
    TEXT[!MAY]:    conventional ANY response or MAY instead send a response with a
    TEXT[!MAY]:    single RRset (or a larger subset of available RRsets) in the answer
    TEXT[!MAY]:    section.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    The RRsets returned in the answer section of the response MAY consist
    TEXT[!MAY]:    of a single RRset owned by the name specified in the QNAME.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Where
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    multiple RRsets exist, the responder SHOULD choose a small subset of
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    those available to reduce the amplification potential of the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    response.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the zone is signed, appropriate RRSIG records MUST be included in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the answer.

  SECTION: [Answer with a Synthesized HINFO RRset](#section-4.2)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    If there is no CNAME present at the owner name matching the QNAME,
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the resource record returned in the response MAY instead be
    TEXT[!MAY]:    synthesized.
