    TEXT[!SHOULD]: In this case, a single HINFO resource record SHOULD be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    returned.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The CPU field of the HINFO RDATA SHOULD be set to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    "RFC8482".
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The OS field of the HINFO RDATA SHOULD be set to the null
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    string to minimize the size of the response.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The TTL encoded for the synthesized HINFO resource record SHOULD be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    chosen by the operator of the DNS responder to be large enough to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    suppress frequent subsequent ANY queries from the same initiator with
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the same QNAME, understanding that a TTL that is too long might make
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    policy changes relating to ANY queries difficult to change in the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    future.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The specific value used SHOULD be configurable by the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    operator of the nameserver according to local policy, based on the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    familiar considerations involved in choosing a TTL value for any
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    resource record in any zone.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the DNS query includes DO=1 and the QNAME corresponds to a zone
    TEXT[!MUST]:    that is known by the responder to be signed, a valid RRSIG for the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRsets in the answer (or authority if answer is empty) section MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be returned.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: In the case of DO=0, the RRSIG SHOULD be omitted.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A system that receives an HINFO response SHOULD NOT infer that the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    response was generated according to this specification and apply any
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    special processing of the response because, in general, it is not
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    possible to tell with certainty whether the HINFO RRset received was
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    synthesized.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: In particular, systems SHOULD NOT rely upon the HINFO
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    RDATA described in this section to distinguish between synthesized
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    and non-synthesized HINFO RRsets.

  SECTION: [Answer with Best Guess as to Intention](#section-4.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    As before, if the zone is signed and the DO bit is set on the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    corresponding query, an RRSIG RRset MUST be included in the response.

  SECTION: [Transport Considerations](#section-4.4)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    A DNS responder MAY behave differently when processing ANY queries
    TEXT[!MAY]:    received over different transports, e.g., by providing a conventional
    TEXT[!MAY]:    ANY response over TCP whilst using one of the other mechanisms
    TEXT[!MAY]:    specified in this document in the case where a query was received
    TEXT[!MAY]:    using UDP.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Implementers MAY provide configuration options to allow operators to
    TEXT[!MAY]:    specify different behavior over different transports.

  SECTION: [Behavior of DNS Initiators](#section-5)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    A DNS initiator that sends a query with QTYPE=ANY and receives a
    TEXT[!MAY]:    response containing an HINFO resource record or a single RRset, as
    TEXT[!MAY]:    described in Section 4, MAY cache the response in the normal way.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Such cached resource records SHOULD be retained in the cache
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    following normal caching semantics, as with any other response
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    received from a DNS responder.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    A DNS initiator MAY suppress queries with QTYPE=ANY in the event that
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the local cache contains a matching HINFO resource record with the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    CPU field of the HINFO RDATA, as described in Section 4.
    TEXT[!MAY]: A DNS
    TEXT[!MAY]:    initiator MAY instead respond to such queries with the contents of
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the local cache in the usual way.

  SECTION: [HINFO Considerations](#section-6)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Operators of authoritative servers who serve zones that rely upon
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    conventional use of the HINFO RRTYPE SHOULD sensibly choose the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    "single RRset" method described in this document or select another
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    type.

  SECTION: [Updates to RFCs 1034 and 1035](#section-7)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The main difference here is that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the TC bit SHOULD NOT be set in the response, thus indicating that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    this is not a complete answer.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    This document describes optional behavior for both DNS initiators and
    TEXT[!MAY]:    responders; implementation of the guidance provided by this document
    TEXT[!MAY]:    is OPTIONAL.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8484
  SECTION: [Selection of DoH Server](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MAY]: DoH servers MAY support
    TEXT[!MAY]:    more than one URI Template.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A DoH client MUST NOT use a different URI simply because it was
    TEXT[!MUST]:    discovered outside of the client's configuration (such as through
    TEXT[!MUST]:    HTTP/2 server push) or because a server offers an unsolicited
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response that appears to be a valid answer to a DNS query.

  SECTION: [The HTTP Request](#section-4.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Future specifications for new media types for DoH MUST define the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    variables used for URI Template processing with this protocol.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DoH servers MUST implement both the POST and GET methods.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The DoH client SHOULD include an HTTP Accept request header field to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    indicate what type of content can be understood in response.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Irrespective of the value of the Accept request header field, the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    client MUST be prepared to process "application/dns-message" (as
    TEXT[!MUST]:    described in Section 6) responses but MAY also process other DNS-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    related media types it receives.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In order to maximize HTTP cache friendliness, DoH clients using media
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    formats that include the ID field from the DNS message header, such
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    as "application/dns-message", SHOULD use a DNS ID of 0 in every DNS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    request.

  SECTION: [The HTTP Response](#section-4.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: A DoH server MUST be able to process
    TEXT[!MUST]:    "application/dns-message" request messages.

  SECTION: [HTTP Integration](#section-5)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    This protocol MUST be used with the https URI scheme [RFC7230].

  SECTION: [Cache Interaction](#section-5.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In particular, DoH servers SHOULD assign an explicit HTTP freshness
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    lifetime (see Section 4.2 of [RFC7234]) so that the DoH client is
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    more likely to use fresh DNS data.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The assigned freshness lifetime of a DoH HTTP response MUST be less
    TEXT[!MUST]:    than or equal to the smallest TTL in the Answer section of the DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: A freshness lifetime equal to the smallest TTL in the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Answer section is RECOMMENDED.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the DNS response has no records in the Answer section, and the DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response has an SOA record in the Authority section, the response
    TEXT[!MUST]:    freshness lifetime MUST NOT be greater than the MINIMUM field from
    TEXT[!MUST]:    that SOA record (see [RFC2308]).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DoH clients MUST account for the Age response header field's value
    TEXT[!MUST]:    [RFC7234] when calculating the DNS TTL of a response.

  SECTION: [HTTP/2](#section-5.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    HTTP/2 [RFC7540] is the minimum RECOMMENDED version of HTTP for use
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    with DoH.

  SECTION: [Server Push](#section-5.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Before using DoH response data for DNS resolution, the client MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    establish that the HTTP request URI can be used for the DoH query.

  SECTION: [Content Negotiation](#section-5.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In order to maximize interoperability, DoH clients and DoH servers
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST support the "application/dns-message" media type.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Other media
    TEXT[!MAY]:    types MAY be used as defined by HTTP Content Negotiation (see
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Section 3.4 of [RFC7231]).
    TEXT[!MUST]: Those media types MUST be flexible enough
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to express every DNS query that would normally be sent in DNS over
    TEXT[!MUST]:    UDP (including queries and responses that use DNS extensions, but not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    those that require multiple responses).

  SECTION: [Definition of the "application/dns-message" Media Type](#section-6)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    DoH clients using this media type MAY have one or more Extension
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Mechanisms for DNS (EDNS) options [RFC6891] in the request.
    TEXT[!MUST]: DoH
    TEXT[!MUST]:    servers using this media type MUST ignore the value given for the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    EDNS UDP payload size in DNS requests.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When using the GET method, the data payload for this media type MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be encoded with base64url [RFC4648] and then provided as a variable
    TEXT[!MUST]:    named "dns" to the URI Template expansion.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Padding characters for
    TEXT[!MUST]:    base64url MUST NOT be included.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When using the POST method, the data payload for this media type MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NOT be encoded and is used directly as the HTTP message body.

  SECTION: [In the Server](#section-8.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: HTTP cookies SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    NOT be accepted by DOH clients unless they are explicitly required by
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    a use case.

  SECTION: [Operational Considerations](#section-10)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: To mitigate the possibility of deadlock, the authentication
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    given DoH servers SHOULD NOT rely on DNS-based references to external
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    resources in the TLS handshake.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8659
  SECTION: [Introduction](#section-1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: Relying Parties MUST NOT use CAA
    TEXT[!MUST]:    records as part of certificate validation.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    CAA records MAY be used by Certificate Evaluators as a possible
    TEXT[!MAY]:    indicator of a security policy violation.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Such use SHOULD take into
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    account the possibility that published CAA records changed between
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the time a certificate was issued and the time at which the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    certificate was observed by the Certificate Evaluator.

  SECTION: [Relevant Resource Record Set](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Before issuing a certificate, a compliant CA MUST check for
    TEXT[!MUST]:    publication of a Relevant RRset.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If such an RRset exists, a CA
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST NOT issue a certificate unless the CA determines that either
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (1) the certificate request is consistent with the applicable CAA
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRset or (2) an exception specified in the relevant CP or CPS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    applies.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    A certificate request MAY specify more than one FQDN and MAY specify
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Wildcard Domain Names.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Issuers MUST verify authorization for all the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    FQDNs and Wildcard Domain Names specified in the request.

  SECTION: [Syntax](#section-4.1)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    An FQDN MAY have multiple CAA RRs associated with it, and a given
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Property Tag MAY be specified more than once across those RRs.
    TEXT[!MUST]: A CA MUST NOT issue certificates for any
    TEXT[!MUST]:          FQDN if the Relevant RRset for that FQDN contains a CAA
    TEXT[!MUST]:          critical Property for an unknown or unsupported Property Tag.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    To ensure compatibility with future extensions to CAA, DNS records
    TEXT[!MUST]:    compliant with this version of the CAA specification MUST clear (set
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to "0") all reserved flag bits.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Applications that interpret CAA
    TEXT[!MUST]:    records MUST ignore the value of all reserved flag bits.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The tag length MUST be at least 1.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Tags MAY contain ASCII characters "a" through "z", "A" through "Z",
    TEXT[!MAY]:    and the numbers 0 through 9.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Tags MUST NOT contain any other
    TEXT[!MUST]:    characters.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Tags submitted for registration by IANA MUST NOT contain any
    TEXT[!MUST]:    characters other than the (lowercase) ASCII characters "a" through
    TEXT[!MUST]:    "z" and the numbers 0 through 9.
    TEXT[!MAY]:       Property Values are encoded as binary values and MAY employ
    TEXT[!MAY]:       sub-formats.

  SECTION: [CAA issue Property](#section-4.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    An issue Property Tag where the issue-value does not match the ABNF
    TEXT[!MUST]:    grammar MUST be treated the same as one specifying an empty
    TEXT[!MUST]:    issuer-domain-name.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    An Issuer MAY choose to specify parameters that further constrain the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    issue of certificates by that Issuer -- for example, specifying that
    TEXT[!MAY]:    certificates are to be subject to specific validation policies,
    TEXT[!MAY]:    billed to certain accounts, or issued under specific trust anchors.

  SECTION: [CAA issuewild Property](#section-4.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Each issuewild Property MUST be ignored when processing a request for
    TEXT[!MUST]:    an FQDN that is not a Wildcard Domain Name.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If at least one issuewild Property is specified in the Relevant RRset
    TEXT[!MUST]:    for a Wildcard Domain Name, each issue Property MUST be ignored when
    TEXT[!MUST]:    processing a request for that Wildcard Domain Name.

  SECTION: [CAA iodef Property](#section-4.4)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       The mail message sent SHOULD contain a brief text message to alert
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       the recipient to the nature of the attachment.

  SECTION: [Critical Flag](#section-4.5)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The critical flag is intended to permit future versions of CAA to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    introduce new semantics that MUST be understood for correct
    TEXT[!MUST]:    processing of the record, preventing conforming CAs that do not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    recognize the new semantics from issuing certificates for the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    indicated FQDNs.

  SECTION: [Use of DNS Security](#section-5.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The use of DNSSEC to authenticate CAA RRs is strongly RECOMMENDED but
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    not required.
    TEXT[!MUST]: An Issuer MUST NOT issue certificates if doing so
    TEXT[!MUST]:    would conflict with the Relevant RRset, irrespective of whether the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    corresponding DNS records are signed.

  SECTION: [Mis-Issue by Authorized Certification Authority](#section-5.3)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    FQDN holders SHOULD verify that the CAs they authorize to issue
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    certificates for their FQDNs employ appropriate controls to ensure
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    that certificates are issued only to authorized parties within their
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    organization.

  SECTION: [Suppression or Spoofing of CAA Records](#section-5.4)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Where possible, Issuers SHOULD perform DNSSEC validation to detect
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    missing or modified CAA RRsets.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In cases where DNSSEC is not deployed for a corresponding FQDN, an
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Issuer SHOULD attempt to mitigate this risk by employing appropriate
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DNS security controls.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: For example, all portions of the DNS lookup
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    process SHOULD be performed against the authoritative nameserver.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Data cached by third parties MUST NOT be relied on as the sole source
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of DNS CAA information but MAY be used to support additional
    TEXT[!MUST]:    anti-spoofing or anti-suppression controls.

  SECTION: [Delegation to Private Nameservers](#section-6.3)
    TEXT[!MAY]: The CA MAY interpret that as preventing issuance.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: FQDN
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    administrators wishing to issue certificates for private FQDNs SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    use split-horizon DNS with a publicly available nameserver, so that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    CAs can receive a valid, empty CAA response for those FQDNs.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8764
  SECTION: [Transition to DNS Push Notifications](#section-1.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    All existing LLQ implementations are RECOMMENDED to migrate to using
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DNS Push Notifications instead.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Existing LLQ servers are RECOMMENDED to implement and support DNS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Push Notifications so that clients can begin migrating to the newer
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    protocol.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Existing LLQ clients are RECOMMENDED to query for the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    "_dns-push-tls._tcp.<zone>" SRV record first, and then only if DNS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Push Notifications fail, fall back to query for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    "_dns-llq._udp.<zone>" instead.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    It is RECOMMENDED that clients always attempt DNS Push Notifications
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    first for every new request, and only if that fails, then fall back
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    to using LLQ.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Clients SHOULD NOT record that a given server only
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    speaks LLQ and subsequently default to LLQ for that server, since
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    server software gets updated and even a server that speaks only LLQ
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    today may be updated to support DNS Push Notifications tomorrow.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    New client and server implementations are RECOMMENDED to support only
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DNS Push Notifications.

  SECTION: [Opt-RR Format](#section-3.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:           +------------+--------------+-------------------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:           | Field Name | Field Type   | Description             |
    TEXT[!MUST]:           +============+==============+=========================+
    TEXT[!MUST]:           | NAME       | domain name  | MUST be 0 (root domain) |
    TEXT[!MUST]:           +------------+--------------+-------------------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:           | TYPE       | u_int16_t    | OPT (41)                |
    TEXT[!MUST]:           +------------+--------------+-------------------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:           | CLASS      | u_int16_t    | 0*                      |
    TEXT[!MUST]:           +------------+--------------+-------------------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:           | TTL        | u_int32_t    | 0                       |
    TEXT[!MUST]:           +------------+--------------+-------------------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:           | RDLEN      | u_int16_t    | length of all RDATA     |
    TEXT[!MUST]:           +------------+--------------+-------------------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:           | RDATA      | octet stream | (see below)             |
    TEXT[!MUST]:           +------------+--------------+-------------------------+
    TEXT[!MAY]: Thus, the sender of an LLQ Request
    TEXT[!MAY]:    or Response MAY set the CLASS field to 0.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The recipient MUST ignore
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the class field if it is set to 0.

  SECTION: [LLQ Address and Port Identification](#section-4)
    TEXT[!MAY]: Thus, servers MAY listen for
    TEXT[!MAY]:    LLQs on a different port (typically 5352).
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the record exists, then the server MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    answer with that SOA record in the Answer section.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If a record of
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    type SOA with the LLQ name does not exist, then the server SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    include an SOA record for that name's zone in the Authority section.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    An authoritative server for a zone implementing LLQ MUST answer with
    TEXT[!MUST]:    an SRV record [RFC2782] for this name.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The server SHOULD include the address record(s) for the target host
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    in the Additional section of the response.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If the server does not include the target host's address record(s) in
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the Additional section, the client SHOULD query explicitly for the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    address record(s) with the name of the SRV target.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The client MUST send all LLQ requests, refreshes, and acknowledgments
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to the name server specified in the SRV target, at the address
    TEXT[!MUST]:    contained in the address record for that target.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Note that the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    queries described in this section (including those for SOA and SRV
    TEXT[!MAY]:    records) MAY be sent to an intermediate DNS recursive resolver --
    TEXT[!MAY]:    they need not be sent directly to the name server.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If, on issuing the SRV query, the client receives a negative response
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    indicating that the SRV record does not exist, the client SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    conclude that the zone does not support LLQ.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The client then SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    NOT send an LLQ request for the desired name, instead utilizing the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    behavior for LLQ-unaware servers described in Section 5, "LLQ Setup".

  SECTION: [Setup Message Retransmission](#section-5.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    LLQ Setup Requests and Responses sent by the client SHOULD be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    retransmitted if no acknowledgments are received.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The client SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    retry up to two more times (for a total of 3 attempts) before
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    considering the server down or unreachable.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The client MUST wait at
    TEXT[!MUST]:    least 2 seconds before the first retransmission and 4 seconds between
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the first and second retransmissions.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The client SHOULD listen for a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    response for at least 8 seconds after the 3rd attempt before
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    considering the server down or unreachable.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Upon determining a
    TEXT[!MAY]:    server to be down, a client MAY periodically attempt to re-initiate
    TEXT[!MAY]:    an LLQ setup at a rate of not more than once per hour.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Servers MUST NOT retransmit acknowledgments that do not generate
    TEXT[!MUST]:    responses from the client.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If servers receive duplicate messages from clients (perhaps due to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the loss of the server's responses mid-flight), the server MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    resend its reply (possibly modifying the LLQ-LEASE as described in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Section 5.2.4, "ACK + Answers").
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Servers MUST NOT garbage collect LLQs that fail to complete the four-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    way handshake until the initially granted LLQ-LEASE has elapsed.

  SECTION: [Setup Request](#section-5.2.1)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    The request MAY contain multiple questions to set up multiple LLQs.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A Setup Request consisting of multiple questions MUST contain
    TEXT[!MUST]:    multiple LLQ OPTIONS, one per question, with the LLQ OPTIONS in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    same order as the questions they correspond to (i.e., the first LLQ
    TEXT[!MUST]:    OPTION corresponds to the first question, the second LLQ OPTION
    TEXT[!MUST]:    corresponds to the second question, etc.).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If requesting multiple
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    LLQs, clients SHOULD request the same LLQ-LEASE for each LLQ.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Requests over UDP MUST NOT contain multiple questions if doing so
    TEXT[!MUST]:    would cause the message to exceed a single IP packet.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A client MUST NOT request multiple identical LLQs (i.e., containing
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the same qname/type/class) from the same source IP address and port.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The query MUST NOT be for record type ANY (255), class ANY (255), or
    TEXT[!MUST]:    class NONE (0).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Setup Request LLQ OPTION MUST be repeated once for each
    TEXT[!MUST]:    additional query in the Question section.

  SECTION: [Setup Challenge](#section-5.2.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The LLQ OPTIONS MUST be in the same order as the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    questions they correspond to.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Setup Challenge LLQ OPTION MUST be repeated once for each query
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in the Questions section of the Setup Challenge.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Note that if
    TEXT[!MUST]:                         the rest of the DNS message is properly
    TEXT[!MUST]:                         formatted, the DNS header error code MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:                         include a format error code, since to do so
    TEXT[!MUST]:                         would cause ambiguity between the case where a
    TEXT[!MUST]:                         client sends a valid LLQ Setup Request to a
    TEXT[!MUST]:                         server that does not understand LLQ and the case
    TEXT[!MUST]:                         where a client sends a malformed LLQ Setup
    TEXT[!MUST]:                         Request to a server that does understand LLQ.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Upon returning this error, the
    TEXT[!MUST]:                         server MUST include in the LLQ-LEASE field a
    TEXT[!MUST]:                         time interval, in seconds, after which the
    TEXT[!MUST]:                         client may retry the LLQ Setup.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The client
    TEXT[!MUST]:                         MUST honor the resource record TTLs returned and
    TEXT[!MUST]:                         MUST NOT poll sooner than indicated by those
    TEXT[!MUST]:                         TTLs, nor should it retry the LLQ Setup for this
    TEXT[!MUST]:                         name and type.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The LLQ-ID SHOULD be an
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:                      unpredictable random number.
    TEXT[!MAY]: The server MAY
    TEXT[!MAY]:                      discard the LLQ after this LLQ-LEASE expires unless
    TEXT[!MAY]:                      the LLQ has been renewed by the client (see
    TEXT[!MAY]:                      Section 7, "LLQ Lease-Life Expiration").
    TEXT[!MUST]: The
    TEXT[!MUST]:                      server MUST NOT generate events (see Section 6,
    TEXT[!MUST]:                      "Event Responses") for expired LLQs.
    TEXT[!MUST]:                      On SERV-FULL error, LLQ-LEASE MUST be set to a time
    TEXT[!MUST]:                      interval, in seconds, after which the client may
    TEXT[!MUST]:                      retry the LLQ Setup.
    TEXT[!MUST]:                      On other errors, the LLQ-LEASE MUST be set to 0.

  SECTION: [Challenge Response](#section-5.2.3)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: After receiving a successful Setup Challenge, the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    client SHOULD send a Challenge Response to the server.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Challenge Response contains multiple questions, the first question
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST correspond to the first LLQ OPTION, etc.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the Setup Request for a particular LLQ fails with a STATIC error,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the client MUST NOT poll the server for that LLQ.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The client SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    honor the resource record TTLs contained in the response.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    If a Setup Request fails with a SERV-FULL error, the client MAY retry
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the LLQ Setup Request (Section 5.2.1) after the time indicated in the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    LLQ-LEASE field.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    If the Setup Request fails with an error other than STATIC or
    TEXT[!MAY]:    SERV-FULL, or the server is determined not to support LLQ (i.e., the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    client receives a DNS response with a nonzero RCODE, or a DNS
    TEXT[!MAY]:    response containing no LLQ option), the client MAY poll the server
    TEXT[!MAY]:    periodically with standard DNS queries, inferring Add and Remove
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Events (see Section 6, "Event Responses") by comparing answers to
    TEXT[!MAY]:    these queries.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The client SHOULD NOT poll more than once every 15
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    minutes for a given query.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The client MUST NOT poll if it receives a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    STATIC error code in the acknowledgment.

  SECTION: [ACK + Answers](#section-5.2.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Upon receiving a correct Challenge Response, a server MUST return an
    TEXT[!MUST]:    acknowledgment, completing the LLQ setup, and provide all current
    TEXT[!MUST]:    answers to the question(s).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    To acknowledge a successful Challenge Response, i.e., a Challenge
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Response in which the LLQ-ID and LLQ-LEASE echoed by the client match
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the values issued by the server, the server MUST send a DNS response
    TEXT[!MUST]:    containing all available answers to the question(s) contained in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    original Setup Request, along with all additional resource records
    TEXT[!MUST]:    appropriate for those answers in the Additional section.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    If there is a significant delay in receiving a Challenge Response, or
    TEXT[!MAY]:    multiple Challenge Responses are issued (possibly because they were
    TEXT[!MAY]:    lost en route to the client, causing the client to resend the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Challenge Response), the server MAY decrement the LLQ-LEASE by the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    time elapsed since the Setup Challenge was initially issued.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the setup is completed over UDP and all initially available
    TEXT[!MUST]:    answers to the question(s), additional records, and the OPT pseudo-RR
    TEXT[!MUST]:    do not fit in a single IP packet, some or all additional records
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (excluding the OPT pseudo-RR) MUST be omitted.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If, after omission of
    TEXT[!MUST]:    all additional records, the answers still do not fit in a single
    TEXT[!MUST]:    message, answers MUST be removed until the message fits in a single
    TEXT[!MUST]:    IP packet.
    TEXT[!MUST]: These answers not delivered in the ACK + Answers MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    delivered without undue delay to the client via Add Events
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (Section 6, "Event Responses").

  SECTION: [Resource Record TTLs](#section-5.3)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The TTLs of resource records contained in answers to successful LLQs
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD be ignored by the client.
    TEXT[!MAY]: The client MAY cache LLQ answers
    TEXT[!MAY]:    until the client receives a gratuitous announcement (see Section 6,
    TEXT[!MAY]:    "Event Responses") indicating that the answer to the LLQ has changed.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The client SHOULD NOT cache answers after the LLQs LLQ-LEASE expires
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    without being refreshed (see Section 7, "LLQ Lease-Life Expiration").
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If an LLQ request fails, the client SHOULD NOT cache answers for a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    period longer than the client's polling interval.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    TTLs of resource records included in the Additional section of an LLQ
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    response (which do not directly answer the LLQ) SHOULD be honored by
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the client.

  SECTION: [Event Responses](#section-6)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When a change ("event") occurs to a name server's zone, the server
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST check if the new or deleted resource records answer any LLQs.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If so, the changes MUST be communicated to the LLQ requesters in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    form of a gratuitous DNS response sent to the client, with the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    relevant question(s) in the Question section, and the corresponding
    TEXT[!MUST]:    answers in the Answer section.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Gratuitous responses for a single LLQ MAY be batched such that
    TEXT[!MAY]:    multiple changes are communicated in a single message.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Responses
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST NOT be batched if this would cause a message that would
    TEXT[!MUST]:    otherwise fit in a single IP packet to be truncated.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: While responses
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    MAY be deferred to provide opportunities for batching, responses
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD NOT be delayed, for purposes of batching, for more than 30
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    seconds, as this would cause an unacceptable latency for the client.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    After sending a gratuitous response, the server MUST listen for an
    TEXT[!MUST]:    acknowledgment from the client.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the client does not respond, the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    server MUST resend the response.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The server MUST resend two times
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (for a total of 3 transmissions), after which the server MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    consider the client to be unreachable and delete its LLQ.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The server
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST listen for 2 seconds before resending the response, 4 more
    TEXT[!MUST]:    seconds before resending again, and must wait an additional 8 seconds
    TEXT[!MUST]:    after the 3rd transmission before terminating the LLQ.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The DNS message header of the response SHOULD include an
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    unpredictable random number in the DNS message ID field, which is to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    be echoed in the client's acknowledgment.

  SECTION: [Add Events](#section-6.1)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Records that normally accompany this record in responses MAY be
    TEXT[!MAY]:    included in the Additional section as per truncation restrictions
    TEXT[!MAY]:    described above.

  SECTION: [Gratuitous Response Acknowledgments](#section-6.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Upon receiving a gratuitous response ("event"), the client MUST send
    TEXT[!MUST]:    an acknowledgment to the server.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The acknowledgment MUST be sent to the source IP address and port
    TEXT[!MUST]:    from which the event originated.

  SECTION: [Refresh Request](#section-7.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the client desires to maintain the LLQ beyond the duration
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specified in the LLQ-LEASE field of the ACK + Answers
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (Section 5.2.4), the client MUST send a Refresh Request.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The client SHOULD refresh an LLQ when 80% of its LLQ-LEASE has
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    elapsed.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    As a means of reducing network traffic, when constructing refresh
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    messages the client SHOULD include all LLQs established with a given
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    server, even those not yet close to expiration.
    TEXT[!MUST]: However, at least
    TEXT[!MUST]:    one LLQ MUST have elapsed at least 80% of its original LLQ-LEASE.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The client MUST NOT include additional LLQs if doing so would cause
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the message to no longer fit in a single IP packet.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: (These LLQs SHOULD be refreshed
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    in a separate message when 80% of one or more of their lease lives
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    have elapsed.)  When refreshing multiple LLQs simultaneously, the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    message contains multiple questions and a single OPT pseudo-RR with
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    multiple LLQ OPTIONS, one per question, with the LLQ OPTIONS in the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    same order as the questions they correspond to.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The client SHOULD specify the original LLQ-LEASE granted in the LLQ
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    response as the desired LLQ-LEASE in the Refresh Request.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    refreshing multiple LLQs simultaneously, the client SHOULD request
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the same LLQ-LEASE for all LLQs being refreshed (with the exception
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    of termination requests; see below).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The client MUST listen for an acknowledgment from the server.
    TEXT[!MAY]: The
    TEXT[!MAY]:    client MAY retry up to two more times (for a total of 3 attempts)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    before considering the server down or unreachable.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The client MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NOT retry a first time before 90% of the LLQ-LEASE has expired and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST NOT retry again before 95% of the LLQ-LEASE has expired.
    TEXT[!MAY]: If the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    server is determined to be down, the client MAY periodically attempt
    TEXT[!MAY]:    to re-establish the LLQ via an LLQ Setup Request message.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The client
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST NOT attempt the LLQ Setup Request more than once per hour.

  SECTION: [LLQ Refresh Acknowledgment](#section-7.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Upon receiving an LLQ Refresh message, a server MUST send an
    TEXT[!MUST]:    acknowledgment of the Refresh.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    *  NO-SUCH-LLQ MUST be returned as an error code if the client
    TEXT[!MUST]:       attempts to refresh an expired or non-existent LLQ (as determined
    TEXT[!MUST]:       by the LLQ-ID in the request).

  SECTION: [Problems with the LLQ Protocol](#appendix-A)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    LLQ's IETF Standards Track successor, "DNS Push Notifications"
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    [RFC8765], does not suffer from these problems, so all existing LLQ
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    implementations are RECOMMENDED to migrate to using DNS Push
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Notifications, and all new implementations are RECOMMENDED to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    implement DNS Push Notifications instead of LLQ.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Section 5.1 of this LLQ specification states, "Servers MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    garbage collect LLQs that fail to complete the four-way handshake
    TEXT[!MUST]:    until the initially granted LLQ-LEASE has elapsed."  This is probably
    TEXT[!MUST]:    a mistake since it exposes LLQ servers to an easy resource-exhaustion
    TEXT[!MUST]:    denial-of-service attack.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8806
  SECTION: [Introduction](#section-1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Specifically, the root service on the local system MUST be configured
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to only answer queries from resolvers on the same host and MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    answer queries from any other resolver.

  SECTION: [Requirements](#section-2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    *  The system MUST be able to validate every signed record in a zone
    TEXT[!MUST]:       with DNSSEC [RFC4033].
    TEXT[!MUST]:    *  The system MUST have an up-to-date copy of the public part of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:       Key Signing Key (KSK) [RFC4033] used to sign the DNS root.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    *  The system MUST be able to retrieve a copy of the entire root zone
    TEXT[!MUST]:       (including all DNSSEC-related records).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    *  The system MUST be able to run an authoritative service for the
    TEXT[!MUST]:       root zone on the same host.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The authoritative root service MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:       only respond to queries from the same host.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A corollary of the above list is that authoritative data in the root
    TEXT[!MUST]:    zone used on the local authoritative server MUST be identical to the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    same data in the root zone for the DNS.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: It is possible to change the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    unsigned data (the glue records) in the copy of the root zone, but
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    such changes could cause problems for the recursive server that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    accesses the local root zone, and therefore any changes to the glue
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    records SHOULD NOT be made.

  SECTION: [Operation of the Root Zone on the Local Server](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The contents of the root zone MUST be refreshed using the timers from
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the SOA record in the root zone, as described in [RFC1035].
    TEXT[!MUST]: A system using a local authoritative server
    TEXT[!MUST]:    for the root zone MUST NOT serve stale data for the root zone.
    TEXT[!MUST]: To
    TEXT[!MUST]:    mitigate the risk that stale data is served, the local root server
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST immediately switch to using non-local root servers when it
    TEXT[!MUST]:    detects that it would be serving state data.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In a resolver that is using an internal service for the root zone, if
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the contents of the root zone cannot be refreshed before the expire
    TEXT[!MUST]:    time in the SOA, the resolver MUST immediately switch to using non-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    local root servers.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    An administrator using the procedure in this document SHOULD have an
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    automated method to check that the contents of the local root zone
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    are being refreshed; this might be part of the resolver software.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8914
  SECTION: [Extended DNS Error EDNS0 Option Format](#section-2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: EDE text may be
    TEXT[!MUST]:       null terminated but MUST NOT be assumed to be; the length MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:       derived from the OPTION-LENGTH field.

  SECTION: [Extended DNS Error Processing](#section-3)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    When the response grows beyond the requestor's UDP payload size
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    [RFC6891], servers SHOULD truncate messages by dropping EDE options
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    before dropping other data from packets.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Implementations SHOULD set
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the truncation bit when dropping EDE options.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Because long EXTRA-
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    TEXT fields may trigger truncation (which is undesirable given the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    supplemental nature of EDE), implementers and operators creating EDE
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    options SHOULD avoid lengthy EXTRA-TEXT contents.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Implementations MAY choose to not
    TEXT[!MAY]:    forward information, or they MAY choose to create a new EDE option(s)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    that conveys the information encoded in the received EDE.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: When doing
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    so, the source of the error SHOULD be attributed in the EXTRA-TEXT
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    field, since an EDNS0 option received by the original client will
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    appear to have come from the resolver or forwarder sending it.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Some combinations of extended error codes and RCODEs may seem
    TEXT[!MUST]:    nonsensical (such as resolver-specific extended error codes received
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in responses from authoritative servers), so systems interpreting the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    extended error codes MUST NOT assume that a combination will make
    TEXT[!MUST]:    sense.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Receivers MUST be able to accept EDE codes and EXTRA-TEXT in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    all messages, including those with a NOERROR RCODE but need not act
    TEXT[!MUST]:    on them.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Applications MUST continue to follow requirements from
    TEXT[!MUST]:    applicable specifications on how to process RCODEs no matter what EDE
    TEXT[!MUST]:    values are also received.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Senders MAY include more than one EDE
    TEXT[!MUST]:    option and receivers MUST be able to accept (but not necessarily
    TEXT[!MUST]:    process or act on) multiple EDE options in a DNS message.

  SECTION: [Extended DNS Error Code 0 - Other](#section-4.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Implementations SHOULD include an EXTRA-TEXT
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    value to augment this error code with additional information.

  SECTION: [Extended DNS Error Code 20 - Not Authoritative](#section-4.21)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    An authoritative server that receives a query with the Recursion
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Desired (RD) bit clear, or when it is not configured for recursion
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    for a domain for which it is not authoritative, SHOULD include this
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    EDE code in the REFUSED response.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: A resolver that receives a query
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    with the RD bit clear SHOULD include this EDE code in the REFUSED
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    response.

  SECTION: [Security Considerations](#section-6)
    TEXT[!MUST]: As such,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    EDE content should be treated only as diagnostic information and MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NOT alter DNS protocol processing.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8945
  SECTION: [TSIG RR Type](#section-4.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: TSIG is a meta-RR and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST NOT be cached.

  SECTION: [TSIG Record Format](#section-4.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    TYPE:  This MUST be TSIG (250: Transaction SIGnature).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    CLASS:  This MUST be ANY.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    TTL:  This MUST be 0.
    TEXT[!MUST]: As
    TEXT[!MUST]:       per [RFC3597], this name MUST NOT be compressed.
    TEXT[!MUST]: In requests, this MUST be zero.

  SECTION: [Request MAC](#section-4.3.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Only included in the computation of a MAC for a response message (or
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the first message in a multi-message response), the validated request
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MAC MUST be included in the MAC computation.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the request MAC
    TEXT[!MUST]:    failed to validate, an unsigned error message MUST be returned
    TEXT[!MUST]:    instead (Section 5.3.2).

  SECTION: [TSIG Variables](#section-4.3.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    +============+================+====================================+
    TEXT[!MUST]:    | Source     | Field Name     | Notes                              |
    TEXT[!MUST]:    +============+================+====================================+
    TEXT[!MUST]:    | TSIG RR    | NAME           | Key name, in canonical wire format |
    TEXT[!MUST]:    +------------+----------------+------------------------------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:    | TSIG RR    | CLASS          | MUST be ANY                        |
    TEXT[!MUST]:    +------------+----------------+------------------------------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:    | TSIG RR    | TTL            | MUST be 0                          |
    TEXT[!MUST]:    +------------+----------------+------------------------------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:    | TSIG RDATA | Algorithm Name | in canonical wire format           |
    TEXT[!MUST]:    +------------+----------------+------------------------------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:    | TSIG RDATA | Time Signed    | in network byte order              |
    TEXT[!MUST]:    +------------+----------------+------------------------------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:    | TSIG RDATA | Fudge          | in network byte order              |
    TEXT[!MUST]:    +------------+----------------+------------------------------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:    | TSIG RDATA | Error          | in network byte order              |
    TEXT[!MUST]:    +------------+----------------+------------------------------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:    | TSIG RDATA | Other Len      | in network byte order              |
    TEXT[!MUST]:    +------------+----------------+------------------------------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:    | TSIG RDATA | Other Data     | exactly as transmitted             |
    TEXT[!MUST]:    +------------+----------------+------------------------------------+

  SECTION: [Generation of TSIG on Requests](#section-5.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: This TSIG
    TEXT[!MUST]:    record MUST be the only TSIG RR in the message and MUST be the last
    TEXT[!MUST]:    record in the additional data section.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The client MUST store the MAC
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and the key name from the request while awaiting an answer.

  SECTION: [Server Processing of Request](#section-5.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If an incoming message contains a TSIG record, it MUST be the last
    TEXT[!MUST]:    record in the additional section.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If multiple TSIG records are detected or a TSIG record is
    TEXT[!MUST]:    present in any other position, the DNS message is dropped and a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response with RCODE 1 (FORMERR) MUST be returned.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the TSIG RR cannot be interpreted, the server MUST regard the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    message as corrupt and return a FORMERR to the server.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Otherwise,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the server is REQUIRED to return a TSIG RR in the response.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    To validate the received TSIG RR, the server MUST perform the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    following checks in the following order:

  SECTION: [Key Check and Error Handling](#section-5.2.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If a non-forwarding server does not recognize the key or algorithm
    TEXT[!MUST]:    used by the client (or recognizes the algorithm but does not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    implement it), the server MUST generate an error response with RCODE
    TEXT[!MUST]:    9 (NOTAUTH) and TSIG ERROR 17 (BADKEY).
    TEXT[!MUST]: This response MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    unsigned as specified in Section 5.3.2.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The server SHOULD log the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    error.

  SECTION: [MAC Check and Error Handling](#section-5.2.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Using the information in the TSIG, the server MUST verify the MAC by
    TEXT[!MUST]:    doing its own calculation and comparing the result with the MAC
    TEXT[!MUST]:    received.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the MAC fails to verify, the server MUST generate an
    TEXT[!MUST]:    error response as specified in Section 5.3.2 with RCODE 9 (NOTAUTH)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and TSIG ERROR 16 (BADSIG).
    TEXT[!MUST]: This response MUST be unsigned, as
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specified in Section 5.3.2.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The server SHOULD log the error.

  SECTION: [MAC Truncation](#section-5.2.2.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the MAC Size field is greater than the keyed hash output
    TEXT[!MUST]:    length:  This case MUST NOT be generated and, if received, MUST cause
    TEXT[!MUST]:       the DNS message to be dropped and RCODE 1 (FORMERR) to be
    TEXT[!MUST]:       returned.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the MAC Size field is less than the larger of 10 (octets) and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    half the length of the hash function in use:  With the exception of
    TEXT[!MUST]:       certain TSIG error messages described in Section 5.3.2, where it
    TEXT[!MUST]:       is permitted that the MAC Size be zero, this case MUST NOT be
    TEXT[!MUST]:       generated and, if received, MUST cause the DNS message to be
    TEXT[!MUST]:       dropped and RCODE 1 (FORMERR) to be returned.

  SECTION: [Time Check and Error Handling](#section-5.2.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the server time is outside the time interval specified by the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    request (which is the Time Signed value plus/minus the Fudge value),
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the server MUST generate an error response with RCODE 9 (NOTAUTH) and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    TSIG ERROR 18 (BADTIME).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The server SHOULD also cache the most
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    recent Time Signed value in a message generated by a key and SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    return BADTIME if a message received later has an earlier Time Signed
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    value.
    TEXT[!MUST]: A response indicating a BADTIME error MUST be signed by the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    same key as the request.
    TEXT[!MUST]: It MUST include the client's current time
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in the Time Signed field, the server's current time (an unsigned
    TEXT[!MUST]:    48-bit integer) in the Other Data field, and 6 in the Other Len
    TEXT[!MUST]:    field.
    TEXT[!MUST]: In addition, the Fudge field MUST be set to the fudge value
    TEXT[!MUST]:    received from the client.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The server SHOULD log the error.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If implementations do retry
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    requests in these cases, a limit SHOULD be placed on the maximum
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    number of retries.

  SECTION: [Truncation Check and Error Handling](#section-5.2.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If a TSIG is received with truncation that is permitted per
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Section 5.2.2.1 but the MAC is too short for the local policy in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    force, an RCODE 9 (NOTAUTH) and TSIG ERROR 22 (BADTRUNC) MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    returned.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The server SHOULD log the error.

  SECTION: [Generation of TSIG on Answers](#section-5.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The server MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    generate a signed response to a request if either the key is invalid
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (e.g., key name or algorithm name are unknown) or the MAC fails
    TEXT[!MUST]:    validation; see Section 5.3.2 for details of responding in these
    TEXT[!MUST]:    cases.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    It also MUST NOT generate a signed response to an unsigned request,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    except in the case of a response to a client's unsigned TKEY request
    TEXT[!MUST]:    if the secret key is established on the server side after the server
    TEXT[!MUST]:    processed the client's request.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Signing responses to unsigned TKEY
    TEXT[!MUST]:    requests MUST be explicitly specified in the description of an
    TEXT[!MUST]:    individual secret key establishment algorithm [RFC3645].
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If addition of the TSIG record will cause the message to be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    truncated, the server MUST alter the response so that a TSIG can be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    included.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: At this
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    point, the client SHOULD retry the request using TCP (as per
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Section 4.2.2 of [RFC1035]).

  SECTION: [TSIG on TCP Connections](#section-5.3.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The TSIG MUST be included
    TEXT[!MUST]:    on all DNS messages in the response.
    TEXT[!MUST]: For backward compatibility, a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    client that receives DNS messages and verifies TSIG MUST accept up to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    99 intermediary messages without a TSIG and MUST verify that both the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    first and last message contain a TSIG.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    client TSIG verification fails, the client MUST close the connection.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If the client does not receive TSIG records frequently enough (as
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    specified above), it SHOULD assume the connection has been hijacked,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    and it SHOULD close the connection.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The client SHOULD treat this the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    same way as they would any other interrupted transfer (although the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    exact behavior is not specified).

  SECTION: [Generation of TSIG on Error Returns](#section-5.3.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    When a server detects an error relating to the key or MAC in the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    incoming request, the server SHOULD send back an unsigned error
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    message (MAC Size == 0 and empty MAC).
    TEXT[!MUST]: It MUST NOT send back a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    signed error message.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If an error is detected relating to the TSIG validity period or the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    MAC is too short for the local policy, the server SHOULD send back a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    signed error message.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the error is not a TSIG error, the response MUST be generated as
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specified in Section 5.3.

  SECTION: [Client Processing of Answer](#section-5.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the TSIG RR is unsigned as specified in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Section 5.3.2 or does not validate, the message MUST be discarded
    TEXT[!MUST]:    unless the RCODE is 9 (NOAUTH).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: In this case, the client SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    attempt to verify the response as if it were a TSIG error, as
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    described in the following subsections.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Regardless of the RCODE, a message containing a TSIG RR that is
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    unsigned as specified in Section 5.3.2 or that fails verification
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD NOT be considered an acceptable response, as it may have been
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    spoofed or manipulated.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Instead, the client SHOULD log an error and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    continue to wait for a signed response until the request times out.

  SECTION: [Key Error Handling](#section-5.4.1)
    TEXT[!MAY]: The client MAY retry the request using the key specified by
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the server.
    TEXT[!MUST]: However, this should never occur, as a server MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    sign a response with a different key to that used to sign the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    request.

  SECTION: [MAC Error Handling](#section-5.4.2)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    If the response RCODE is 9 (NOTAUTH) and TSIG ERROR is 16 (BADSIG),
    TEXT[!MAY]:    this is a MAC-related error, and clients MAY retry the request with a
    TEXT[!MAY]:    new request ID, but it would be better to try a different shared key
    TEXT[!MAY]:    if one is available.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Clients SHOULD keep track of how many MAC
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    errors are associated with each key.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Clients SHOULD log this event.

  SECTION: [Time Error Handling](#section-5.4.3)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In this case, the client SHOULD log the event.
    TEXT[!MUST]: DNS resolvers MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NOT adjust any clocks in the client based on BADTIME errors, but the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    server's time in the Other Data field SHOULD be logged.

  SECTION: [Truncation Error Handling](#section-5.4.4)
    TEXT[!MAY]: The client MAY
    TEXT[!MAY]:    retry with a lesser truncation up to the full HMAC output (no
    TEXT[!MAY]:    truncation), using the truncation used in the response as a hint for
    TEXT[!MAY]:    what the server policy allowed (Section 7).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Clients SHOULD log this
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    event.

  SECTION: [Special Considerations for Forwarding Servers](#section-5.5)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    A server acting as a forwarding server of a DNS message SHOULD check
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    for the existence of a TSIG record.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the name on the TSIG is not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of a secret that the server shares with the originator, the server
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST forward the message unchanged including the TSIG.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the name
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of the TSIG is of a key this server shares with the originator, it
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST process the TSIG.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the TSIG passes all checks, the forwarding
    TEXT[!MUST]:    server MUST, if possible, include a TSIG of its own to the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    destination or the next forwarder.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If no transaction security is
    TEXT[!MUST]:    available to the destination and the message is a query, and if the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    corresponding response has the AD flag (see [RFC4035]) set, the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    forwarder MUST clear the AD flag before adding the TSIG to the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response and returning the result to the system from which it
    TEXT[!MUST]:    received the query.

  SECTION: [Algorithms and Identifiers](#section-6)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Although support for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    hmac-sha1 in TSIG is still mandatory for compatibility reasons,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    existing uses SHOULD be replaced with hmac-sha256 or other SHA-2
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    digest algorithms ([FIPS180-4], [RFC3874], [RFC6234]).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Implementations that support TSIG MUST also implement HMAC SHA1 and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    HMAC SHA256 and MAY implement gss-tsig and the other algorithms
    TEXT[!MUST]:    listed below.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: SHA-1 truncated to 96 bits (12 octets) SHOULD be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    implemented.
    TEXT[!MUST]:       +==========================+================+=================+
    TEXT[!MUST]:       | Algorithm Name           | Implementation | Use             |
    TEXT[!MUST]:       +==========================+================+=================+
    TEXT[!MUST]:       | HMAC-MD5.SIG-ALG.REG.INT | MAY            | MUST NOT        |
    TEXT[!MUST]:       +--------------------------+----------------+-----------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:       | gss-tsig                 | MAY            | MAY             |
    TEXT[!MUST]:       +--------------------------+----------------+-----------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:       | hmac-sha1                | MUST           | NOT RECOMMENDED |
    TEXT[!MUST]:       +--------------------------+----------------+-----------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:       | hmac-sha224              | MAY            | MAY             |
    TEXT[!MUST]:       +--------------------------+----------------+-----------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:       | hmac-sha256              | MUST           | RECOMMENDED     |
    TEXT[!MUST]:       +--------------------------+----------------+-----------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:       | hmac-sha256-128          | MAY            | MAY             |
    TEXT[!MUST]:       +--------------------------+----------------+-----------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:       | hmac-sha384              | MAY            | MAY             |
    TEXT[!MUST]:       +--------------------------+----------------+-----------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:       | hmac-sha384-192          | MAY            | MAY             |
    TEXT[!MUST]:       +--------------------------+----------------+-----------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:       | hmac-sha512              | MAY            | MAY             |
    TEXT[!MUST]:       +--------------------------+----------------+-----------------+
    TEXT[!MUST]:       | hmac-sha512-256          | MAY            | MAY             |
    TEXT[!MUST]:       +--------------------------+----------------+-----------------+

  SECTION: [TSIG Truncation Policy](#section-7)
    TEXT[!MAY]: Local policies MAY require the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    rejection of TSIGs, even though they use an algorithm for which
    TEXT[!MAY]:    implementation is mandatory.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    When a local policy permits acceptance of a TSIG with a particular
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    algorithm and a particular non-zero amount of truncation, it SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    also permit the use of that algorithm with lesser truncation (a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    longer MAC) up to the full keyed hash output.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Regardless of a lower acceptable truncated MAC length specified by
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    local policy, a reply SHOULD be sent with a MAC at least as long as
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    that in the corresponding request.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Implementations permitting multiple acceptable algorithms and/or
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    truncations SHOULD permit this list to be ordered by presumed
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    strength and SHOULD allow different truncations for the same
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    algorithm to be treated as separate entities in this list.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: When so
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    implemented, policies SHOULD accept a presumed stronger algorithm and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    truncation than the minimum strength required by the policy.

  SECTION: [Shared Secrets](#section-8)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The secret
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD be at least as long as the keyed hash output [RFC2104].

  SECTION: [Security Considerations](#section-10)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Secrets SHOULD NOT be shared by more than
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    two entities; any such additional sharing would allow any party
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    knowing the key to impersonate any other such party to members of the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    group.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The RECOMMENDED value in most situations is 300 seconds.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    To prevent cross-algorithm attacks, there SHOULD only be one
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    algorithm associated with any given key name.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8976
  SECTION: [Introduction](#section-1)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    This specification is OPTIONAL to implement by both publishers and
    TEXT[!MAY]:    consumers of zone data.

  SECTION: [Non-apex ZONEMD Records](#section-2.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: Non-apex ZONEMD RRs MUST NOT be used for
    TEXT[!MUST]:    verification.

  SECTION: [The Scheme Field](#section-2.2.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Herein, SIMPLE, with Scheme value 1, is the only standardized Scheme
    TEXT[!MUST]:    defined for ZONEMD records and it MUST be supported by
    TEXT[!MUST]:    implementations.

  SECTION: [The Hash Algorithm Field](#section-2.2.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Herein, SHA384 ([RFC6234]), with Hash Algorithm value 1, is the only
    TEXT[!MUST]:    standardized Hash Algorithm defined for ZONEMD records that MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    supported by implementations.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The result of the SHA384 digest algorithm
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST NOT be truncated, and the entire 48-octet digest is published in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the ZONEMD record.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHA512 ([RFC6234]), with Hash Algorithm value 2, is also defined for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    ZONEMD records and SHOULD be supported by implementations.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The
    TEXT[!MUST]:    result of the SHA512 digest algorithm MUST NOT be truncated, and the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    entire 64-octet digest is published in the ZONEMD record.

  SECTION: [The Digest Field](#section-2.2.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Digest field MUST NOT be shorter than 12 octets.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Digests for future hash algorithms MAY be truncated but
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST NOT be truncated to a length that results in less than 96 bits
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (12 octets) of equivalent strength.

  SECTION: [Including ZONEMD RRs in a Zone](#section-2.5)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    The zone operator MAY choose any of the defined hash algorithms and
    TEXT[!MAY]:    schemes, including the Private Use code points.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    The ZONEMD RRset MAY contain multiple records to support algorithm
    TEXT[!MAY]:    agility ([BCP201]).
    TEXT[!MUST]: When multiple ZONEMD RRs are present, each MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specify a unique Scheme and Hash Algorithm tuple.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: It is RECOMMENDED
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    that a zone include only one ZONEMD RR, unless the zone operator is
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    in the process of transitioning to a new scheme or hash algorithm.

  SECTION: [Add ZONEMD Placeholder](#section-3.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When multiple ZONEMD RRs are published in the zone, e.g., during an
    TEXT[!MUST]:    algorithm rollover, each MUST specify a unique Scheme and Hash
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Algorithm tuple.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    It is RECOMMENDED that the TTL of the ZONEMD record match the TTL of
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the Start of Authority (SOA).

  SECTION: [Optionally, Sign the Zone](#section-3.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: When the digest calculation is complete, and the ZONEMD
    TEXT[!MUST]:    record is updated, the signature(s) for the ZONEMD RRset MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    recalculated and updated as well.

  SECTION: [The SIMPLE Scheme](#section-3.3.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: This specification uses DNSSEC's
    TEXT[!MUST]:    canonical on-the-wire RR format (without name compression) and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    ordering as specified in Sections 6.1, 6.2, and 6.3 of [RFC4034] with
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the additional provision that RRsets having the same owner name MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be numerically ordered, in ascending order, by their numeric RR TYPE.

  SECTION: [SIMPLE Scheme Inclusion/Exclusion Rules](#section-3.3.1.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    *  All records in the zone, including glue records, MUST be included
    TEXT[!MUST]:       unless excluded by a subsequent rule.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    *  Occluded data ([RFC5936], Section 3.5) MUST be included.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    *  If there are duplicate RRs with equal owner, class, type, and
    TEXT[!MUST]:       RDATA, only one instance is included ([RFC4034], Section 6.3) and
    TEXT[!MUST]:       the duplicates MUST be omitted.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    *  The placeholder apex ZONEMD RR(s) MUST NOT be included.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    *  If the zone is signed, DNSSEC RRs MUST be included, except:
    TEXT[!MUST]:    *  The RRSIG covering the apex ZONEMD RRset MUST NOT be included
    TEXT[!MUST]:       because the RRSIG will be updated after all digests have been
    TEXT[!MUST]:       calculated.

  SECTION: [Update ZONEMD RR](#section-3.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the zone is signed with DNSSEC, the RRSIG record(s) covering the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    ZONEMD RRset MUST then be added or updated.
    TEXT[!MUST]: To
    TEXT[!MUST]:    preserve the calculated digest, generation of a ZONEMD signature MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NOT also result in a change to the SOA serial number.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The ZONEMD RR
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and the matching SOA MUST be published at the same time.

  SECTION: [Verifying Zone Digest](#section-4)
    TEXT[!MAY]: The verifier MAY ignore a ZONEMD RR if its
    TEXT[!MAY]:       |  Scheme and Hash Algorithm violates local policy.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The verifier MUST first determine whether or not to expect DNSSEC
    TEXT[!MUST]:        records in the zone.
    TEXT[!MUST]: For zones where signatures are expected, the existence of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:        apex ZONEMD record MUST be validated.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the DNSSEC data proves the ZONEMD does exist, but is
    TEXT[!MUST]:        not found in the zone, digest verification MUST NOT be considered
    TEXT[!MUST]:        successful.
    TEXT[!MUST]: For zones where signatures are expected, the SOA and ZONEMD
    TEXT[!MUST]:        RRsets MUST have valid signatures, chaining up to a trust anchor.
    TEXT[!MUST]:        If DNSSEC validation of the SOA or ZONEMD RRsets fails, digest
    TEXT[!MUST]:        verification MUST NOT be considered successful.
    TEXT[!MUST]: When multiple ZONEMD RRs are present, each MUST specify a unique
    TEXT[!MUST]:        Scheme and Hash Algorithm tuple.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the ZONEMD RRset contains
    TEXT[!MUST]:        more than one RR with the same Scheme and Hash Algorithm, digest
    TEXT[!MUST]:        verification for those ZONEMD RRs MUST NOT be considered
    TEXT[!MUST]:        successful.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The SOA Serial field MUST exactly match the ZONEMD Serial
    TEXT[!MUST]:            field.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the fields do not match, digest verification MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:            NOT be considered successful with this ZONEMD RR.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The Scheme field MUST be checked.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the verifier does not
    TEXT[!MUST]:            support the given scheme, verification MUST NOT be considered
    TEXT[!MUST]:            successful with this ZONEMD RR.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The Hash Algorithm field MUST be checked.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the verifier
    TEXT[!MUST]:            does not support the given hash algorithm, verification MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:            NOT be considered successful with this ZONEMD RR.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The Digest field size MUST be checked.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the size of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:            given Digest field is smaller than 12 octets, or if the size
    TEXT[!MUST]:            is not equal to the size expected for the corresponding Hash
    TEXT[!MUST]:            Algorithm, verification MUST NOT be considered successful
    TEXT[!MUST]:            with this ZONEMD RR.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Otherwise, verification MUST NOT be considered
    TEXT[!MUST]:            successful for this ZONEMD RR.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Each time zone verification is performed, the verifier SHOULD report
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the status as either successful or unsuccessful.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: When unsuccessful,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the verifier SHOULD report the reason(s) that verification did not
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    succeed.

  SECTION: [Attacks Utilizing ZONEMD Queries](#section-6.5)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Servers SHOULD NOT
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    calculate zone digests dynamically (for each query) as this can be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    used as a CPU resource exhaustion attack.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9018
  SECTION: [Introduction](#section-1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In Section 6 of [RFC7873], for simplicity, it is "RECOMMENDED that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the same Server Secret be used by each DNS server in a set of anycast
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    servers."  However, how precisely a Server Cookie is calculated from
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    this Server Secret is left to the implementation.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: As a result, DNS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Cookies are impractical to deploy on multi-vendor anycast networks
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    because even when all DNS Software shares the same secret, as
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    RECOMMENDED in Section 6 of [RFC7873], the Server Cookie constructed
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    by one implementation cannot generally be validated by another.

  SECTION: [Changes to RFC 7873](#section-2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    These algorithms MUST NOT be used as the resulting cookies are too
    TEXT[!MUST]:    weak when evaluated against modern security standards.
    TEXT[!MUST]: This algorithm is replaced by the interoperable
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specification in Section 4 of this document, which MUST be used by
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Server Cookie implementations.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The previous example in Appendix A.2 of [RFC7873] is NOT
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    RECOMMENDED.

  SECTION: [Constructing a Client Cookie](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: In order to provide minimal
    TEXT[!MUST]:    authentication of the targeted server, a client MUST use a different
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Client Cookie for each different Server IP address.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Client Cookie SHOULD have 64 bits of entropy.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When a server does not support DNS Cookies, the client MUST NOT send
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the same Client Cookie to that same server again.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    However, for privacy reasons, in order to prevent tracking of devices
    TEXT[!MUST]:    across links and to not circumvent IPv6 Privacy Extensions [RFC8981],
    TEXT[!MUST]:    clients MUST NOT reuse a Client or Server Cookie after the Client IP
    TEXT[!MUST]:    address has changed.
    TEXT[!MUST]: In subsequent queries to the server with that Server
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Cookie, the socket MUST be bound to the Client IP address that was
    TEXT[!MUST]:    also used (and registered) when it received the Server Cookie.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Failure to bind MUST then result in a new Client Cookie.

  SECTION: [Constructing a Server Cookie](#section-4)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    For calculation of the Server Cookie, a pseudorandom function is
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    RECOMMENDED with the property that an attacker that does not know the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Server Secret, cannot find (any information about) the Server Secret,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    and cannot create a Server Cookie for any combination of the Client
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Cookie, the series of Sub-Fields specified below, and the client IP
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    address, for which it has not seen a Server Cookie before.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Because
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DNS servers need to use the pseudorandom function in order to verify
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Server Cookies, it is RECOMMENDED that it be efficient to calculate.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Changing the Server Secret regularly is RECOMMENDED but, when a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    secure pseudorandom function is used, it need not be changed too
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    frequently.

  SECTION: [The Reserved Sub-Field](#section-4.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: On construction, it MUST be set
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to zero octets.
    TEXT[!MUST]: On Server Cookie verification, the server MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    enforce those fields to be zero, and the Hash should be computed with
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the received value as described in Section 4.4.

  SECTION: [The Timestamp Sub-Field](#section-4.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Timestamp value prevents Replay Attacks and MUST be checked by
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the server to be within a defined period of time.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The DNS server
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD allow cookies within a 1-hour period in the past and a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    5-minute period into the future to allow operation of low-volume
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    clients and some limited time skew between the DNS servers in the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    anycast set.
    TEXT[!MUST]: All comparisons
    TEXT[!MUST]:    involving these fields MUST use "Serial number arithmetic", as
    TEXT[!MUST]:    defined in [RFC1982].
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The DNS server SHOULD generate a new Server Cookie at least if the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    received Server Cookie from the client is more than half an hour old,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    but it MAY generate a new cookie more often than that.

  SECTION: [The Hash Sub-Field](#section-4.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The length of all the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    concatenated elements (the input into [SipHash-2-4]) MUST be either
    TEXT[!MUST]:    precisely 20 bytes in case of an IPv4 Client-IP or precisely 32 bytes
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in case of an IPv6 Client-IP.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When a DNS server receives a Server Cookie version 1 for validation,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the length of the received COOKIE option MUST be precisely 24 bytes:
    TEXT[!MUST]:    8 bytes for the Client Cookie plus 16 bytes for the Server Cookie.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Verification of the length of the received COOKIE option is REQUIRED
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to guarantee the length of the input into [SipHash-2-4] to be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    precisely 20 bytes in the case of an IPv4 Client-IP and precisely 32
    TEXT[!MUST]:    bytes in the case of an IPv6 Client-IP.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The Server Secret MUST be configurable to make sure that servers in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    an anycast network return consistent results.

  SECTION: [Updating the Server Secret](#section-5)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Changing the Server Secret regularly is RECOMMENDED.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    To facilitate this, deployment of a new Server Secret MUST be done in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    three stages:
    TEXT[!MUST]:       With this stage, the previous Server Secret can be removed and
    TEXT[!MUST]:       MUST NOT be used anymore for verifying.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       It is RECOMMENDED that the operator wait, after initiating Stage 2
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       and before initiating Stage 3, at least a period of time equal to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       the longest TTL in the zones served by the server plus 1 hour.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       The operator SHOULD wait at least longer than the period clients
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       are allowed to use the same Server Cookie, which SHOULD be 1 hour
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       (see Section 4.3).

  SECTION: [Cookie Algorithms](#section-6)
    TEXT[!MUST]: It is REQUIRED that a compliant DNS server use
    TEXT[!MUST]:    SipHash-2-4 as a mandatory and default algorithm for DNS Cookies to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    ensure interoperability between the DNS Implementations.

  SECTION: [Client Cookie Construction](#section-8.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In [RFC7873], it was RECOMMENDED to construct a Client Cookie by
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    using a pseudorandom function of the Client IP address, the Server IP
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    address, and a secret quantity known only to the client.
    TEXT[!MUST]: To prevent tracking, a new Client
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Cookie for a server MUST be created whenever the Client IP address
    TEXT[!MUST]:    changes.
    TEXT[!MUST]: To prevent tracking of
    TEXT[!MUST]:    clients with non-DNS Cookie-supporting servers, a client MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    send a previously sent Client Cookie to a server not known to support
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNS Cookies.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: To prevent the creation of a new Client Cookie for each
