    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    query to a non-DNS Cookie-supporting server, it is RECOMMENDED to not
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    send a Client Cookie to that server for a certain period, for example
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    five minutes.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    *  In order to provide minimal authentication, a client MUST use a
    TEXT[!MUST]:       different Client Cookie for each different Server IP address.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    *  To prevent tracking of clients, a new Client Cookie MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:       created when the Client IP address changes.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    *  To prevent tracking of clients by a non-DNS Cookie-supporting
    TEXT[!MUST]:       server, a client MUST NOT send a previously sent Client Cookie to
    TEXT[!MUST]:       a server in the absence of an associated Server Cookie.

  SECTION: [The Same Client Learning a Renewed (Fresh) Server Cookie](#appendix-A.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The server SHOULD do this because it can see the Server
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Cookie sent by the client is older than half an hour (Section 4.3),
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    but it is also fine for a server to generate a new Server Cookie
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    sooner or even for every answer.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9077
  SECTION: [Introduction](#section-1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  The NSEC RR SHOULD have the same TTL value as the SOA minimum TTL
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  field.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  A resolver that supports aggressive use of NSEC and NSEC3 SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  reduce the TTL of NSEC and NSEC3 records to match the SOA.MINIMUM
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  field in the authority section of a negative response, if
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  SOA.MINIMUM is smaller.

  SECTION: [NSEC and NSEC3 TTL Changes](#section-3)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    [RFC4034], [RFC4035], and [RFC5155] use the SHOULD requirement level,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    but they were written prior to the publication of [RFC8198] when
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    [RFC4035] still said:
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  ...DNSSEC-enabled validating resolvers SHOULD use wildcards and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  NSEC/NSEC3 resource records to generate positive and negative
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  responses until the effective TTLs or signatures for those records
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  expire.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Because of that, the updates in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    this document upgrade the requirement level to MUST.

  SECTION: [Updates to RFC 4034](#section-3.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  The NSEC RR SHOULD have the same TTL value as the SOA minimum TTL
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  field.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |  The TTL of the NSEC RR that is returned MUST be the lesser of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |  MINIMUM field of the SOA record and the TTL of the SOA itself.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Because some signers incrementally update the NSEC
    TEXT[!MAY]:    |  chain, a transient inconsistency between the observed and expected
    TEXT[!MAY]:    |  TTL MAY exist.

  SECTION: [Updates to RFC 4035](#section-3.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  The TTL value for any NSEC RR SHOULD be the same as the minimum
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  TTL value field in the zone SOA RR.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |  The TTL of the NSEC RR that is returned MUST be the lesser of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |  MINIMUM field of the SOA record and the TTL of the SOA itself.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Because some signers incrementally update the NSEC
    TEXT[!MAY]:    |  chain, a transient inconsistency between the observed and expected
    TEXT[!MAY]:    |  TTL MAY exist.

  SECTION: [Updates to RFC 5155](#section-3.3)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  The NSEC3 RR SHOULD have the same TTL value as the SOA minimum TTL
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  field.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |  The TTL of the NSEC3 RR that is returned MUST be the lesser of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |  MINIMUM field of the SOA record and the TTL of the SOA itself.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Because some signers incrementally update the NSEC3
    TEXT[!MAY]:    |  chain, a transient inconsistency between the observed and expected
    TEXT[!MAY]:    |  TTL MAY exist.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  *  The TTL value for any NSEC3 RR SHOULD be the same as the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |     minimum TTL value field in the zone SOA RR.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |  *  The TTL value for each NSEC3 RR MUST be the lesser of the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |     MINIMUM field of the zone SOA RR and the TTL of the zone SOA RR
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |     itself.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Because some signers incrementally update the NSEC3
    TEXT[!MAY]:    |     chain, a transient inconsistency between the observed and
    TEXT[!MAY]:    |     expected TTL MAY exist.

  SECTION: [Updates to RFC 8198](#section-3.4)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: It is RECOMMENDED that validating
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  resolvers limit the maximum effective TTL value of negative
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  responses (NSEC/NSEC3 RRs) to this same value.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    |  A resolver that supports aggressive use of NSEC and NSEC3 MAY
    TEXT[!MAY]:    |  limit the TTL of NSEC and NSEC3 records to the lesser of the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    |  SOA.MINIMUM field and the TTL of the SOA in a response, if
    TEXT[!MAY]:    |  present.
    TEXT[!MAY]: It MAY also use a previously cached SOA for a zone to
    TEXT[!MAY]:    |  find these values.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9103
  SECTION: [Updates to Existing Specifications](#section-6)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    *  Implementations MUST use [RFC7766] ("DNS Transport over TCP -
    TEXT[!MUST]:       Implementation Requirements") to optimize the use of TCP
    TEXT[!MUST]:       connections.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    *  Whilst [RFC7766] states that "DNS clients SHOULD pipeline their
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       queries" on TCP connections, it did not distinguish between XFRs
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       and other queries for this behavior.
    TEXT[!MAY]: For these reasons, it is
    TEXT[!MAY]:       clarified here that a valid reason for not pipelining queries is
    TEXT[!MAY]:       when they are all XFR queries, i.e., clients sending multiple XFRs
    TEXT[!MAY]:       MAY choose not to pipeline those queries.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    *  Implementations SHOULD use the edns-tcp-keepalive EDNS(0) option
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       [RFC7828] to manage persistent connections.

  SECTION: [Update to RFC 1995 for IXFR over TCP](#section-6.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    For clarity, an IXFR-over-TCP server compliant with this
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specification MUST be able to handle multiple concurrent IXoT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    requests on a single TCP connection (for the same and different
    TEXT[!MUST]:    zones) and SHOULD send the responses as soon as they are available,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    which might be out of order compared to the requests.

  SECTION: [Update to RFC 5936 for AXFR over TCP](#section-6.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    For clarity, an AXFR-over-TCP server compliant with this
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specification MUST be able to handle multiple concurrent AXoT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    sessions on a single TCP connection (for the same and different
    TEXT[!MUST]:    zones).
    TEXT[!MUST]: The response streams for concurrent AXFRs MAY be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    intermingled, and AXFR-over-TCP clients compliant with this
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specification, which pipeline AXFR requests, MUST be able to handle
    TEXT[!MUST]:    this.

  SECTION: [Connection Reuse](#section-6.3.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    As specified, XFR-over-TCP clients SHOULD reuse any existing open TCP
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    connection when starting any new XFR request to the same primary, and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    for issuing SOA queries, instead of opening a new connection.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    number of TCP connections between a secondary and primary SHOULD be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    minimized (also see Section 6.4).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: In this case,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       the number of concurrent connections for zone transfers SHOULD be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       limited to the total number of zones transferred between the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       client and server.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    If no TCP connections are currently open, XFR clients MAY send SOA
    TEXT[!MAY]:    queries over UDP or a new TCP connection.

  SECTION: [AXFRs and IXFRs on the Same Connection](#section-6.3.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In this document, the above is clarified to indicate that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    implementations capable of both AXFR and IXFR and compliant with this
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    specification SHOULD:
    TEXT[!MAY]:    *  pipeline such requests (if they pipeline XFR requests in general)
    TEXT[!MAY]:       and MAY intermingle them, and
    TEXT[!MAY]:    *  send the response(s) for each request as soon as they are
    TEXT[!MAY]:       available, i.e., responses MAY be sent intermingled.

  SECTION: [XFR Limits](#section-6.3.3)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    The server MAY limit the number of concurrent IXFRs, AXFRs, or total
    TEXT[!MAY]:    XFR transfers in progress (or from a given secondary) to protect
    TEXT[!MAY]:    server resources.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Servers SHOULD return SERVFAIL if this limit is
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    hit, since it is a transient error and a retry at a later time might
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    succeed (there is no previous specification for this behavior).

  SECTION: [The edns-tcp-keepalive EDNS(0) Option](#section-6.3.4)
    TEXT[!MAY]: If the server
    TEXT[!MAY]:    does not support edns-tcp-keepalive, the client MAY keep the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    connection open for a few seconds ([RFC7766] recommends that servers
    TEXT[!MAY]:    use timeouts of at least a few seconds).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |  If an OPT record is present in a received request, compliant
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |  responders MUST include an OPT record in their respective
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |  responses.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In this document, the above is clarified to indicate that if an OPT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    record is present in a received AXFR request, compliant responders
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST include an OPT record in each of the subsequent AXFR responses.

  SECTION: [Update to RFC 7766](#section-6.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |  To mitigate the risk of unintentional server overload, DNS clients
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |  MUST take care to minimize the number of concurrent TCP
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |  connections made to any individual server.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: It is RECOMMENDED that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  for any given client/server interaction there SHOULD be no more
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  than one connection for regular queries, one for zone transfers,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  and one for each protocol that is being used on top of TCP (for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  example, if the resolver was using TLS).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Therefore, it is RECOMMENDED that for each protocol used on top of
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    TCP in any given client/server interaction there SHOULD be no more
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    than one connection for regular queries and one for zone transfers.

  SECTION: [Connection Establishment](#section-7.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    During connection establishment, the Application-Layer Protocol
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Negotiation (ALPN) token "dot" [DoT-ALPN] MUST be selected in the TLS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    handshake.

  SECTION: [TLS Versions](#section-7.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    All implementations of this specification MUST use only TLS 1.3
    TEXT[!MUST]:    [RFC8446] or later.

  SECTION: [Port Selection](#section-7.3)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The connection for XoT SHOULD be established using port 853, as
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    specified in [RFC7858], unless there is mutual agreement between the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    primary and secondary to use a port other than port 853 for XoT.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    There MAY be agreement to use different ports for AXoT and IXoT or
    TEXT[!MAY]:    for different zones.

  SECTION: [XoT Transfers](#section-7.5)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    For a zone transfer between two endpoints to be considered protected
    TEXT[!MUST]:    with XoT, all XFR requests and responses for that zone MUST be sent
    TEXT[!MUST]:    over TLS connections, where at a minimum:
    TEXT[!MUST]:    *  The client MUST authenticate the server by use of an
    TEXT[!MUST]:       authentication domain name using a Strict Privacy profile, as
    TEXT[!MUST]:       described in [RFC8310].
    TEXT[!MUST]:    *  The server MUST validate the client is authorized to request or
    TEXT[!MUST]:       proxy a zone transfer by using one or both of the following
    TEXT[!MUST]:       methods:

  SECTION: [XoT Connections](#section-7.6)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    If no TLS connections are currently open, XoT clients MAY send SOA
    TEXT[!MAY]:    queries over UDP, TCP, or TLS.

  SECTION: [Response RCODES](#section-7.8)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    XoT clients and servers MUST implement EDE codes.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If a XoT server
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    receives non-XoT traffic it is not willing to answer on a TLS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    connection, it SHOULD respond with REFUSED and the extended DNS error
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    code 21 - Not Supported [RFC8914].

  SECTION: [Padding AXoT Responses](#section-7.9.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    However, as with existing AXFR, the last AXoT response message sent
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST contain the same SOA that was in the first message of the AXoT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response series in order to signal the conclusion of the zone
    TEXT[!MUST]:    transfer.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  Each AXFR response message SHOULD contain a sufficient number of
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  RRs to reasonably amortize the per-message overhead, up to the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  largest number that will fit within a DNS message (taking the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  required content of the other sections into account, as described
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    |  below).
    TEXT[!MUST]: For
    TEXT[!MUST]:    flexibility, for future proofing, and in order to guarantee support
    TEXT[!MUST]:    for future padding policies, it is stated here that secondary
    TEXT[!MUST]:    implementations MUST be resilient to receiving padded AXoT responses,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    including 'empty' AXoT responses that contain only an OPT RR
    TEXT[!MUST]:    containing the EDNS(0) option for padding.

  SECTION: [Condensation of Responses](#section-7.10.1)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    [RFC1995] says that condensation of responses is optional and MAY be
    TEXT[!MAY]:    done.

  SECTION: [Fallback to AXFR](#section-7.10.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Just as with IXFR over TCP, after a failed IXFR, an IXoT client
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD request the AXFR on the already open XoT connection.

  SECTION: [Padding of IXoT Responses](#section-7.10.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In order to guarantee support for future padding policies, it is
    TEXT[!MUST]:    stated here that secondary implementations MUST be resilient to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    receiving padded IXoT responses.

  SECTION: [Opportunistic TLS](#section-9.3.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    *  if clients know authentication information for a server, they
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       SHOULD try to authenticate the server,
    TEXT[!MAY]:    *  if this fails or clients do not know the information, they MAY
    TEXT[!MAY]:       fallback to using TLS without authentication, or
    TEXT[!MAY]:    *  clients MAY fallback to using cleartext if TLS is not available.

  SECTION: [Strict TLS](#section-9.3.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Strict TLS for DoT [RFC8310] requires that a client is configured
    TEXT[!MUST]:    with an authentication domain name (and/or Subject Public Key Info
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (SPKI) pin set) that MUST be used to authenticate the TLS handshake
    TEXT[!MUST]:    with the server.

  SECTION: [Policies for Both AXoT and IXoT](#section-11)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In order to assure the confidentiality of the zone information, the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    entire transfer group MUST have a consistent policy of using XoT.
    TEXT[!MUST]: For
    TEXT[!MUST]:    clarification, this means that within any transfer group both AXFRs
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and IXFRs for a zone MUST all use XoT.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A XoT policy MUST specify if:

  SECTION: [Operational Considerations](#section-13)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the options described in Section 12 are available, such
    TEXT[!MUST]:    configuration options MUST only be used in a 'migration mode' and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    therefore should be used with great care.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9156
  SECTION: [Limitation of the Number of Queries](#section-2.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: Resolvers
    TEXT[!MUST]:    supporting QNAME minimisation MUST implement a mechanism to limit the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    number of outgoing queries per user request.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    One mechanism that MAY be used to reduce this attack vector is by
    TEXT[!MAY]:    appending more than one label per iteration for QNAMEs with a large
    TEXT[!MAY]:    number of labels.
    TEXT[!MUST]: To do this, a maximum number of QNAME minimisation
    TEXT[!MUST]:    iterations MUST be selected (MAX_MINIMISE_COUNT); a RECOMMENDED value
    TEXT[!MUST]:    is 10.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Optionally, a value for the number of queries that should
    TEXT[!MAY]:    only have one label appended MAY be selected (MINIMISE_ONE_LAB); a
    TEXT[!MAY]:    good value is 4.

  SECTION: [Implementation by Stub and Forwarding Resolvers](#section-2.4)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Stub and forwarding resolvers MAY implement QNAME minimisation.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9250
  SECTION: [Port Selection](#section-4.1.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    By default, a DNS server that supports DoQ MUST listen for and accept
    TEXT[!MUST]:    QUIC connections on the dedicated UDP port 853 (Section 8), unless
    TEXT[!MUST]:    there is a mutual agreement to use another port.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    By default, a DNS client desiring to use DoQ with a particular server
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST establish a QUIC connection to UDP port 853 on the server,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    unless there is a mutual agreement to use another port.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DoQ connections MUST NOT use UDP port 53.

  SECTION: [Stream Mapping and Usage](#section-4.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    All DNS messages (queries and responses) sent over DoQ connections
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST be encoded as a 2-octet length field followed by the message
    TEXT[!MUST]:    content as specified in [RFC1035].
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The client MUST select the next available client-initiated
    TEXT[!MUST]:    bidirectional stream for each subsequent query on a QUIC connection,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in conformance with the QUIC transport specification [RFC9000].
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Servers SHOULD process queries as they arrive,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    as not doing so would cause unnecessary delays.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The client MUST send the DNS query over the selected stream and MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    indicate through the STREAM FIN mechanism that no further data will
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be sent on that stream.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The server MUST send the response(s) on the same stream and MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    indicate, after the last response, through the STREAM FIN mechanism
    TEXT[!MUST]:    that no further data will be sent on that stream.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Servers MAY defer processing of a query until the STREAM FIN has been
    TEXT[!MAY]:    indicated on the stream selected by the client.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Servers and clients MAY monitor the number of "dangling" streams.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Implementations MAY impose a limit on the number of such dangling
    TEXT[!MAY]:    streams.
    TEXT[!MAY]: If limits are encountered, implementations MAY close the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    connection.

  SECTION: [DNS Message IDs](#section-4.2.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When sending queries over a QUIC connection, the DNS Message ID MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be set to 0.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When forwarding a DNS message from DoQ over another transport, a DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Message ID MUST be generated according to the rules of the protocol
    TEXT[!MUST]:    that is in use.
    TEXT[!MUST]: When forwarding a DNS message from another transport
    TEXT[!MUST]:    over DoQ, the Message ID MUST be set to 0.

  SECTION: [Transaction Cancellation](#section-4.3.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: If a DoQ client wishes to cancel an outstanding
    TEXT[!MUST]:    request, it MUST issue a QUIC STOP_SENDING, and it SHOULD use the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    error code DOQ_REQUEST_CANCELLED.
    TEXT[!MAY]: It MAY use a more specific error
    TEXT[!MAY]:    code registered according to Section 8.4.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The corresponding DNS transaction
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST be abandoned.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Servers SHOULD NOT continue processing a DNS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    transaction if they receive a STOP_SENDING.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Servers MAY impose implementation limits on the total number or rate
    TEXT[!MAY]:    of cancellation requests.
    TEXT[!MAY]: If limits are encountered, servers MAY
    TEXT[!MAY]:    close the connection.
    TEXT[!MAY]: In this case, servers wanting to help client
    TEXT[!MAY]:    debugging MAY use the error code DOQ_EXCESSIVE_LOAD.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Servers MUST NOT continue processing a DNS transaction if they
    TEXT[!MUST]:    receive a RESET_STREAM request from the client before the client
    TEXT[!MUST]:    indicates the STREAM FIN.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The server MUST issue a RESET_STREAM to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    indicate that the transaction is abandoned unless:

  SECTION: [Transaction Errors](#section-4.3.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: For example, a client SHOULD be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    notified of a Server Failure (SERVFAIL, [RFC1035]) through a response
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    with the Response Code set to SERVFAIL.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If a server is incapable of sending a DNS response due to an internal
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    error, it SHOULD issue a QUIC RESET_STREAM frame.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: The error code
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD be set to DOQ_INTERNAL_ERROR.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The corresponding DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    transaction MUST be abandoned.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Clients MAY limit the number of
    TEXT[!MAY]:    unsolicited QUIC RESET_STREAM frames received on a connection before
    TEXT[!MAY]:    choosing to close the connection.

  SECTION: [Protocol Errors](#section-4.3.3)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: It SHOULD forcibly abort the connection using QUIC's
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    CONNECTION_CLOSE mechanism and SHOULD use the DoQ error code
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DOQ_PROTOCOL_ERROR.
    TEXT[!MAY]: In some cases, it MAY instead silently abandon
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the connection, which uses fewer of the local resources but makes
    TEXT[!MAY]:    debugging at the offending node more difficult.

  SECTION: [Alternative Error Codes](#section-4.3.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Because new error codes can be defined without negotiation, use of an
    TEXT[!MUST]:    error code in an unexpected context or receipt of an unknown error
    TEXT[!MUST]:    code MUST be treated as equivalent to DOQ_UNSPECIFIED_ERROR.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Implementations MAY wish to test the support for the error code
    TEXT[!MAY]:    extension mechanism by using error codes not listed in this document,
    TEXT[!MAY]:    or they MAY use DOQ_ERROR_RESERVED.

  SECTION: [Connection Management](#section-4.4)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Clients and servers implementing DoQ SHOULD negotiate use of the idle
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    timeout.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Clients SHOULD monitor the idle time incurred on their connection to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the server, defined by the time spent since the last packet from the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    server has been received.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: When a client prepares to send a new DNS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    query to the server, it SHOULD check whether the idle time is
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    sufficiently lower than the idle timer.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If it is, the client SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    send the DNS query over the existing connection.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If not, the client
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD establish a new connection and send the query over that
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    connection.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Clients MAY discard their connections to the server before the idle
    TEXT[!MAY]:    timeout expires.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: A client that has outstanding queries SHOULD close
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the connection explicitly using QUIC's CONNECTION_CLOSE mechanism and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the DoQ error code DOQ_NO_ERROR.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Clients and servers MAY close the connection for a variety of other
    TEXT[!MAY]:    reasons, indicated using QUIC's CONNECTION_CLOSE.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If a connection fails, all the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in-progress transactions on that connection MUST be abandoned.

  SECTION: [Session Resumption and 0-RTT](#section-4.5)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    A client MAY take advantage of the session resumption and 0-RTT
    TEXT[!MAY]:    mechanisms supported by QUIC transport [RFC9000] and QUIC TLS
    TEXT[!MAY]:    [RFC9001] if the server supports them.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Clients SHOULD consider
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    potential privacy issues associated with session resumption before
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    deciding to use this mechanism and specifically evaluate the trade-
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    offs presented in the various sections of this document.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The 0-RTT mechanism MUST NOT be used to send DNS requests that are
    TEXT[!MUST]:    not "replayable" transactions.
    TEXT[!MUST]: In this specification, only
    TEXT[!MUST]:    transactions that have an OPCODE of QUERY or NOTIFY are considered
    TEXT[!MUST]:    replayable; therefore, other OPCODES MUST NOT be sent in 0-RTT data.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Servers MAY support session resumption, and MAY do that with or
    TEXT[!MAY]:    without supporting 0-RTT, using the mechanisms described in
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Section 4.6.1 of [RFC9001].
    TEXT[!MUST]: Servers supporting 0-RTT MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    immediately process non-replayable transactions received in 0-RTT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    data but instead MUST adopt one of the following behaviors:

  SECTION: [Authentication](#section-5.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: [RFC8932] states that DNS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    privacy services SHOULD provide credentials that clients can use to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    authenticate the server.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Given this, and to align with the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    authentication model for DoH, DoQ stubs SHOULD use a Strict usage
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    profile.

  SECTION: [Fallback to Other Protocols on Connection Failure](#section-5.2)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    If the establishment of the DoQ connection fails, clients MAY attempt
    TEXT[!MAY]:    to fall back to DoT and then potentially cleartext, as specified in
    TEXT[!MAY]:    DoT [RFC7858] and "Usage Profiles for DNS over TLS and DNS over DTLS"
    TEXT[!MAY]:    [RFC8310], depending on their usage profile.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DNS clients SHOULD remember server IP addresses that don't support
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DoQ.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Clients SHOULD NOT
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    attempt DoQ queries to a server that does not support DoQ for a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    reasonable period (such as one hour per server).
    TEXT[!MAY]: DNS clients
    TEXT[!MAY]:    following an out-of-band key-pinned usage profile [RFC7858] MAY be
    TEXT[!MAY]:    more aggressive about retrying after DoQ connection failures.

  SECTION: [Address Validation](#section-5.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: DoQ implementations MUST conform to this
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specification, which limits the worst-case amplification to a factor
    TEXT[!MUST]:    3.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DoQ implementations SHOULD consider configuring servers to use the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Address Validation using Retry Packets procedure defined in
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Section 8.1.2 of [RFC9000], the QUIC transport specification.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DoQ implementations that configure Address Validation using Retry
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Packets SHOULD implement the Address Validation for Future
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Connections procedure defined in Section 8.1.3 of [RFC9000], the QUIC
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    transport specification.

  SECTION: [Padding](#section-5.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Implementations MUST protect against the traffic analysis attacks
    TEXT[!MUST]:    described in Section 7.5 by the judicious injection of padding.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    *  If the implementation of QUIC exposes APIs to set a padding
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       policy, DoQ SHOULD use that API to align the packet length to a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:       small set of fixed sizes.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    *  If padding at the QUIC packet level is not available or not used,
    TEXT[!MUST]:       DoQ MUST ensure that all DNS queries and responses are padded to a
    TEXT[!MUST]:       small set of fixed sizes, using the EDNS(0) padding extension as
    TEXT[!MUST]:       specified in [RFC7830].
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In the absence of a standard policy for padding sizes,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    implementations SHOULD follow the recommendations of the Experimental
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    status "Padding Policies for Extension Mechanisms for DNS (EDNS(0))"
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    [RFC8467].

  SECTION: [Connection Reuse](#section-5.5.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: To amortize connection setup
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    costs, both clients and servers SHOULD support connection reuse by
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    sending multiple queries and responses over a single persistent QUIC
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    connection.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    In order to achieve performance on par with UDP, DNS clients SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    send their queries concurrently over the QUIC streams on a QUIC
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    connection.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: That is, when a DNS client sends multiple queries to a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    server over a QUIC connection, it SHOULD NOT wait for an outstanding
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    reply before sending the next query.

  SECTION: [Resource Management](#section-5.5.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    An implementation of DoQ SHOULD follow best practices similar to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    those specified for DNS over TCP [RFC7766], in particular with regard
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    to:
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Clients that want to maintain long duration DoQ connections SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    use the idle timeout mechanisms defined in Section 10.1 of [RFC9000],
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the QUIC transport specification.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Clients and servers MUST NOT send
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the edns-tcp-keepalive EDNS(0) Option [RFC7828] in any messages sent
    TEXT[!MUST]:    on a DoQ connection (because it is specific to the use of TCP/TLS as
    TEXT[!MUST]:    a transport).

  SECTION: [Using 0-RTT and Session Resumption](#section-5.5.3)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Clients SHOULD use resumption tickets only once, as specified in
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Appendix C.4 of [RFC8446].
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: By default, clients SHOULD NOT use
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    session resumption if the client's connectivity has changed.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Clients SHOULD only use
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the address validation tokens when they are also using session
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    resumption thus avoiding additional tracking risks.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Servers SHOULD issue session resumption tickets with a sufficiently
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    long lifetime (e.g., 6 hours), so that clients are not tempted to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    either keep the connection alive or frequently poll the server to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    renew session resumption tickets.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Servers SHOULD implement the anti-
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    replay mechanisms specified in Section 8 of [RFC8446].

  SECTION: [Controlling Connection Migration for Privacy](#section-5.5.4)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: By default, clients SHOULD be configured to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    prioritize privacy and start new sessions if their connectivity
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    changes.

  SECTION: [Processing Queries in Parallel](#section-5.6)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    As specified in Section 7 of [RFC7766] "DNS Transport over TCP -
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Implementation Requirements", resolvers are RECOMMENDED to support
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the preparing of responses in parallel and sending them out of order.

  SECTION: [Zone Transfer](#section-5.7)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    *  DoQ servers MUST be able to handle multiple concurrent IXFR
    TEXT[!MUST]:       requests on a single QUIC connection.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    *  DoQ servers MUST be able to handle multiple concurrent AXFR
    TEXT[!MUST]:       requests on a single QUIC connection.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    *  DoQ implementations SHOULD
    TEXT[!MAY]:       -  send the response(s) for each request as soon as they are
    TEXT[!MAY]:          available, i.e., response streams MAY be sent intermingled

  SECTION: [Traffic Analysis](#section-7.5)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Implementations SHOULD use the mechanisms defined in Section 5.4 to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    mitigate this attack.

  SECTION: [DNS-over-QUIC Error Codes Registry](#section-8.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Registrations in this registry MUST include the following fields:
    TEXT[!MUST]:    In addition, permanent registrations MUST include:
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Description:  A brief description of the error code semantics, which
    TEXT[!MAY]:       MAY be a summary if a specification reference is provided
    TEXT[!MUST]: In addition to the parameters listed above, provisional
    TEXT[!MUST]:    registrations MUST include:

  SECTION: [The NOTIFY Service](#appendix-A)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Section 4.5 says "The 0-RTT mechanism MUST NOT be used to send DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    requests that are not "replayable" transactions".

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9276
  SECTION: [Best Practice for Zone Publishers](#section-3.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    First, if the operational or security features of NSEC3 are not
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    needed, then NSEC SHOULD be used in preference to NSEC3.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If NSEC3 must be used, then an iterations count of 0 MUST be used to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    alleviate computational burdens.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    For small zones, the use of opt-out-based NSEC3 records is NOT
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    RECOMMENDED.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    For very large and sparsely signed zones, where the majority of the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    records are insecure delegations, opt-out MAY be used.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Operators SHOULD NOT use a salt by indicating a zero-length salt
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    value instead (represented as a "-" in the presentation format).

  SECTION: [Recommendation for Validating Resolvers](#section-3.2)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Validating resolvers MAY return an insecure response to their clients
    TEXT[!MAY]:    when processing NSEC3 records with iterations larger than 0.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Note
    TEXT[!MUST]:    also that a validating resolver returning an insecure response MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    still validate the signature over the NSEC3 record to ensure the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    iteration count was not altered since record publication (see
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Section 10.3 of [RFC5155]).
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Validating resolvers MAY also return a SERVFAIL response when
    TEXT[!MAY]:    processing NSEC3 records with iterations larger than 0.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Validating
    TEXT[!MAY]:    resolvers MAY choose to ignore authoritative server responses with
    TEXT[!MAY]:    iteration counts greater than 0, which will likely result in
    TEXT[!MAY]:    returning a SERVFAIL to the client when no acceptable responses are
    TEXT[!MAY]:    received from authoritative servers.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Validating resolvers returning an insecure or SERVFAIL answer to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    their client after receiving and validating an unsupported NSEC3
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    parameter from the authoritative server(s) SHOULD return an Extended
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    DNS Error (EDE) [RFC8914] EDNS0 option of value 27.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Validating
    TEXT[!MUST]:    resolvers that choose to ignore a response with an unsupported
    TEXT[!MUST]:    iteration count (and that do not validate the signature) MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    return this EDE option.

  SECTION: [Security Considerations](#section-4)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Thus, validating resolver operators and software implementers SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    set the point above which a zone is treated as insecure for certain
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    values of NSEC3 iterations to the same as the point where a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    validating resolver begins returning SERVFAIL.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9460
  SECTION: [Zone-File Presentation Format](#section-2.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Each SvcParamKey SHALL appear at most once in the SvcParams.
    TEXT[!MUST]: A SvcParam in this form SHALL be parsed as
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specified above, and the decoded value SHALL be used as its wire-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    format encoding.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Presentation formats for such keys SHOULD use a comma-
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    separated list (Appendix A.1).
    TEXT[!MUST]:    SvcParams in presentation format MAY appear in any order, but keys
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST NOT be repeated.

  SECTION: [RDATA Wire Format](#section-2.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    SvcParamKeys SHALL appear in increasing numeric order.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Clients MUST consider an RR malformed if:
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If any RRs are malformed, the client MUST reject the entire RRset and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    fall back to non-SVCB connection establishment.

  SECTION: [SVCB Query Names](#section-2.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: This follows the Attrleaf naming
    TEXT[!MUST]:    pattern [Attrleaf], so the scheme MUST be registered appropriately
    TEXT[!MUST]:    with IANA (see Section 11).
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Protocol mapping documents MAY specify additional underscore-prefixed
    TEXT[!MAY]:    labels to be prepended.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When a prior CNAME or SVCB record has aliased to a SVCB record, each
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RR SHALL be returned under its own owner name, as in ordinary CNAME
    TEXT[!MUST]:    processing ([RFC1034], Section 3.6.2).
    TEXT[!MUST]: For example, TLS clients MUST continue to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    validate TLS certificates for the original service name.

  SECTION: [SvcPriority](#section-2.4.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Within a SVCB RRset, all RRs SHOULD have the same mode.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If an RRset
    TEXT[!MUST]:    contains a record in AliasMode, the recipient MUST ignore any
    TEXT[!MUST]:    ServiceMode records in the set.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    When receiving an RRset containing multiple SVCB records with the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    same SvcPriority value, clients SHOULD apply a random shuffle within
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    a priority level to the records before using them, to ensure uniform
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    load balancing.

  SECTION: [AliasMode](#section-2.4.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SVCB RRsets SHOULD only have a single RR in AliasMode.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If multiple
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    AliasMode RRs are present, clients or recursive resolvers SHOULD pick
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    one at random.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The AliasMode TargetName SHOULD NOT be equal to the owner name, as
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    this would result in a loop.
    TEXT[!MUST]: In AliasMode, recipients MUST ignore
    TEXT[!MUST]:    any SvcParams that are present.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Zone-file parsers MAY emit a warning
    TEXT[!MAY]:    if an AliasMode record has SvcParams.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Note that the SVCB record's owner name MAY be the canonical name of a
    TEXT[!MAY]:    CNAME record, and the TargetName MAY be the owner of a CNAME record.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Clients and recursive resolvers MUST follow CNAMEs as normal.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    To avoid unbounded alias chains, clients and recursive resolvers MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    impose a limit on the total number of SVCB aliases they will follow
    TEXT[!MUST]:    for each resolution request.
    TEXT[!MUST]: This limit MUST NOT be zero, i.e.,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    implementations MUST be able to follow at least one AliasMode record.

  SECTION: [ServiceMode](#section-2.4.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Each protocol scheme that uses SVCB MUST define a protocol mapping
    TEXT[!MUST]:    that explains how SvcParams are applied for connections of that
    TEXT[!MUST]:    scheme.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Unless specified otherwise by the protocol mapping, clients
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST ignore any SvcParam that they do not recognize.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Clients MUST reject any RR
    TEXT[!MUST]:    whose recognized SvcParams are not self-consistent and MAY reject the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    entire RRset.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: To help zone operators avoid this condition, zone-file
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    implementations SHOULD enforce self-consistency as well.

  SECTION: [AliasMode](#section-2.5.1)
    TEXT[!MAY]: This indication is
    TEXT[!MAY]:    advisory: clients encountering this indication MAY ignore it and
    TEXT[!MAY]:    attempt to connect without the use of SVCB.

  SECTION: [ServiceMode](#section-2.5.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    For ServiceMode SVCB RRs, if TargetName has the value ".", then the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    owner name of this record MUST be used as the effective TargetName.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the record has a wildcard owner name in the zone file, the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    recipient SHALL use the response's synthesized owner name as the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    effective TargetName.

  SECTION: [Client Behavior](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Clients for pre-existing protocols (e.g., HTTP) SHALL implement SVCB-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    optional behavior (except as noted in Section 3.1 or when modified by
    TEXT[!MUST]:    future specifications).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SVCB-optional clients SHOULD issue in parallel any other DNS queries
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    that might be needed for connection establishment if the SVCB record
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    is absent, in order to minimize delay in that case and enable the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    optimizations discussed in Section 5.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Once SVCB resolution has concluded, whether successful or not, if at
    TEXT[!MUST]:    least one AliasMode record was processed, SVCB-optional clients SHALL
    TEXT[!MUST]:    append to the list of endpoints an endpoint consisting of the final
    TEXT[!MUST]:    value of $QNAME, the authority endpoint's port number, and no
    TEXT[!MUST]:    SvcParams.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Clients SHOULD try higher-priority alternatives first,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    with fallback to lower-priority alternatives.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Clients resolve AAAA
    TEXT[!MAY]:    and/or A records for the selected TargetName and MAY choose between
    TEXT[!MAY]:    them using an approach such as Happy Eyeballs [HappyEyeballsV2].

  SECTION: [Handling Resolution Failures](#section-3.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If DNS responses are cryptographically protected (e.g., using DNSSEC
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    or TLS [DoT] [DoH]) and SVCB resolution fails due to an
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    authentication error, SERVFAIL response, transport error, or timeout,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the client SHOULD abandon its attempt to reach the service, even if
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the client is SVCB-optional.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If the client enforces DNSSEC validation on A/AAAA responses, it
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD apply the same validation policy to SVCB.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    If DNS responses are not cryptographically protected, clients MAY
    TEXT[!MAY]:    treat SVCB resolution failure as fatal or nonfatal.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If the client is unable to complete SVCB resolution due to its chain
    TEXT[!MUST]:    length limit, the client MUST fall back to the authority endpoint, as
    TEXT[!MUST]:    if the service's SVCB record did not exist.

  SECTION: [Clients Using a Proxy](#section-3.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Clients in this configuration SHOULD arrange
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    for a separate SVCB resolution procedure with appropriate privacy
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    properties.
    TEXT[!MUST]: If this is not possible, SVCB-optional clients MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    disable SVCB resolution entirely, and SVCB-reliant clients MUST treat
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the configuration as invalid.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If the client does use SVCB and named destinations, the client SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    follow the standard SVCB resolution process, selecting the smallest-
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SvcPriority option that is compatible with the client and the proxy.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When connecting using a SVCB record, clients MUST provide the final
    TEXT[!MUST]:    TargetName and port to the proxy, which will perform any required A
    TEXT[!MUST]:    and AAAA lookups.

  SECTION: [Authoritative Servers](#section-4.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    When replying to a SVCB query, authoritative DNS servers SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    return A, AAAA, and SVCB records in the Additional section for any
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    TargetNames that are in the zone.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If the zone is signed, the server
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD also include DNSSEC records authenticating the existence or
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    nonexistence of these records in the Additional section.

  SECTION: [Recursive Resolvers](#section-4.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Recursive resolvers
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    that are aware of SVCB SHOULD help the client to execute the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    procedure in Section 3 with minimum overall latency by incorporating
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    additional useful information into the Additional section of the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    response as follows:
    TEXT[!MUST]: Errors or anomalies in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    obtaining additional records MAY cause this process to terminate but
    TEXT[!MUST]:    MUST NOT themselves cause the resolver to send a failure response.

  SECTION: [DNS64](#section-4.2.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: SVCB-aware DNS64
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    resolvers SHOULD apply the same synthesis logic when resolving AAAA
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    records for the TargetName for inclusion in the Additional section
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    (Step 2 in Section 4.2) and MAY omit the A records from this section.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNS64 resolvers MUST NOT extrapolate the AAAA synthesis logic to the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    IP hints in the SvcParams (Section 7.3).

  SECTION: [General Requirements](#section-4.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Recursive resolvers MUST be able to convey SVCB records with
    TEXT[!MUST]:    unrecognized SvcParamKeys.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Resolvers MAY accomplish this by treating
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the entire SvcParams portion of the record as opaque, even if the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    contents are invalid.
    TEXT[!MAY]: If a recognized SvcParamKey is followed by a
    TEXT[!MAY]:    value that is invalid according to the SvcParam's specification, a
    TEXT[!MAY]:    recursive resolver MAY report an error such as SERVFAIL instead of
    TEXT[!MAY]:    returning the record.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: For complex value types whose interpretation
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    might differ between implementations or have additional future
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    allowed values added (e.g., URIs or "alpn"), resolvers SHOULD limit
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    validation to specified constraints.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When responding to a query that includes the DNSSEC OK bit [RFC3225],
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNSSEC-capable recursive and authoritative DNS servers MUST accompany
    TEXT[!MUST]:    each RRset in the Additional section with the same DNSSEC-related
    TEXT[!MUST]:    records that they would send when providing that RRset as an Answer
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (e.g., RRSIG, NSEC, NSEC3).
    TEXT[!MAY]: They may be returned as additional
    TEXT[!MAY]:    information where appropriate."  Recursive resolvers therefore MAY
    TEXT[!MAY]:    cache records from the Additional section for use in populating
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Additional section responses and MAY cache them for general use if
    TEXT[!MAY]:    they are authenticated by DNSSEC.

  SECTION: [EDNS Client Subnet (ECS)](#section-4.4)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: SVCB records may contain IP addresses (in ipv*hint
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SvcParams) or direct users to a subnet-specific TargetName, so
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    recursive resolvers SHOULD include the same ECS option in SVCB
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    queries as in A/AAAA queries.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    According to Section 7.3.1 of [RFC7871], "Any records from [the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Additional section] MUST NOT be tied to a network."  Accordingly,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    when processing a response whose QTYPE is SVCB-compatible, resolvers
    TEXT[!MUST]:    SHOULD treat any records in the Additional section as having SOURCE
    TEXT[!MUST]:    PREFIX-LENGTH set to zero and SCOPE PREFIX-LENGTH as specified in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    ECS option.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Authoritative servers MUST omit such records if they are
    TEXT[!MUST]:    not suitable for use by any stub resolvers that set SOURCE PREFIX-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    LENGTH to zero.

  SECTION: [Performance Optimizations](#section-5)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    For optimal performance (i.e., minimum connection setup time),
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    clients SHOULD implement a client-side DNS cache.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Responses in the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Additional section of a SVCB response SHOULD be placed in cache
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    before performing any follow-up queries.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    To improve performance when using a non-conforming recursive
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    resolver, clients SHOULD issue speculative A and/or AAAA queries in
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    parallel with each SVCB query, based on a predicted value of
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    TargetName (see Section 10.2).
    TEXT[!MAY]:    After a ServiceMode RRset is received, clients MAY try more than one
    TEXT[!MAY]:    option in parallel and MAY prefetch A and AAAA records for multiple
    TEXT[!MAY]:    TargetNames.

  SECTION: [Optimistic Pre-connection and Connection Reuse](#section-5.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If an address response arrives before the corresponding SVCB
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response, the client MAY initiate a connection as if the SVCB query
    TEXT[!MUST]:    returned NODATA but MUST NOT transmit any information that could be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    altered by the SVCB response until it arrives.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Clients implementing this optimization SHOULD wait for 50
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    milliseconds before starting optimistic pre-connection, as per the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    guidance in [HappyEyeballsV2].
    TEXT[!MAY]: If
    TEXT[!MAY]:    a SVCB record is consistent with an active or in-progress connection
    TEXT[!MAY]:    C, the client MAY prefer that record and use C as its connection.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    If the client has an in-progress TCP connection to
    TEXT[!MAY]:    [2001:db8::2]:1234, it MAY proceed with TLS on that connection, even
    TEXT[!MAY]:    though the other record in the RRset has higher priority.

  SECTION: [Generating and Using Incomplete Responses](#section-5.2)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    When following the procedure in Section 4.2, recursive resolvers MAY
    TEXT[!MAY]:    terminate the procedure early and produce a reply that omits some of
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the associated RRsets.
    TEXT[!MUST]: This is REQUIRED when the chain length limit
    TEXT[!MUST]:    is reached (Step 1 in Section 4.2) but might also be appropriate when
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the maximum response size is reached or when responding before fully
    TEXT[!MUST]:    chasing dependencies would improve performance.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: When omitting
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    certain RRsets, recursive resolvers SHOULD prioritize information for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    smaller-SvcPriority records.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    As discussed in Section 3, clients MUST be able to fetch additional
    TEXT[!MUST]:    information that is required to use a SVCB record, if it is not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    included in the initial response.
    TEXT[!MAY]: As a performance optimization, if
    TEXT[!MAY]:    some of the SVCB records in the response can be used without
    TEXT[!MAY]:    requiring additional DNS queries, the client MAY prefer those
    TEXT[!MAY]:    records, regardless of their priorities.

  SECTION: [SVCB-Compatible RR Types](#section-6)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    When following an AliasMode record (Section 2.4.2) of RR type $T, the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    follow-up query to the TargetName MUST also be for type $T.

  SECTION: [Initial SvcParamKeys](#section-7)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Each new protocol mapping document MUST specify which keys are
    TEXT[!MUST]:    applicable and safe to use.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Protocol mappings MAY alter the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    interpretation of SvcParamKeys but MUST NOT alter their presentation
    TEXT[!MUST]:    or wire formats.

  SECTION: ["alpn" and "no-default-alpn"](#section-7.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: ALPN protocol
    TEXT[!MUST]:    identifiers that do not uniquely identify a protocol suite (e.g., an
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Identification Sequence that can be used with both TLS and DTLS) are
    TEXT[!MUST]:    not compatible with this SvcParamKey and MUST NOT be included in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    SVCB ALPN set.

  SECTION: [Representation](#section-7.1.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    For "alpn", the presentation value SHALL be a comma-separated list
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (Appendix A.1) of one or more alpn-ids.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Zone-file implementations
    TEXT[!MAY]:    MAY disallow the "," and "\" characters in ALPN IDs instead of
    TEXT[!MAY]:    implementing the value-list escaping procedure, relying on the opaque
    TEXT[!MAY]:    key format (e.g., key1=\002h2) in the event that these characters are
    TEXT[!MAY]:    needed.
    TEXT[!MUST]: These pairs MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    exactly fill the SvcParamValue; otherwise, the SvcParamValue is
    TEXT[!MUST]:    malformed.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    For "no-default-alpn", the presentation and wire-format values MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    be empty.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Each scheme that uses this SvcParamKey defines a "default set" of
    TEXT[!MAY]:    ALPN IDs that are supported by nearly all clients and servers; this
    TEXT[!MAY]:    set MAY be empty.

  SECTION: [Use](#section-7.1.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    To establish a connection to the endpoint, clients MUST
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Clients MAY implement a fallback procedure, using a less-preferred
    TEXT[!MAY]:    transport if more-preferred transports fail to connect.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Clients SHOULD NOT attempt connection to a service endpoint whose
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SVCB ALPN set does not contain any supported protocols.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    To ensure consistency of behavior, clients MAY reject the entire SVCB
    TEXT[!MAY]:    RRset and fall back to basic connection establishment if all of the
    TEXT[!MAY]:    compatible RRs indicate "no-default-alpn", even if connection could
    TEXT[!MAY]:    have succeeded using a non-default ALPN protocol.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Zone operators SHOULD ensure that at least one RR in each RRset
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    supports the default transports.

  SECTION: ["port"](#section-7.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: If this key is not present,
    TEXT[!MUST]:    clients SHALL use the authority endpoint's port number.
    TEXT[!MUST]: To enable simpler parsing, this
    TEXT[!MUST]:    SvcParamValue MUST NOT contain escape sequences.

  SECTION: ["ipv4hint" and "ipv6hint"](#section-7.3)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    The "ipv4hint" and "ipv6hint" keys convey IP addresses that clients
    TEXT[!MAY]:    MAY use to reach the service.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: If A and AAAA records for TargetName
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    are locally available, the client SHOULD ignore these hints.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Otherwise, clients SHOULD perform A and/or AAAA queries for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    TargetName per Section 3, and clients SHOULD use the IP address in
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    those responses for future connections.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Clients MAY opt to terminate
    TEXT[!MAY]:    any connections using the addresses in hints and instead switch to
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the addresses in response to the TargetName query.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The presentation value SHALL be a comma-separated list (Appendix A.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of one or more IP addresses of the appropriate family in standard
    TEXT[!MUST]:    textual format [RFC5952] [RFC4001].
    TEXT[!MUST]: To enable simpler parsing, this
    TEXT[!MUST]:    SvcParamValue MUST NOT contain escape sequences.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Like an A or
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    AAAA RRset, the list of addresses represents an unordered collection,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    and clients SHOULD pick addresses to use in a random order.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: For best performance, server operators
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD include an "ipv6hint" parameter whenever they include an
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    "ipv4hint" parameter.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    These parameters are intended to minimize additional connection
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    latency when a recursive resolver is not compliant with the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    requirements in Section 4 and SHOULD NOT be included if most clients
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    are using compliant recursive resolvers.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: When TargetName is the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    service name or the owner name (which can be written as "."), server
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    operators SHOULD NOT include these hints, because they are unlikely
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    to convey any performance benefit.

  SECTION: [ServiceMode RR Compatibility and Mandatory Keys](#section-8)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Each SVCB protocol mapping SHOULD specify a set of keys
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    that are "automatically mandatory", i.e., mandatory if they are
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    present in an RR.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The presentation value SHALL be a comma-separated list (Appendix A.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of one or more valid SvcParamKeys, either by their registered name or
    TEXT[!MUST]:    in the unknown-key format (Section 2.1).
    TEXT[!MUST]: Keys MAY appear in any
    TEXT[!MUST]:    order but MUST NOT appear more than once.
    TEXT[!MUST]: For self-consistency
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (Section 2.4.3), listed keys MUST also appear in the SvcParams.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    To enable simpler parsing, this SvcParamValue MUST NOT contain escape
    TEXT[!MUST]:    sequences.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    This SvcParamKey is always automatically mandatory and MUST NOT
    TEXT[!MUST]:    appear in its own value-list.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Other automatically mandatory keys
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD NOT appear in the list either.

  SECTION: [Using Service Bindings with HTTP](#section-9)
    TEXT[!MUST]: Clients MUST NOT perform SVCB queries or accept SVCB
    TEXT[!MUST]:    responses for "https" or "http" schemes.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: (As described in Section 8, clients
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    must either implement these keys or ignore any RR in which they
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    appear.)  Clients that restrict the destination port in "https" URIs
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    (e.g., using the "bad ports" list from [FETCH]) SHOULD apply the same
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    restriction to the "port" SvcParam.

  SECTION: [Query Names for HTTPS RRs](#section-9.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Clients always convert "http" URLs to "https" before performing an
    TEXT[!MUST]:    HTTPS RR query using the process described in Section 9.5, so domain
    TEXT[!MUST]:    owners MUST NOT publish HTTPS RRs with a prefix of "_http".
    TEXT[!MUST]:    For example, clients MUST continue to validate TLS certificate
    TEXT[!MUST]:    hostnames based on the origin.

  SECTION: [Untrusted Channels](#section-9.2.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: (DNSSEC signing and verification, which would provide
    TEXT[!MUST]:    such assurance, are OPTIONAL.)  The DNS resolution process is modeled
    TEXT[!MUST]:    as an untrusted channel that might be controlled by an attacker, so
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Alt-Svc parameters that cannot be safely received in this model MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:    NOT have a corresponding defined SvcParamKey.

  SECTION: [Cache Lifetime](#section-9.2.3)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Shortening the TTL to compensate for incorrect caching is NOT
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    RECOMMENDED, as this practice impairs the performance of correctly
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    functioning caches and does not guarantee faster expiration from
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    incorrect caches.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Instead, server operators SHOULD maintain
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    compatibility with expired records until they observe that nearly all
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    connections have migrated to the new configuration.

  SECTION: [Interaction with Alt-Svc](#section-9.3)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Clients that implement support for both Alt-Svc and HTTPS records and
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    are making a connection based on a cached Alt-Svc response SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    retrieve any HTTPS records for the Alt-Svc alt-authority and ensure
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    that their connection attempts are consistent with both the Alt-Svc
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    parameters and any received HTTPS SvcParams.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Alt-authorities SHOULD carry the same SvcParams as the origin unless
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    a deviation is specifically known to be safe.
    TEXT[!MAY]: As noted in
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Section 2.4 of [AltSvc], clients MAY disallow any Alt-Svc connection
    TEXT[!MAY]:    according to their own criteria, e.g., disallowing Alt-Svc
    TEXT[!MAY]:    connections that lack support for privacy features that are available
    TEXT[!MAY]:    on the authority endpoint.

  SECTION: [Requiring Server Name Indication](#section-9.4)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Clients MUST NOT use an HTTPS RR response unless the client supports
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the TLS Server Name Indication (SNI) extension and indicates the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    origin name in the TLS ClientHello (which might be encrypted via a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    future specification such as [ECH]).

  SECTION: [HTTP Strict Transport Security (HSTS)](#section-9.5)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Prior to making an
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    "http" scheme request, the client SHOULD perform a lookup to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    determine if any HTTPS RRs exist for that origin.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: To do so, the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    client SHOULD construct a corresponding "https" URL as follows:
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If an HTTPS RR query for this "https" URL returns any AliasMode HTTPS
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    RRs or any compatible ServiceMode HTTPS RRs (see Section 8), the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    client SHOULD behave as if it has received an HTTP 307 (Temporary
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Redirect) status code with this "https" URL in the "Location" field.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (Receipt of an incompatible ServiceMode RR does not trigger the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    redirect behavior.)  Because HTTPS RRs are received over an often-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    insecure channel (DNS), clients MUST NOT place any more trust in this
    TEXT[!MUST]:    signal than if they had received a 307 (Temporary Redirect) response
    TEXT[!MUST]:    over cleartext HTTP.
    TEXT[!MAY]: When making an "https"
    TEXT[!MAY]:    scheme request to an origin with an HTTPS RR, either directly or via
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the above redirect, such a client MAY remove the user recourse
    TEXT[!MAY]:    option.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Origins that publish HTTPS RRs therefore MUST NOT rely on
    TEXT[!MUST]:    user recourse for access.

  SECTION: [Use of HTTPS RRs in Other Protocols](#section-9.6)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: For
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    example, clients that support HTTPS RRs and implement [WebSocket]
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    using the altered opening handshake from [FETCH-WEBSOCKETS] SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    use HTTPS RRs for the requestURL.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    When HTTP is used in a context where URLs or redirects are not
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    applicable (e.g., connections to an HTTP proxy), clients that find a
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    corresponding HTTPS RR SHOULD implement security upgrade behavior
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    equivalent to that specified in Section 9.5.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Such protocols MAY define their own SVCB mappings, which MAY be
    TEXT[!MAY]:    defined to take precedence over HTTPS RRs.

  SECTION: [Structuring Zones for Flexibility](#section-10.1)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    When using the generic SVCB RR type with aliasing, zone owners SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    choose alias target names that indicate the scheme in use (e.g.,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    "foosvc.example.net" for "foo" schemes).

  SECTION: [Structuring Zones for Performance](#section-10.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    To avoid a delay for clients using a non-conforming recursive
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    resolver, domain owners SHOULD minimize the use of AliasMode records
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    and SHOULD choose TargetName according to a predictable convention
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    that is known to the client, so that clients can issue A and/or AAAA
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    queries for TargetName in advance (see Section 5).
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Domain owners SHOULD avoid using a TargetName that is below a DNAME,
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    as this is likely unnecessary and makes responses slower and larger.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Also, zone structures that require following more than eight aliases
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    (counting both AliasMode and CNAME records) are NOT RECOMMENDED.

  SECTION: [Interaction with Other Standards](#section-11)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Server operators implementing this standard SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    also implement TLS 1.3 [RFC8446] and Online Certificate Status
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Protocol (OCSP) Stapling (i.e., Certificate Status Request in
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Section 8 of [RFC6066]), both of which confer substantial performance
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    and privacy benefits when used in combination with SVCB records.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Any specification for the use of SVCB with a protocol MUST have an
    TEXT[!MUST]:    entry for its scheme under the SVCB RR type in the IANA DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    "Underscored and Globally Scoped DNS Node Names" registry [Attrleaf].
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The scheme MUST have an entry in the "Uniform Resource Identifier
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (URI) Schemes" registry [RFC7595] and MUST have a defined
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specification for use with SVCB.

  SECTION: [Security Considerations](#section-12)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    SVCB/HTTPS RRs permit distribution over untrusted channels, and
    TEXT[!MUST]:    clients are REQUIRED to verify that the alternative endpoint is
    TEXT[!MUST]:    authoritative for the service (similar to Section 2.1 of [AltSvc]).
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Therefore, DNSSEC signing and validation are OPTIONAL for publishing
    TEXT[!MAY]:    and using SVCB and HTTPS RRs.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Clients MUST ensure that their DNS cache is partitioned for each
    TEXT[!MUST]:    local network, or flushed on network changes, to prevent a local
    TEXT[!MUST]:    adversary in one network from implanting a forged DNS record that
    TEXT[!MUST]:    allows them to track users or hinder their connections after they
    TEXT[!MUST]:    leave that network.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Clients that might be
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    subject to such attacks SHOULD ignore AliasMode "." records.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: (The same concerns apply to SRV records, HTTP Alt-
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Svc, and HTTP redirects.)  As a mitigation, SVCB mapping documents
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    SHOULD indicate any port number restrictions that are appropriate for
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    the supported transports.

  SECTION: [Procedure](#section-14.3.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A registration MUST include the following fields:
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The characters in the registered Name field entry MUST be lowercase
    TEXT[!MUST]:    alphanumeric or "-" (Section 2.1).
    TEXT[!MUST]: The name MUST NOT start with
    TEXT[!MUST]:    "key" or "invalid".
    TEXT[!MUST]: The designated expert MUST ensure that the reference
    TEXT[!MUST]:    is stable and publicly available and that it specifies how to convert
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the SvcParamValue's presentation format to wire format.
    TEXT[!MAY]: The
    TEXT[!MAY]:    reference MAY be any individual's Internet-Draft or a document from
    TEXT[!MAY]:    any other source with similar assurances of stability and
    TEXT[!MAY]:    availability.
    TEXT[!MAY]: An entry MAY specify a reference of the form "Same as
    TEXT[!MAY]:    (other key name)" if it uses the same presentation and wire formats
    TEXT[!MAY]:    as an existing key.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9471
  SECTION: [Introduction](#section-1)
    TEXT[!MUST]: If message size constraints prevent
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the inclusion of all glue records for in-domain name servers over the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    chosen transport, the server MUST set the TC (Truncated) flag to
    TEXT[!MUST]:    inform the client that the response is incomplete and that the client
    TEXT[!MUST]:    SHOULD use another transport to retrieve the full response.

  SECTION: [Glue for In-Domain Name Servers](#section-3.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    This document clarifies that when a name server generates a referral
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response, it MUST include all available glue records for in-domain
    TEXT[!MUST]:    name servers in the additional section or MUST set TC=1 if
    TEXT[!MUST]:    constrained by message size.

  SECTION: [Glue for Sibling Domain Name Servers](#section-3.2)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    This document clarifies that when a name server generates a referral
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    response, it SHOULD include all available glue records in the
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    additional section.
    TEXT[!MAY]: If, after adding glue for all in-domain name
    TEXT[!MAY]:    servers, the glue for all sibling domain name servers does not fit
    TEXT[!MAY]:    due to message size constraints, the name server MAY set TC=1 but is
    TEXT[!MAY]:    not obligated to do so.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9520
  SECTION: [Retries and Timeouts](#section-3.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A resolver MUST NOT retry a given query to a server address over a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    given DNS transport more than twice (i.e., three queries in total)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    before considering the server address unresponsive over that DNS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    transport for that query.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    A resolver MAY retry a given query over a different DNS transport to
    TEXT[!MAY]:    the same server if it has reason to believe the DNS transport is
    TEXT[!MAY]:    available for that server and is compatible with the resolver's
    TEXT[!MAY]:    security policies.

  SECTION: [Caching](#section-3.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Resolvers MUST implement a cache for resolution failures.
    TEXT[!MUST]: When an incoming query matches a cached
    TEXT[!MUST]:    resolution failure, the resolver MUST NOT send any corresponding
    TEXT[!MUST]:    outgoing queries until after the cache entries expire.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Resolvers MUST cache resolution failures for at least 1 second.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Resolvers MAY cache different types of resolution failures for
    TEXT[!MAY]:    different (i.e., longer) amounts of time.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Consistent with [RFC2308],
    TEXT[!MUST]:    resolution failures MUST NOT be cached for longer than 5 minutes.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    The minimum cache duration SHOULD be configurable by the operator.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Resolvers SHOULD employ an exponential or linear backoff algorithm to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    increase the cache duration for persistent resolution failures.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    Notwithstanding the above, resolvers SHOULD implement measures to
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    mitigate resource exhaustion attacks on the failed resolution cache.

  SECTION: [Requerying Delegation Information](#section-3.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |  Upon encountering a zone whose name servers are all non-
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |  responsive, a resolver MUST cache the resolution failure.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |  Furthermore, the resolver MUST limit queries to the non-responsive
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |  zone's parent zone (and to other ancestor zones) just as it would
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |  limit subsequent queries to the non-responsive zone.

  SECTION: [DNSSEC Validation Failures](#section-3.4)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    |  To prevent such unnecessary DNS traffic, security-aware resolvers
    TEXT[!MAY]:    |  MAY cache data with invalid signatures, with some restrictions.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |  To prevent such unnecessary DNS traffic, security-aware resolvers
    TEXT[!MUST]:    |  MUST cache DNSSEC validation failures, with some restrictions.

  SECTION: [Security Considerations](#section-5)
    TEXT[!SHOULD]: Resolvers SHOULD
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    implement measures to protect themselves and bound the amount of
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    memory devoted to caching resolution failures.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9558
  SECTION: [DNSKEY Resource Records](#section-2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The wire representation of a
    TEXT[!MUST]:    public key MUST contain 64 octets, where the first 32 octets contain
    TEXT[!MUST]:    the little-endian representation of x and the second 32 octets
    TEXT[!MUST]:    contain the little-endian representation of y.

  SECTION: [RRSIG RR Example](#section-3.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    This value for k MUST NOT be used when computing GOST R 34.10-2012
    TEXT[!MUST]:    signatures.

  SECTION: [Key Sizes](#section-5.1)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The key size of GOST R 34.10-2012 public keys conforming to this
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specification MUST be 512 bits according to RFC 7091 [RFC7091].

  SECTION: [Signature Sizes](#section-5.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The size of a GOST R 34.10-2012 signature conforming to this
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specification MUST be 512 bits according to RFC 7091 [RFC7091].

  SECTION: [Digest Sizes](#section-5.3)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The size of a GOST R 34.11-2012 digest conforming to this
    TEXT[!MUST]:    specification MUST be 256 bits according to RFC 6986 [RFC6986].

  SECTION: [Implementation Considerations](#section-6)
    TEXT[!MAY]:    The support of this cryptographic suite in DNSSEC-aware systems is
    TEXT[!MAY]:    OPTIONAL.
    TEXT[!MUST]: According to RFC 6840 [RFC6840], Section 5.2, systems that
    TEXT[!MUST]:    do not support these algorithms MUST ignore the RRSIG, DNSKEY, and DS
    TEXT[!MUST]:    resource records associated with the GOST R 34.10-2012 digital
    TEXT[!MUST]:    signature algorithm.

  SECTION: [IANA Considerations](#section-7)
    TEXT[!MAY]:            +=======+===================+==========+===========+
    TEXT[!MAY]:            | Value | Description       | Status   | Reference |
    TEXT[!MAY]:            +=======+===================+==========+===========+
    TEXT[!MAY]:            | 5     | GOST R 34.11-2012 | OPTIONAL | RFC 9558  |
    TEXT[!MAY]:            +-------+-------------------+----------+-----------+

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9563
  SECTION: [RRSIG Resource Records](#section-4.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: (Conversion of the integers
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to bit strings is described in Section 4.2.1 of [GMT-0003.1].)  Each
    TEXT[!MUST]:    integer MUST be encoded as 32 octets.
    TEXT[!MAY]:    Conformant implementations that create records to be put into the DNS
    TEXT[!MAY]:    MAY implement signing and verification for the SM2 digital signature
    TEXT[!MAY]:    algorithm.
    TEXT[!MAY]: Conformant DNSSEC verifiers MAY implement verification
    TEXT[!MAY]:    for the above algorithm.

  SECTION: [Support for NSEC3 Denial of Existence](#section-5)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    A DNSSEC validator that implements the signing algorithms defined in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    this document MUST be able to validate negative answers in the form
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of both NSEC and NSEC3 with hash algorithm SHA-1, as defined in
    TEXT[!MUST]:    [RFC5155].
    TEXT[!MAY]: An authoritative server that does not implement NSEC3 MAY
    TEXT[!MAY]:    still serve zones that use the signing algorithms defined in this
    TEXT[!MAY]:    document with NSEC denial of existence.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    If using NSEC3, the iterations MUST be 0 and salt MUST be an empty
    TEXT[!MUST]:    string as recommended in Section 3.1 of [RFC9276].

  SECTION: [IANA Considerations](#section-7)
    TEXT[!MAY]:             +=======+=============+==========+===============+
    TEXT[!MAY]:             | Value | Digest Type | Status   | Reference     |
    TEXT[!MAY]:             +=======+=============+==========+===============+
    TEXT[!MAY]:             | 6     | SM3         | OPTIONAL | This document |
    TEXT[!MAY]:             +-------+-------------+----------+---------------+

  SECTION: [Security Considerations](#section-8)
    TEXT[!MUST]: Care MUST be taken in this situation to permit appropriate
    TEXT[!MUST]:    rollovers, taking into account record caching.

SPECIFICATION: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9606
  SECTION: [Retrieving Resolver Information](#section-3)
    TEXT[!MUST]: If the resolver understands the RESINFO RR type, the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    RRset MUST have exactly one record.
    TEXT[!MUST]: Invalid records MUST be silently
    TEXT[!MUST]:    ignored by DNS clients.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    The DNS client MUST set the Recursion Desired (RD) bit of the query
    TEXT[!MUST]:    to 0.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The DNS client MUST discard the response if the AA flag in the
    TEXT[!MUST]:    response is set to 0, indicating that the DNS resolver is not
    TEXT[!MUST]:    authoritative for the response.
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    If a group of resolvers is sharing the same ADN and/or anycast
    TEXT[!SHOULD]:    address, then these instances SHOULD expose a consistent RESINFO.

  SECTION: [Format of the Resolver Information](#section-4)
    TEXT[!MUST]: If a DNS client sees unknown
    TEXT[!MUST]:    keys in a RESINFO RR type, it MUST silently ignore them.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The same
    TEXT[!MUST]:    rules for the keys, as defined in Section 6.4 of [RFC6763], MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:    followed for RESINFO.
    TEXT[!MUST]:    Resolver information keys MUST either be defined in the IANA registry
    TEXT[!MUST]:    (Section 8.2) or begin with the substring "temp-" for names defined
    TEXT[!MUST]:    for local use only.

  SECTION: [Resolver Information Keys/Values](#section-5)
    TEXT[!MUST]: Range values MUST be
    TEXT[!MUST]:       identified by "-".
    TEXT[!MUST]: When multiple non-contiguous values are
    TEXT[!MUST]:       present, these values MUST be comma-separated.
    TEXT[!MUST]:       The resolver information server MUST support only the content-type
    TEXT[!MUST]:       "text/html" for the resolver information.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The DNS client MUST
    TEXT[!MUST]:       reject the URL as invalid if the scheme is not "https".
    TEXT[!MUST]: Invalid
    TEXT[!MUST]:       URLs MUST be ignored.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The URL MUST be treated only as diagnostic
    TEXT[!MUST]:       information for IT staff.

  SECTION: [Security Considerations](#section-7)
    TEXT[!MUST]:    DNS clients communicating with discovered DNS resolvers MUST use one
    TEXT[!MUST]:    of the following measures to prevent DNS response forgery attacks:

  SECTION: [DNS Resolver Information Keys Registration](#section-8.2)
    TEXT[!MUST]: The name MUST conform to the definition in
    TEXT[!MUST]:       Section 4 of this document.
    TEXT[!MUST]: The IANA registry MUST NOT register
    TEXT[!MUST]:       names that begin with "temp-" so that these names can be used
